<Author>MilwaukeeCol
<Content>The Waikiki Marriott is Okay for an Airline Overnight Our family was bumped from a US Airways flight and they put us up at the Marriott Waikiki for the night (and a majority of the next day). The Marriott was not a bad place to stay. The check-in (at 1 in the morning) was quick and efficient. The airline had booked us for 2 nights (since the flight out was at midnight the next day). The food prices are pretty outrageous ($19.95 for breakfast buffet and $26.95 for dinner buffet), but the food is really very good. The airline gave us coupons for breakfast, lunch and dinner ($5, $5 and $10, respectively) which helped (a little) to defray the costs, but not much. The people at the hotel seemed nice enough. We did not interact with them a lot, but the ones we spoke with were nice. The hotel is nicely situated on Waikiki beach and the room we got was on the 30th floor with a great view of Diamondhead and the end of Waikiki Beach. It also had two pools and a jacuzzi which were very nice. All in all, we had an okay time at the Marriott Waikiki. It was not outstanding in any respect, but it was adequate to get us ready for our flight out the next night.  
<Date>Jan 7, 2009

<Author>davidnhollyminor
<Content>Taking the Family on a Business Trip Nice Hotel in the heart of Waikiki. The Beach by the hotel is protected by a man-made surf break that makes it great for small children. Our 2 1/2 year old son loved playing in the water and it barely was over his head in the deep areas. It was a great place to have him in the water and not be scared.The area around the hotel is full of tourist trap shops and some shady characters, but it is safe. The food at the hotel is good, but nothing spectacular.I would definitely recommend this hotel for other people, but you should not expect too much. Just enjoy it for what it is.

<Author>yumikat2006
<Content>Great hotel! I don't understand all the negative reviews here. Although it is a little on the far end of the hustle and bustle of Kalakaua Avenue and most importantly Waikiki, my family and I had a very pleasurable stay here, made possible by American Express. Our room was very clean and we had a great full view of Diamond Head and a partial ocean view. I really recommend the restaurant Arancino di Mare for breakfast, lunch, and dinner, but for dinner, I would recommend making reservations to avoid waiting in line for 15-20 minutes. The service here was great; we were staying at this hotel during the power outage, but the staff told us to stay calm and told us the cause, and told us there was a flashlight in case we needed one. All in all, I had a wonderful stay here at the Waikiki Beach Marriott, and I hope to stay here again!

<Author>BrisbaneGlad
<Content>Never be tempted to stay here! The worst hotel I've stayed in for a long time, and an unbelievable price rip-off. We will be taking up their dishonest charging practices with our credit card provider!The room was not cleaned the first day and on two days of four it was cleaned in the late afternoon while we were trying to relax in the room. Cleaning staff were friendly and polite. The rest of the staff were arrogant and unhelfpul, and at times downright rude. Getting attention for anything from checkin/checkout to concierge services required standing in long queues. Bell-boy services were non-existent. Information on facilities and services was very poor. Advertising messages left on our room phone drove us insane and rendered the voicemail service completely useless. Excessive noise and poor air conditioning that caused us to boil, then freeze, meant we got no sleep.Lifts didn't work properly. (We almost missed an expensive tour because we had to wait for 20 minutes for an elevator!). Food costs were outrageous - $17.50 USD for a small bowl of oatmeal! And despite a rate of over $300 per night, an internet connection was an expensive extra! Even the in-room coffee was limited to enough to make 2 cups per day if you didn't need sugar, and only 1cup per day per room (regardless of number of occupants) with sugar. The buffet breakfast was quite good, but at $19.95 USD each, you would expect it to be! As for lunch and dinner, the restaurants around the corner offered far better at a quarter the price, with courteous service thrown in at no extra cost! And don't even think of booking activities through the Marriott! Tour service operators one block away offered identical tours and activities for an average of 60% of the price and were much nicer to deal with!My daughter arranged our bookings at $159 USD per night, but when we checked in we were told no bookings existed at that rate and it was actually $275 per night, but they could offer a 4th night free special. (My daughter actually paid the apparently non-existent $159 rate for an identical room!) On checkout, the charge levied was over $300 per night, and no fourth night free. When I complained, we were told they had a 'pre-auth' on our credit card and had placed the charge and did not need a signature or approval of any charges. (That suggests they think they can defraud whenever they please! I'll be taking that up with my card provider!)Overall, a miserable experience that spoiled an otherwise enjoyable holiday.

<Author>Worltravelah
<Content>Flophouse ala Marriott First let me say that the staff in the restaurant waiting tables and making my food were great. If you can find a way to wrangle breakfast: do so. It goes to 11 AM so you can make it brunch and skip lunch. The nice ladies pouring my coffee saw I was by myself and chatted me up just enough. I liked that, and they are credit to the staff. Tips were included in my breakfast voucher but I still left a couple a bucks most days. They were so nice I guiltted myself into it.Second the lady cleaning my room (16th floor back tower) was so nice! She was always cheery and chatting my up a bit in the halls. These are the people who should be running the place. Management got bonus money: spend it there.The pool areas were nice. I liked relaxing there, and the older pool guy gave me a friendly welcome and chat one day. Good towel service. (However, younger guy noticeably snobby and above it all. Hey you are a pool boy here's a clue: put a smile on.) Even the noisy kids didn't bug me. It was kinda fun hearing Christmas Carols on the ukulele with Hawaiian words on the loudspeakers. Fun and relaxing good choice and atmosphere.Now for the bad news.This must be an old building with poor construction standards, and in my opinion, Marriott needs to sell this building and look for something else down here in Waikiki. You can noise from above, and both sides. This includes but is not limited to banging doors and furniture sliding. The automatic door closers are adjusted to a slam level. No kidding the plastic fake wood headboard in my room banged my head, with a gut wrenching BANG when the door next door closed. But all the noisy doors on the hall were clearly audible. And there must have been an elephant in the room above me dragging furniture around on the balcony. Now I had the bonus (add sarcasm) of being in the room next to the elevators, providing me with a 24 by 7 inescapable on and off whirring vibration every time the elevator moved. Imagine that morning noon and night for a 7 day stay. Now combine that with an unsympathetic staff who won't change your room. Which brings me to my next point.The front desk staff is surly and incompetent, although the woman checking me in did smile and try to accommodate me. To Wendel one of the managers: nice try by moving me 36 hours before the end of a one week stay, but it was just not worth it. And a special shout out to Kaori who was not only rude, but treated a Marriott Preferred member and a millionaire, MBA and double Masters like a complete idiot and a bum. Honestly, if someone from corporate saw a video of how she treated me, she would be fired without question. Someone in a management position should simply pose as a customer and get in line with her.Watch your bill! I chained 3 reservations together. They tried to get me to pay upgrade fees, upgrading two of the lower rates to the higher grade room. Due to all the problems they upgraded my ocean view room to one where I could actually see the ocean! How big of them! Then without telling me they tried to sneak on the 20 dollar a night charge they told me I did not have to pay. If I had not noted it I would have paid and I am sure many do. Then they treated me like they were doing me some big [--] favor to take it off.Let's talk parking. When I pay 27 dollars a night for an entire weel to park the door should open when I put my key in. And if it doesn't, someone should call to bring me new keys when I get back. Twice I had to wait in line to solve the problem of my key not working. If the front desk had not worn me down I would have fought with them to have one night removed from my bill. At that price I should not have to wait at the desk for surly treatment twice.That's enough. Again. My the pool, my housekeeper, the waitresses, and the gentleman cooking me a perfect western omelet in the morning were the only saving graces of this one week stay. The quality of the building resulting in almost unbearable noise is something in my opinion which is insurmountable. If you are expecting Marriott quality with this stay you are going to be sorely disappointed.

<Author>u761154
<Content>Don't expect any smiles. Was due to stay here for 7 nights, but ended up moving after 3. The hotel is in a very convenient location right across the road from Waikiki beach. It is an ideal location if you want to be near the beach, the restaurants, bars and shops. There are ABC stores everywhere, plenty of transport options, tours and activities. The main reason we moved to the JW at Ko Olina was that it was just too busy, don't expect to find any quiet spots to chill, as the tourists and traffic is constant, and you'll be stopped by people trying to sell you tours/activities/restaurants/etc every 50m as you walk along the main beach road.There are two large towers, try to request the one nearer to the beach, as you will get better views. Unfortunately we were placed in the other one, in a partial ocean view room. Well the only way you could see the view from the tiny balcony was to learn over the edge of the railings and look down the street between the buildings, not my ideal of even a 'partial' ocean view. The room was very dated, and the bathroom was the strangest I have seen. The bathroom was small, containing the shower/bath and the toilet, the basin was outside in the room. The door to the bathroom was a flimsy sliding door, not what the standard that you would expect from a Marriott hotel at all. As others have commented the walls are thin, we could hear the noise from neighbouring rooms, and also from people outside in the hallway as we were placed right next to the lifts. On the positive side the room was clean, a very comfortable bed and had an empty refrigerator for you to stock up on stuff from the ABC stores.We never ate at the hotel as there are plenty of cheaper options right outside the hotel, we generally went to the coffee shop located in the stores within the hotel complex. The worst aspect of the hotel from our point of view was the staff. They had to be the most miserable staff I have ever encountered, a surly bunch that never managed a single smile. It felt like they just had so many people to deal with everyday that they were disillusioned, there was no attempt at providing a personal touch. Like the previous reviewer, we also found the concierge service very poor.This hotel would be a good choice if you want convenience and to be near all the action, and we found it to be a reasonable price when compared to the other similar hotels. Not for you if you want some peace and quiet, with some relaxation by the pool or beach.  
<Date>Dec 1, 2008

<Content>Average Hotel Pros: +Decent rooms, comfortable beds+Good location (across the street from the beach)Cons:-Horrible concierge service.At 1st night we asked for restaurant recommendations and the only suggestion she had was the sushi bar at the hotel (we didn't want sushi). Keep in mind that you have to do all the research by yourself. In case if you're looking for a 4* service, stay somewhere else, this is not a luxurious hotel. This hotel has 3* rooms but 1* service.

<Author>weehawks
<Content>Great location, excellent service! We went there for the beginning of our honeymoon and had a fantastic time. Check in was swift and they were able to accommodate our early check in request. Since we are Platinum members and on our honeymoon, they upgraded us to a Ocean View, double balcony on the 32nd floor. The room was a decent size with an extra seating area.Pros:The location is excellent. You can go to the beach right across the street or take one of the many buses that go through the island.The concierge was very helpful in renting a car for the day and they also have a Hertz on site. You definitely do not need a car since there is public transportation, but on other islands, you do. We rented a car for a day to go to Hanauma Bay (absolutely gorgeous!), but a lot of the coral looked dead so there wasn鈥檛 a swarm of fish as I expected. Got to swim with a turtle though and there are octopus in the water.The hotel is huge - about the size of a NY city block. The pools are outdoors and heated and it was nice swimming in the evening when it was empty. They have mini marts (called ABC stores) everyone and there is a rather big on in the hotel.Service was excellent. Truly everyone was hospitable and warm.Lots of eateries within walking distance and there is a fridge in the room if you don't want to go out for every meal. The hotel faces the beach and is along a lot of high end shops, as well as local outdoor shops. All the outdoor vendors pretty much sell the same thing (bathing suits, souvenirs, leis, sarongs鈥tc) and if you are making a multi-island stop, buy it here as it is the cheaper than in Maui or the Big Island. I regretted not buying bathing suits while I was there.Weather was perfect every day!!I had no noise problems like someone else mentioned in their post. Maybe because I was on a higher floor? Cons:Being on a high floor meant sometimes waiting for the elevator. There was a conference during two of the days we were there so sometimes there was a wait and the elevator was crowded. A very, very small inconvenience.There is a daily resort fee.All in all, great experience, the location was fantastic and we were very happy with our experience.

<Author>lovebossa
<Content>Great price, Great service! My mother and I stayed at this hotel for 6 days. We love Hawai'i, and we stayed at different hotels in Oahu (Halekulani, Hilton, Hyatt, Moana Surf Rider, Sheraton) but Marriott Waikiki is still our favorite. We stayed at Ocean Front room (corner room facing the ocean at two sides) at Kealohiliani Tower (the one closer to beach). The room was renovated recently and did not see any old piece of furniture as described in some of the previous reviews. The room was appointed with red and green and it was more spacious than other hotels around the same (or even a bit higher) level. You can check the view of the renovated room on Marriott Waikiki website. One thing I loved most about the room was the view! It had one window on one side and also balcony on the other side. It was nice to see sunrise from the bed, and go to balcony to see early-morning rainbow above Royal Hawaiian.Bathroom was also good! It was very luminous which complimented my skin and had two big sinks. Also there was a separate shower room. And it was always filled with soooo many towels which made us go to the hotel pool and beach all the time. Yes, pool was nice, too. It is simple but it was nicely appointed with comfortable lounge chairs. You can also borrow their towels at pool side, too. We enjoyed reasonably priced breakfast at Italian restaurant. I have to admit that they didn't have the luxury that Halekulani has but their food was great and the staffs were very helpful. It seemed that they are trained to treat each customer individually - they remember you and such small talk made me feel special. I saw some people complaining about the distance to the center of Downtown but it's not far at all! Just enjoy walking two more blocks in sunshine. Really, if you have a budget to spend for the same/higher-ranked hotel with smaller rooms, I recommend staying at this room at Marriott.

<Author>hawkeyelady
<Content>Wonderful Hotel For our first time in Hawaii this hotel was absolutely fabulous! Beautiful view if you have an ocean view room. The pool was warm and very relaxing. Note for first-timers in Hawaii - if you prefer to be where the action is - stay in Waikiki, if you want total relaxation with not much else to do, stay at the North Shore. <Author>TravelTeacher215
<Content>Good enough We started our honeymoon here before our cruise. FYI, if you are doing the cruise on either end of the stay, book the hotel through NCL and they will take your bags for you. Otherwise, the NCL office in the lobby will not give a care about you.The hotel was confusing, not signs as to where to go for check in from the shuttle and no one waiting to take our bags. The check in was great, the woman was very nice, our room was in the front tower close to the beach. The view was amazing, in fact, I preferred the balcony view of the beach to the actual beach.They have obviously tried to update the hotel, there are big screen TV's in the rooms and the bathrooms have newer sinks. It is odd what they chose to neglect, like old vents that still have rust. The room was comfortable and the beds were nice.The breakfast buffet was included, it was a nice breakfast, but not worth the $22 price tag if not included.The hotel is across the street from the beach. You are at the end of Waikiki and close to the zoo and Diamond Head. They beach was dirty and kind of sketchy. People actually live in tents n the beach or just have all of their things in a cart or something there. I was not haggled for money, but it just did not feel safe.You will have to walk a bit for a meal, the POSH area is about 6 blocks up the road. Do not walk towards Diamond Head to eat, walk the other way. They have the normal chain stuff. There are many sushi places along the main drag, too. Don't waste your time eating in the hotel, there are many choices if you do not mind the walk.The pool is okay, nothing special, but will suffice. My suggestion is rent a car and go to a better beach than Waikiki.They have a hospitality room. FYI - you share it, so it is weird to go in alone because only the shower area locks and you have to leave all of your stuff in the common area. They do not do a great job saying which sex goes where, so it is quite possible that someone will walk in on you as ANY hotel key opens the door.

<Content>Great place to spend a week in the sun My husband and I just spent 8 days at the Marriot in Waikiki for some rest and relaxation.Check in was fine the lady who helped us was very friendly and explained where everything was.Our room was on the 31st floor which was great. <Author>Anon_Texas
<Content>I would not stay here again. Stayed here 4 days in August 2008 in an ocean front room on the 17th floor. The location was right across the street from Waikiki beach and I even fed the fish right there on the beach. Be sure to bring breadcrumbs to feed the fish. Actually, most of the major hotels on Waikiki are on the same stretch of beach. Location is really not an issue on Waikiki beach itself. Upon arriving by chartered bus/group bus, as other reviewers have noted, you will be dropped off in the back of the hotel. There were no hotel personnel to help with luggage when we arrived. We did not have too much luggage and this was not an issue for us.The Waikiki Marriott itself was average at best. Our room had a good view but the sink was cracked and the bathroom was old. There were spots on the carpet and a visible patch on the wall. I did mention the obvious issues to a manager the morning after arrival but did not request a room change since we were rarely in the room and had unpacked. Naturally, staying ocean front is always expensive and we did pay a premium for the view. The view itself was very good but the room left a lot to be desired. Everything in the room pointed to cost savings. There were no robes, crusty coffee maker, sparse towels and few hangers created the impression that anything not bolted down was cut out to save expenses. One would expect more in a room that cost US$300 - US$350 per night. Apart from the room, the personnel were excellent and the on-site sushi restaurant was quite good. However, I would not stay at the Waikiki Marriott again in lieu of the vast number of other hotels within a block of each other, for the price. Regardless, based on every beach-based hotel I鈥檝e stayed in over the last 20 years (Miami, Clearwater, Sydney, Maui, Cancun), the Waikiki Marriott had some of the worst rooms for the price. Since I have not stayed at other hotels in the area, I cannot recommend an alternative. There is a valid reason though as to why this hotel is not in the top 10 hotels for Waikiki on TripAdvisor. Wish I had listened to the other reviews and stayed elsewhere.

<Author>Rhine-and-Roses
<Content>Nice Hotel, Noisy Area I spent a week at the Marriott Waikiki on a business trip. My room was clean, spacious, and attractive. I had a standard room, with a view that was disappointing at first glance. However once out on the balcony, I had a view of both the ocean and Diamond Head, although Diamond Head was a partial view through the two buildings across the street.I liked the tropical ambiance the lined and tied back draperies added.My bathroom was immaculate, with toiletries replenished daily. Housekeeping was excellent- I think her name was Carmelita. I would hire her to take care of my home! Front desk was efficient and friendly. I never had to wait in line. The hotel did cash a few checks for me- not sure if they do it for all guests or because I am a Rewards member.The pools were both nice. The P Tower pool was never crowded.The meeting rooms were adequate, but cold.We had catered meals and I thought they were excellent- lots and lots of fresh fruit and vegetables, with everything cooked well- not overcooked as you often find in catered hotel food. There were several choices for each meal, with fish being available for almost every meal. We also used the coffee bar available in the lounge- the coffee was way better than Starbuck's, in my opinion. The Japanese restaurant (on premises) with sushi was excellent.I do have to say I hated all the noise in Waikiki. I was on the 6th floor and asked for a higher floor since I couldn't really use my balcony for the noise, and I was having trouble sleeping with car alarms, etc all night long. They offered me a room on the 31st floor with a fabulous view on the quiet side of the hotel (facing the church) but when I went on the balcony, the street noise was still present, still loud, although not quite as loud. I realize the noise is out of the control of the hotel, but it was disappointing not to be able to use my balcony without ear plugs. All in all, I though this was a great hotel- so much in it, so close to Waikiki Beach and all the activities. However, I would probably not choose to go back because of the noise level. After my meeting I moved to the Hilton Hawaiian Village. See my review.

Waikiki is full of Japanese tourists and the restaraunt put the Japanese breakfast favorites on their own table, with labels in Japanese. Our room was very nice with two balconies. However, we had a large screen TV - it was High Def - but fuzzy channels. Why bother? Honolulu itself was a huge let down. First - Waikiki beach is beautiful and right across the street, but it is covered with homeless people. We saw a homeless man peeing right in the middle of the major thoroughfare. Some were quiet and minded their own business and others made everyone very uncomfortable. These people are clearly mentally ill and need help and Honolulu does nothing. Traffic is terrible there. You can see the highway, but they hide the on-ramps. Also - they dont really believe in road signs either, because we would miss exits since they gave no indication that these exits were upcoming. The best meals were found at the Ala Mauna mall. Went to Hawaii and had to go to the mall to get a decently priced meal!Pearl Harbor was good, but you are better off watching something about the Arizona on the History Channel. We went to the Missouri, which was awesome and you can see the Arizona easily from the decks of the Mo. However, at noon, we were told the Arizona trips were full for the day. Seems you have to get your free tickets very early in the morning. Get out of Honolulu and go to the North Shore. Amazing scenery  
<Date>Jul 27, 2008

<Content>A Good Value for the Money I've stayed in this hotel three times. Once, I was in the tower farther away from the beach, and twice I was in the tower closer to the beach. I got a partial ocean view room when I was in the tower closer to the beach. I enjoyed the views a lot, particularly early in the morning and late at night. The rooms are not luxurious, but they are very nice---perfectly comfortable and pleasant. <Author>mrselett
<Content>Enjoyed Our Stay As part of a special annivesary, we booked the Waikiki Marriott with rewards points. We booked a standard city view with a queen sized bed and upon arrival were upgraded to a partial oceanview king, which was quite large. It has a desk area, chair, closet, refrigerator, a large balcony with two chairs and a chaise. The Marriott appears to be recently remodeled but the furniture is not modern, it's more of a throwback tribute to old Hawaii. We still enjoyed it though.The customer service was great. Again, we had the upgrade. I'm not sure if it's because of my marriott rewards status or the annivesary or both. They also gave us free drink tickets as a congratulations. The pools are rather small and not very impressive, but you've got the beach right across the street. We had a wonderful dinner at the steakhouse there at the hotel. We enjoyed a very generous buffet with everything from crab legs to lamb at another restaurant at the hotel. And we dined poolside. Don't get the pizza! My husband didn't like it and they gave him another meal for free and didn't charge him for the pizza.We had wonderful massages at the spa. The gym is a good size. We planned to use it but caught vacation fever. :-) The hotel is near the end of Waikiki headed toward Diamond Head so there wasn't as much hustle and bustle as mid-Waikiki. It was still busy though. Waikiki isn't one of those rest and relaxation type places. The Marriott is large, not an intimate boutique type hotel. You don't need a car the entire time you're there. You can do a lot of walking, catch the buy or the trolley do get around Waikiki. We rented a car for two days to see other parts of the island. Parking isn't cheap, about $26 per night but you do have in and out priviledges. They program your room key to get in and out of the garage. It was quite convenient.But we really enjoyed our stay. The beds were nice and comfortable. We're big Marriott fans and ended up buying a time share at Ko Olina.

They were able to bring the price down to the elite rate, but their policy is to give you an upgrade to Platinum members at all costs. This Marriott did not have a Concierge Lounge, even though I had been told they had one. he concierge people at the hotel are very poor. One lady recommend a restaurant that she indicated was a short walking distance away but it was at least a half mile away and not a place you would walk through at night (towards diamond head).The hotel is close to shopping and dining, but this is not really a perk as all the hotels are close to dining, and in fact, the marriott is actually a bit away from all the other areas and finer dining and shopping. I could go on an on about the poor service at the pool-side bar, the non-helpful concierge, the slow and unfriendly check-in personel but I don't have the time. Do your self a favor and spend the extra $50-100 a night and stay a a much better place that has a nice restaurant, better pools, better rooms, friendly staff with a better concierge. Stay away at this hotel at all costs. This is coming from someone who was a diehard of marriott and was a loyal follower. There is something wrong with the management of this hotel and they do not cater to their guests. My suspicion is that they don't make there money on repeat business and they do marriott vacations and tours and nothing else. The only good thing I can say about the hotel were the bell hops and valet guys, they were helpful in gettting cabs, telling me how to get diamond head, etc.One last thing, I have stayed at other Marriotts in the US and in Europe and this hotel did not match their standards. I have seen other people accustomed to Marriott state this as well on this hotel, so don't expect much from this Marriott.

<Author>anne777
<Content>Okay hotel, a little too far away I stayed at the Marriott Waikiki for 9 nights with my husband and adult son. We booked a corner ocean view room to ensure having extra space for 3 adults.The room was of a good size, but only had 2 double beds instead of the 2 queen beds the site advertised.The bathroom was tiny for a 4 star hotel room. The shower is over the bathtub but it had good water pressure and an easy to operate tap system. The toilet and bath are seperated from the vanity basin area by a door. The vanity is a single sink with ample bench space but the whole concept could certainly benefit from modernisation.Cupboard space was very limited with several of the drawers under the tv unit being so shallow as to be useless.Housekeeping always did a great job of cleaning the room and were very flexible in waiting for us to leave the room at our leisure.The hotel is very large, so we were quite disappointed with the tiny pool. It is definitely not a resort pool. It is quite deep with little space to just stand and relax. With the beach just across the road, perhaps they expect guests not to be too fussed over the pool facilities.For a Marriott hotel, it did not really meet our expectations. We have stayed in Marriotts in Asia many times, and there is no comparison when you compare the service and the facilities of the Asian hotels.The Waikiki staff were polite and courteous but not overly welcoming or helpful.We felt that the location of the hotel was just too far away from the centre of the tourist strip, so it involved quite a bit of walking, which became a bit tiresome with a lot of shopping bags etc, especially after a week or so. We thought the Moana Surfrider Hotel looked very elegant and had a central location, so we will probably stay there next time, even though we will miss out on earning points with the Marriott rewards scheme.To summarize, a good hotel but we think the location is a little too far out and the pool size is a definite disappointment.

<Author>KimmyMassachusetts
<Content>Much better than I thought After reading some of the reviews on this hotel I was a little skeptical about what we were going to find. I asked for a room in the renovated tower and it was perfectly fine. Ok...the toilet/shower enclosure is a little small but it was clean and functional. We had a view of Diamond Head and if we looked a little to the right we could see Waikiki. The bed was the most comfortable we encountered in Hawaii and we slept great every night.Check in went smoothly although I could understand some people were upset when they came in on a bus and waited 40 minutes for check in. We didn't have any problems with the front desk or the concierge.We ate most of our meals at the Kuhio grill and despite the complaints of some people about its location or quality of food, we found it to have very decent, even good food, with pleasant help. My husband likes over-easy eggs and omelets that are not overcooked. At most hotels these two things are difficult to get. Not so here. The cooks did a fine job. As a matter of fact, any food that we got here at the Kuhio grill was better that everything we had on the subsequent Pride of America cruise (awful) or even at the JW Marriott Ilihani that we stayed at after the cruise (overpriced and not as good).The location was perfect for being picked up for tour buses and the 2 tours we did went very smoothly. Waikiki was a bit like Disney World with its throngs of tourists crowding the sidewalks but I didn't go there for peace and quite. We wanted to get used to the time change (6 hours) and see a few things before getting on the cruise.I would stay at this hotel again.One word of advice, always watch your itemized bill at any hotel. We had a restaurant charge that didn't belong to us at this hotel, mini bar charges that didn't belong to us on the cruise and incorrect upgrade charges added to our bill at another hotel.

<Author>Saysum
<Content>Great Family Hotel in, nice access to Family friendly things... Hello, the family and I (2 kids- 3 y/o and 2y/o) spent a week at this hotel during a big conference. I really enjoyed this hotel and will outline the details for you.Overview: This is a very big hotel located at the far end of Waikiki. It is composed of 2 big towers. The hotel has some nice restaurants and shops.Location: I liked the location even though it was exactly in the middle of Waikiki. You have easy access to Highway 1. It is very close to the Zoo, the beach, and the international marketplace. The downside was that it was across town from the Convention center (where meeting was held). People also don't like the fact that it is across the street from the beach. To be honest, we really never went to Waikiki Beach. We found a way better beach (see tip).Price: My company paid for this trip so I was really never concerned about the cost. We got a 2 double beds for $259 a night.Service: I really liked the service. Everyone was friendly (maybe just a hawaii thing). We asked for a crib and microwave and it was both delivered to our room in a timely fashion. Housekeeping was always quick to bring up more towels as needed.Room: The room was a fairly size one. I would have preferred 2 queens but they only had 2 doubles. There was a soft comfy chair with a chaise in the room as well. The room comes with a fridge and beautiful LCD TV. The beds were comfy and the showers had great water pressure. We had a nice ocean view from our balcony. Some people complained about the noise level. It was definitely not absent, but was bearable (we were on the 19th floor).Ammenities: WiFi was $12.95 a day. There were 2 pools. I think this was one of their weak points. I was hoping for a bigger, family friendly pool area. But the pool for this size of a hotel was disappointing. There were plenty of pool towels and they really didn't check to see how many you took. In the morning, we would load up on towels and just returned it at the end of the day. There were 2 ABC stores which made things convenient. Parking cost $24 for self and $29 for valet. My biggest tip would be to park across the street at Waikiki Banyan Tree for $50 a week. There was nightly entertainment next to the pool.All in all, we had a great time at this hotel and would definately stay here again. If you are looking to stay right on the beach, this hotel is not for you. It is not over the top fancy, but very nice.

<Author>Mrs.LTD
<Content>Wonderful Resort! We stayed at the Waikiki Marriott from April 17th-April 21st. We had an executive suite on the 24th floor, with a city view. Hotel - The hotel was so clean and such a pleasant place to be. They have two pools and one really hot hot tub on the 3rd floor. Plenty of towels that you could take to the pool or beach with you. There is a bar next to the pool that plays live music every night, and the view is great. There is a laundry room on the 3rd floor also, that was really nice for washing clothes before returning home. The lobby is beautiful, and there are many shops on the main level of the hotel, with an ABC store (like a Walgreens minus the pharmacy) to buy anything you may have forgotten, or suveniors for very reasonable prices. The resort is right across from the beach, and has everything from umbrella to long board rentals. The water also has a wall that breaks waves, so it is a perfect spot if you are bringing kids. But, right down the beach is a great spot for surfing, boogie boarding ect with tons of waves.Room - The room was fantastic. Recently renovated and very hip/chic. Huge, soft bed with 9 pillows, a pull out couch, flat screen TV, mini kitchen area with a refridgerator and sink and two nice lanais. Full length mirror in the closet that is attached to the bathroom. The water pressure was great, and they had plenty of shampoo, conditioner, body wash, soap and lotion.We were in town for the Kokua festival, and it was a 5 minute walk down the street. It is in a perfect location to bars, restaurants and great shopping.

<Author>chisox05
<Content>Nice Overnight Stay My wife, teenage son and I spent one night here as a treat so that we could easily attend Jack Johnson's Kokua Festival at the Waikiki Shell. The Shell is an easy walk from the hotel. We stayed in a partial ocean view room which means that you can see the ocean while seated on the lanai, but not from inside the room. The room was very nice and everything was in good condition. The front desk staff displayed fine Aloha spirit. We tried to get a late checkout, but unfortunately they were sold out for that night. They were generous enough to let us keep our car parked there into the evening at no extra charge (It was $24/day), however, and that was a big help since parking is a premium in Waikiki.We had a great dinner at Arancino di Mare, an Italian restaurant in the hotel. I wouldn't normally recommend that visitor eat Italian food in Hawaii, but the quality of the food here would be a good choice after you've tried some of Hawaii's regional cuisine.The pool was fine with nicely padded lounge chairs, plenty of towels and poolside drink and food service. We had a little trouble flagging down a waitress for service though. Two of them walked right past us. I think they're instructed not to pester the guests for drinks which is a good policy, but they may have gone a little too low key.I was a little disappointed that you could hear traffic noise in the room. Not too loud, but bothersome when big trucks went by. We were on the 9th floor, but since you're right on Kalakaua Ave there's lots of traffic well into the night. If noise like that bothers you you may be happier somewhere like the Sheraton, Halekulani, Outrigger Reef or Hilton Hawaiian Village that are on the beach, but a block away from Kalakaua.Overall we were quite happy and we'd come back here again.

<Author>lmn2
<Content>Served its purpose My husband, daughter and I just returned from our stay at The Waikiki Beach Marriott. As the title of my review suggests, this property served it's purpose. It has a wonderful location across the street from Kuhio Beach and just about any where you wanted to go eat or do in the Waikiki area was within walking distance ( a good way to burn off some of those calories). We did not encounter any noise from Resort Quest as mentioned in other reviews. The nightly entertainment was good.  What keeps this property from getting an above average rating or better is that some of the employees were barely luke warm. Our best luck with concierge was with the male concierge people, one woman in the concierge desk (the K building) could not have been more uninterested in helping with anything. My husband and I inquired about going to pearl harbor and she struggled to write down that there is a shuttle you could take. She is clearly unhappy in her job We got more info from the woman at the time share desk next to her than from G. If you want good info with good service, stick with the concierge desk next to the check-in desk. The gentlemen here were very happy to help whether it was advising us on how to best get to Diamond Head for a hike or for dinner reservations unlike the other woman at the desk in our building Speaking of checking in, we had booked an ocean view room. What we were assigned was a partial ocean view room (which the picture I took from the balcony matched the digital picture frame at the desk for this category). After what was like haggling for a car (the desk person kept going to a back room) we finally were upgraded (at our expense no less) the next day. I had even called my travel agent and was told that the reservation manager was to call me (no phone call). My husband and I figured that this was because they avoided calling us as the travel agent would have negotiated a better price for the upgrade and since there is a six hour time difference from where our travel is (EDT) and the hotel, we probably didn't get the better price. Just a point of reference, when booking a room(s) along with the better room, better view, the beds were bigger. We went from full size beds to queen size and given that husband is a big guy (~ 230 lbs) this was well worth the price for me. You wouldn't think you would have to call a hotel directly to discern the finer points of the rooms but this is what the desk person told us we needed to do in the future so as not to get in a repeat situation.A small sticking point to be aware of is that given the one way streets in Waikiki, what I found less than satisfactory is that when you are being dropped off at the hotel, you are brought in the rear entrance. Not a problem when you are coming from dinner but when you arrive after a very long day of travel from the east coast and you would like help from the bell hops, there are none on this side to help you when you arrive. They do help you when you leave though.The gym here is small given the size of the property. It is very crowded in the morning but in the afternoon (~ 4pm) no issues. The web site mentions a complimentary membership to 24 hour Fitness. They (meaning the hotel) didn't offer (including the book on the desk that tells you about services offered the hotel) and I didn't ask. This was our second trip to Oahu and we felt the service was much better at the Hyatt down the street than at the Marriott.

<Author>giromondo
<Content>It's everything that's good and bad about Marriotts This is an absolute monster of a hotel - it's huge and has only a single front desk. So you may encounter lines at check-in or check-out. It's fairly nice as far as Marriotts go - but kind of sterile, dull, predictable (which isn't all bad, but if you close the curtains, you may as well be in Ohio or Kansas). i.e., they haven't done a great job of giving a local feel to the place (aside from the palm trees and orchids in the atrium). There's a fair amount of street noise if you're on the lower floors.It's not a super value - we paid $1000 for 3 nights in an ocean view room. We really enjoyed watching the spectacular sunsets from the balcony. The configuration of the hotel is L-shaped so that for the most expensive rooms, the balconies have no privacy. One way, you have a great beach view, the other way, you're looking into dozens of hotel rooms. The bed and bathroom were clean and comfortable - not super-luxe by any means.The extras add up quickly. $22/day for parking (more if you valet). $26 for the breakfast buffet (it was included in the package we booked thru Travelocity). The buffet was quite good, but there was often a 10-15 minute lineup to get in.The pool is fine - again, nothing special. Many Waikiki hotels have more interesting pools. There's a big pile of towels that you can use for the beach.We liked the location - at the Diamond Head end of the strip. There are several great restaurants on Kapahulu Ave, if you want to avoid eating in the hotel or on the strip (generally, very mediocre fare unless you're a fan of the Cheesecake Factory). Don't miss Ono Hawaiian Food (about 1/4 mile up Kapahulu) for some authentic Hawaiian food.

<Author>Teacherguy
<Content>Loved our stay here. A beautiful hotel on the beach. I stayed at the Marriott Beach resort in Waikiki in January 2008 with my wife and kids. We loved it. It is located right on the main strip (accross the street from the beach). The rooms were quiet (no street noise) or party noise from any of the floors. It takes less than 10 mins to get from the room to the beach. With so many hotels in the area, it was well worth the money to have a hotel that is a quick walk from the beach.The staff were all very friendly,and very willing to answer any questions. The rooms are beautifully decorated, included flat screen tv, soft beds, duvet, and in room fridge. There is a parking garage ($20/day parking fee), which comes in handy due to the lack of public parking in the area.This resort is large, having two towers, 5 restaurants, 2 pools, a spa, etc. After a day or so, it is easy to navigate your way around the grounds.A couple of things to note. The restaurants are very expensive to eat in (breakfast buffet at the Kuhio Grill was about $35/adult). Also, the staff at the recreation counter are more than happy to make reccomendations on things to do. The problem we found was that they only refer you to certain tour companies (the ones that were the most expensive). Ask around and shop around for better deals. The ABC convenience store staff (in the lobby) gave us the scoop that only the locals know.

<Author>BigdawgChicago
<Content>Rooms Need Renovation!! This was my fourth time at the hotel and the most disappointing. When I stayed here two months ago I booked only a city view room because I was there just three nights and didn't want to pay extra for a better view. I was in room 2452 in the P tower which was a corner room with two lanai, one facing Diamond Head and the other facing the ocean, albeit a couple of blocks away. The views were very nice and the room was freshly renovated and spacious. When I returned with my wife in January I paid the extra $50 a night to be in the K tower to get a partial ocean view and had a decent view of Waikiki Beach and the ocean. The problem was the room, and all others on the floor, are sadly in need of renovation. The furniture and carperting were worn and outdated, the lamp shades were faded and the light was totally inadequate, the desk chair was not suited for desk work and the the bathroom was not only the size of a small closet but also needed renovation. So the room I paid an extra $50 a night for paled in comparison to the cheaper room. Makes sense huh?Not to mention that if you read other reviews of the hotel you will see that guests are upgraded to the K trower for no additional cost which the hotel did not do for me despite knowing it was my fourth stay and I was a Silver Rewards customer. If you get a renovated room the hotel is worth it, if you get a room like I had you will be disappointed. Also, the pool has to be one of the worst at any Marriott resort hotel so if you are looking to spend a lot of time at the pool, do not stay here. The breakfast buffet, which I have had in the past, is good but for the $22 they charge you should walk on by and go down a block to Lulu's for a good view of the ocean and decent food. Or walk a few blocks up Kuhio street to Perry's Smorgyi where you can have the breakfast buffet for $7.95 with a dollar off if you use their coupon in one of the tourist brochures and no tip because there are no waitresses. The selection is not vast and the food is of very average quality but the price is right and you can be in and out very quickly. There are many other inexpensive, fast service places to eat nearby including a Wolfgang Puck take out right across the street. If you park in the garage expect very narrow lanes with blind curves so you need to be very cautious. On the plus side the staff seemed friendly and attentive.

<Author>jkaumana
<Content>Good, But Could have Been Better I stayed at this property four nights in mid-January of 2008.After booking me into one of the worst rooms in the hotel (one of six rooms with no balcony and a bed which was against the wall right next to the parking garage) I was reassigned to a better room in the mauka tower. The hotel was not shy about squeezing you for the extras, either. Approx. $14 a day for use of the internet, $20 a day for parking, and $1 for each local phone call. Be prepared for lots of large tour groups as well.In sum, a decent place to stay, but be very careful of the rate you pay, and don't be afraid to speak up if you don't like your room.

<Author>littlemac4
<Content>Fantastic Deal! Great location This hotel is in an excellent location if you want to avoid the glitz and noise at the center of Waikiki. It is just steps away from the ocean, across Kalakaua Ave., and is near Kehoe Beach for the sunset dance shows. The hotel itself is very nice. There are two rooftop pools, which can get a bit crowded in the middle of the day.The partial ocean view was perfect and we could see Diamond Head as well. If you stay here and are worried about the loud music from the hotel across the street, you should know that they stop at 10:00 PM. The restaurant is very nice, but avoid the outdoor part when there are birds around -- they don't mind landing on your table and nibbling on your meal. The breakfast, which was included in our deal, was a full buffet including omelet bar, every day. Don't be dissuaded by the line for breakfast. When there is one, it moves fast. The service in the restaurant was very competent.Our first room smelled so bad that we had to ask for a change in room. The response from the hotel was immediate and we were moved nearby to an upgaded room, but I wonder why they didn't know about the problem before we checked in.

<Author>CanadaGalOnTheGo
<Content>Better than expected Given some of the so-so reviews about the Marriott, we had modest expectations. However, the hotel was very clean and the staff were always friendly and helpful. The pool was never crowded and we had no problems getting a lounge chair at the sunny pool (p tower), if we were there by 10:00 am.We weren't sure which tower to choose, but asked for the k tower because it was closer to the beach. We were happy with our choice because even with only a partial ocean, the view was amazing. The lanais also appear to be larger in the K tower, which worked for us because we would often get take out from Wolfgang's and other local restaurants and ate outside in privacy. The room was large and was spotless. Nothing too fancy, but it seemed to be freshly painted, and there were no signs of wear and tear, as another reviewer indicated when writing about the K Tower.A bit of a warning -- Waikiki is noisey, even up on our higher floor, but we were prepared for this. We liked the city/beach combination and there was a lot we didn't get to do. We'll definitely be back and would stay at the Marriott again.

<Author>globeseekerpa
<Content>Definitely a disappointment After spending dozens of nights in Marriotts last year, I was looking forward to visiting the Marriott Waikiki Beach, for which I had been saving up all those Marriott Rewards points. The property was definitely a let down and I would not have been pleased had I been paying their high rates for my entire vacation. The hotel does occupy a prime spot across from the beach in the middle of all the Waikiki action. Like many of the other hotels in this area, it is HUGE. The check-in personnel were efficient and friendly, and I was pleased by my room upon arrival. It was definitely the best aspect of the hotel. It was essentially standard Marriott issue, but with some nice decor touches that gave it an island flavor, and island-themed toiletries in the bathroom.The hotel felt over run, perhaps because it was the holiday season. There were people everywhere at all times of day or night. At certain times of the day you even had to wait in line to take the elevator. This was because the hotel was conducting elevator maintenance, not exactly a smart thing to do in peak season when the property is near 100% occupancy. The pool area was always crowded, at times there were so many people in the hot tub that you could not fit another person into it. There definitely need to be more pool attendants. As the day went on, the pool area showed signs of wear and tear. There were dirty towels strewn everywhere and puddles of standing water that needed to be cleaned up. The pads on the lounge chairs needed to be changed more frequently, they often appeared damp and sandy from whoever had used them before.Since you are at a Marriott resort, there are timeshare sales booths everywhere in this hotel. The bell desk staff was noticeably unfriendly when I had to store my bag and when I went to retrieve it. They seemed like they were unhappy to be helping out the haoles  were definitely were not geared towards customer service. While the rooms were nice, this property charges deluxe rates for an experience that is anything but.

<Author>timidtravelerUs
<Content>Big room, beautiful ocean My family stayed here for 4 days over Christmas. I am surprised by the negative reviews. The location is great, across street from the beach and a short walk to less crowded beaches. Near the end of Waikiki, so a bit less crowded. There is a nice park with great banyan trees within 1/2 mile. We didn't rent car, so avoided parking costs and just walked, or took a bus or taxi where we wanted to go.Our room was a suite with ocean view. We loved the balconeys and enjoyed just sitting and looking at the ocean. Yes, the band was loud at night, but we shut the doors and went to bed. Small bathrooms, but our room had two, so they were fine. Comfortable beds, lots of pillows, nice bedding. I enjoyed the towel check out, the ABC stores, and the staff. Really, the ocean is so wonderful, just being near it is great.

<Author>ontheplane
<Content>Overall good hotel We would stay here again. This is our second trip to waikiki and the hotel's proximity to the beach is great. Beach towels can be checked out on the pool deck and the beach is just across the street from the hotel. The hotel is large. Two towers (we stayed in the one closest to the beach). We had no problems with the elevators. The pools are a bit small but are heated and hardly crowded when we were there. The gym, also small, serves its purpose with a few elipticals, treadmills, stationary machines, and a free-weights rack. The hotel has two ABC stores that have everything from quick snacks and essentials to souvenirs. Our package came with breakfast. Buffet style pasteries, fruits, eggs and sausage, cerials and waffles, and a made to order omelet bar.The room we stayed in had a great view of the beach. I often sat out on the lanai just listening to the ocean. The room was cleaned and re-stocked everyday. The bed was very comfortable. The bathroom is on the small side but serves it's purpose. In my opinion the room, and hotel, are a bit dated. I travel often and can tell from older, remodeled, and new from the ground up hotels. This hotel seems older. But still a nice hotel.Location is the hotel's best selling point. It is a few minutes walk to the international market, a block a way from the zoo, and across the street from kuhio beach. (We previously stayed at the Hawaii Prince which had great rooms with the best view but quite a ways from downtown waikiki.)

<Author>samantha2000
<Content>Great Hotel for location and food, but lacking in room quality and decor We just returned from a nine day stay at the Waikiki Beach Marriott Hotel. I give a tip of the hat to the front desk clerks and the housekeeping staff ..... they were really good. The open air theme of the hotel lobby floor was a truly refreshing reminder that we were in Hawaii.The food in the Kuhio Grill was superb .... we had 9 breakfasts there and 3 buffet dinners, and the food and the service was superb. You were never rushed and there never seemed to be line-ups.Elevators worked terrific, no problems there.Being right across the road from the beach was really delightful and all the shops were so close by.Now, for the down side. We stayed in a Deluxe Oceanfront room which was really great. just that we expected more quality from a Marriott Hotel. The room was quite sparesely furnished, with a small clothes cupboard with ancient louvered doors and 6 coat hangers. There were 2 small drawers in the TV cupboard to store all the rest of our belongings. Luggage was barely able to be stored in the closet. We had 2 chairs, and a writing desk and a small round table. The bathroom left a lot to be desired. They have replaced the taps and faucets ........ but the bathtub has been cleaned so much that it is down below the enamel and it did not drain so you were standing in 3 inches of water while showering. I hated even standing in it to shower. The tub and toilet are in a small cramped room with a door and the basin and mirror are located just outside. Again, an old sink that should have been replaced years ago.Other that that our stay in Hawaii was really great. Next time we come we are planning on checking out a Condo, as you really do not spend that much time in the Hotel, but when you do you want the quality you paid for in the surroundings.

<Author>Tim2458
<Content>Huge Hotel, Good Location and Decent Price This is a large hotel with two separate buildings connected via an outdoor walkway on the third floor. That walkway is where you will also find the hotel's two pools, one of which has a whirlpool/hot tub nearby. The pools are not large, but in my 12 days there, I did not see them packed. There is also a coin--operated laundry on this floor.If you do not like crowds, do not stay here. Many collegiate athletic teams stay here. Several women's basketball teams and the Boise State football team were here during my stay.The staff are welcoming and friendly. Since I was here for almost two weeks, there was a familiarity that led to nice greetings and good service, from the front desk to the guys who did the valet parking ($25 a day, only $5 more per day than self-parking in the large garage at the hotel -- valet was handled in a more convenient outdoor lot across the street from the driveway at the hotel). I had a very late-night flight back east and I was extended a late check-out of 6 p.m. at no charge. However, I will point out that two other parties in my group were charged $100 for the same courtesy, so I guess it all depends on who you get at the front desk.My room was on a floor in the middle of the Paoakalani tower. If you are given a room in the Kealohilani, the older of the two high-rises -- the one closest to the beach and Kalakaua Avenue, ask to be put into the Paoakalani. A colleague in the other tower asked for a move because the rooms in the Kealohilani tower were in sad shape.Rooms are small, relative to other Marriotts in which I've stayed, and the bathrooms are snug. The sink is outside the room in which the toilet and shower are located. There is good water pressure and toiletries are replenished daily. The bed is super comfy and I had an oceanview room, which truly was oceanview -- as long as you looked straight out, rather than down at the parking lot and the tops of several buildings (including St. Augustine's Catholic Church, conveniently located across the street). There was a small refrigerator in the armoire, convenient but its compressor was very loud.The hotel can be noisy. There was a large group from Japan going from room to room at very late hours, and the room next to mine sounded like they had a drinking game going on at 2 a.m. A call to hotel security quieted that. However, the room must have been vacant several times during my stay because I could hear the alarm go off at 5 a.m. and buzz for quite some time.My often-stated complaint about Marriott rings true for this hotel, too. While there is wireless service, it is $12.95 a day., with no discount for longer stays. It is a nickel and dime attack on guests that many other hotels (and some Marriotts) have abandoned. This chain should do so across the board.There are two very good restaurants out of the many in the hotel -- Sansei for sushi and d.k. Steak House, which served one of the best NY strip steaks I've ever had. As for Sansei, one evening I went after 10 p.m. and all sushi was 50 percent off.And, a few hours after you enjoy your meals, you can go to the very small gym one floor below. Sorry to say the StarTrac CV equipment is subpar. The treadmills had cardiotheater TVs. For the crosstrainers and one stair machine, there are a couple of regular TVs at the front of the room. There is also a small collection of free weights. There is a 24-hour gym about a block from the hotel on Kalakaua to which a friend belongs. If you're a hard-core workout fiend, you may want to go there.There is a spa adjacent to the fitness center with a limited selection of treatments, plus a manicure station and hair salon. If you want to go to a VERY nice spa, go out 18 miles west of Waikiki to the Marriott Ihilani, which offers a beautiful facility with an assortment of massages, wraps, scrubs, and other treatments.The beaches of Waikiki are right across the street from the Marriott and there are many restaurants nearby. Roy's opened a Waikiki branch across from the Halekulani -- very fine food and great service. Speaking of the Halekulani, I had a significantly better breakfast at a lower price there than I had at the Marriott, which has a decent buffet, but if you are going to just order off-the-menu, I recommend a stroll to the Halekulani where you can enjoy the beachfront view and be treated like royalty while enjoying a fine morning repast.Would I stay here again? This was already my second visit, and overall, it's fine. Posh, no. Comfy, yes. For about $269 a night, not a bad price for Waikiki at Thanksgiving time.

<Author>irun5k
<Content>Consistently Good I've stayed here a few times for business and most recently for pleasure. They sometimes have good rates for Hawaii residents, which was the case for the recent pleasure stay.In all cases the rooms have been consistent. I've never had much of a view in the P tower, but I've visited rooms in the K tower that have a phenomenal view of the beach. I assume these rooms are out of my price range by a long shot, which would explain why I've never stayed in one. The rooms are similar in quality, the main difference is the view.The rooms are relatively quiet for the location, all things considered. The beds are comfortable. The bathrooms aren't anything exciting. Personally, I think the rooms at a place like the Hawaii Prince are a good deal nicer, but it is unfortunately in the marina district and not really walking distance to the main part of the Waikiki strip.I enjoy the pool deck and especially the hot tub. This area is spacious and is actually a terrace. There is something about being perched up a few stories high that makes it pleasurable- can't really explain it.Their restaurant, Sansei, is my favorite place to eat in the entire state. If you like sushi, or even steak or normal seafood, it is hard to go wrong.Overall, assuming you get a decent price, this is a good place to stay for anybody who wants a slightly nicer property.

<Author>bice710
<Content>A nice facade, but look closer- it's worn down and not Marriott quality I have been to Waikiki several times and though I have hung out at the Waikiki Beach Marriott, I'd never stayed there. I have actually gone scuba diving with the dive shop there and those guys are really good. The bar closes REALLY early (11 even on a Saturday night) and is pretty low key. For a little more lively atmosphere go to the ResortQuest bar right across the street. They have live music and it's usually a pretty full house.So, I finally stayed at the WBM one night and I have to admit, I expected a lot from seeing the beautiful lobby and shops. Obviously the location, right across the street from the beach in the heart of Waikiki, is fantastic. When you get to the rooms, they look nice at first, until you look a little closer. The glass on the bathroom door was cracked. The tub and shower was cracking and peeling. The chairs were old and musty. The beds (which look beautiful) were a false front...a hard as nails mattress with some foam on top (which didn't help) and like 50 thread-count sheets...yes that's right, not a normal Marriott resort 300 TC or higher. These were so rough my skin actually got irritated from them. It's clear that rather than doing room renovations (which this old hotel needs), they decided to add some things that look good to hide the problems of the rooms. Sorry WBM, I expected better from you. I realize they're getting away with it because of the location, but it's just not the normal Marriott quality. I do have to say the staff was very friendly and helpful.

<Author>Angela_o
<Content>Paradise My husband I just came back from a 7 day vacation. We stayed at the Marriott Waikiki and we were very pleased. We were married there 5 years ago and decided to go back this year for our anniversary and we couldn't have been more pleased. Our room was ready a little early so we were able to check-in and shower and get our vacation started which was great after flying for hours.The rooms are very nice. Housekeeping does a wonderful job. The rooms do not come with microwaves but you can request one if they have one available. We didnt know you could do that until i read a comment from this site. We were very pleased. We requested it and they actually took it to the room before we made it there. Having a microwave makes the vacation a little more convenient.This hotel is located right across the street from the beach and near shopping. We did not rent a car this time, although you can rent one from the hotel. We took tours which were very educational and less stressful. Everything is within walking distance from the hotel. The trolley which we didn't know about until this trip is very accessible. It stops right next door every 20 minutes and will take you to the mall for just 2 dollars per person. We took a few tours which at first I thought were overpriced but in the end they were worth it. We learned a lot more about the wonderful island and people living there.I do get a little annoyed by the timeshare people but it seems like you cant go anywhere these days without running into them. Once they start recognizing you they stop pestering you.This time we went to the flea market. They are opened on weekends and wednesdays. The hotel offers a shuttle to take you there which is 9 dollars a person which is roundtrip. You just tell the driver what time you want to be picked up. I would definitely wait to buy souveniers until you go to the flea market. I made the mistake of buying mine right off the main street and I paid way more. You can get everything at the flea market for lower prices but dont forget to bring comfortable shoes, its huge!I would definitely stay at this hotel again. I miss it already.Now back to reality..........................

<Author>sonjaandrob
<Content>Excellent Me and my husband just spent 7 days at the Marriott as part of our honeymoon and we had no complaints at all.We arrived to be greeted with the expected staff wishing to carry our bags inside but we kindly declined. The entrance was quite spectacular with a large rockery with plants and a mini waterfall feature.We arrived early afternoon. Check-in was quick and efficient. We paid 拢195 per night for our room on the 16th floor that had a king-sized bed and view overlooking the beach and a balcony. My first impression of the room was very good. It was very big and spotlessly clean with good facilities - ironing board, iron, hairdryer, toiletries etc. I've read one person comment on the mediocre nature of the toiletries but I would have thought most people take their own anyway so I wouldn't let that put you off. There was a fridge in the room as well which I thought was much better than the usual extortionately priced mini-bars you find in hotels. We bought our own water and alcohol to store in it and drank it at our leisure on the balcony. The room was made up every day and towels changed if require - leave in the bath if you want them changing or hang up if you can re-use them.We didn't sample any of the hotel's restaurants or food except breakfast, that was included in our room rate.It was possibly the best breakfast experience I've had at a hotel. We got there at about 7.30am every morning. Service was excellent. We were shown to our table and then served tea and coffee and frm then on it was self-service. There was everything you could have possibly wanted....hot cooked food, cereals, juisces, meats and chesses, oriental food, pastries and a fantastic omelette station that also served hot waffles and pancakes.We did notice there was always a large queue building up whilst we were eating but this always went down very quickly.We didn't use any of the hotel's facilities but could see the swimming pool from our room. It looked a decent size and i never saw anybody in it.There were a couple of things that slightly annoyed me about the place but we soon got used to them - the toilets in the bedroom - they were very forceful and noisy ( abit like aeroplane ones) and you could always hear other customers in neighbouring rooms and rooms above whenever they flushed their toilets.Me and my husband were early to bed and early to rise on the first few nights and I couldn't help hearing some loud and annoying karaoke type entertainer every night. He seemed to be coming from the pool deck of the hotel. I don't know if he was on every night but he was very annoying when we were trying to relax and all you could hear was his voice blaring out.The hotel was very conveniently located right opposite waikiki beach and close to all the local high street shops.All in all a very pleasant stay and we would return here again.

<Author>PHXroadwarrior
<Content>Tired and Rough around the edges I am a business traveler and stay at Marriott properties 150+ nights a year, and am very loyal to the chain. Thus, I generally know what to expect when I arrive at a hotel. I value consistency across properties and a standardized level of service and amenities, and I find Marriott generally does this better than other chains.I was disappointed by this property. While it is located right across the street from the beach, and the view from most of the rooms is beautiful, other aspects of the property left me disappointed.This is an older hotel (probably 30 years old), not built originally as a Marriott, and it gets heavy foreign tourist traffic...all ingredients for disaster even before you set foot on the property. I realize that this is not the typical airport business Marriott, and a resort is different, but it still failed in many respects where Marriott should know how to do better.The room (2269) had the terrific new Marriott Revive bed, but the rest of the room was tired and in need of refurbishment. The carpet, furniture and wallcovering were worn out and shabby. The bathroom smelled badly of mold in the shower, and I tried in vain to find the source of the terrible smell. Bath towels were cheap and small, and they did not stock adequate numbers in the room for a resort hotel where you may shower a couple times a day coming and going from your activities. Even just better linens would have classed the room up a great deal. No robe. Tolietries were average. Standard glaring fluorescent lights in all the lamps which always make it too bright in one part of the room and pitch black in another part. The room did have a great lanai which was fun to sit on for the sunsets.My room rate, booked on [--], was $191/night, which is fairly reasonable these days now that hotel prices are so high. They accidentally put another guest's bill under my door, and he was paying $269.Elevators were undergoing renovation, meaning a 5-10 minute wait most times, sometimes waiting for two or three elevator cars because you were standing in the lobby with 20 other people also waiting.I ate two times at the poolside restaurant on the third floor overlooking the beach. Each time I found the food of crappy theme park snackbar quality, the service nonchalant and slow, and the prices high. I was really taken by the big bowl on every table of individual packets of every imaginable condiment....is this how you serve ketchup and mustard in a place with any class at all? Ick. My simple lunch with two fruity Hawaii cocktails ran over $40. Dinner one evening in the Steakhouse, also on the third floor, was delicious (the steaks really are as great as they claim) and the service was really attentive, but I was befuddled by the restaurant's decor which was an odd cross between Denny's and a Chinese Restaurant and had a bunch of vinyl seats and fake plants.. I also found it funny how they advertise a beach view for the restaurant, and the picture window is about the same size as the one on the front of my house back home. Unless you get one of three or four tables by the window, forget about seeing the beach.I agree with another poster that the pools were really small for a property of this size. The one nearest the beach gets the most traffic and it's teeny-tiny and chock full of kids and middle-aged fat men in Speedos. The back pool always looked empty to me and much quieter.There are lots of shops on-site and nearby, and the hotel really is in the heart of everything, which is a huge plus. All the fun stuff in Waikiki is within a 1-15 minute walk.Valet parking (at $25/day) was fast, efficient and professional. My car was always waiting when I called down before leaving the room. Self parking was $15/day.Every staff member I encountered was friendly and helpful.Overall, if I had to stay at a Marriott, and I was really loyal, I would stay here again. If I was open to other properties, I would definitely consider something more fresh and a little more refined elsewhere in Waikiki. I'll be back again if they renovate!  
<Date>Oct 14, 2007

<Author>pamurchu
<Content>Solid four stars We just returned from eight nights at the Marriott Waikiki Beach. Our reservation was exactly as it was booked. The front desk employees were courteous and efficient. There was an erroneous charge to our room at check out and the problem was handled in a professional manner. We were checked out and on our way in five minutes. The elevators ran in a timely fashion, and the breakfast buffet was excellent. Half way through our stay, the room locks were changed as were our automated keys. The older locks were difficult to use, but the new lock worked the first time we inserted the key cards. (They might be changing locks floor by floor. I read where others had trouble using the key cards, but apparently they are trying to correct this.) We could hear the music from the pool bar, but it finished before 11 o'clock nightly and was pleasurable. If we did not wish to hear the music, we simply closed the lanai door. And of course, the beds were comfy and easy to get lost in! We used the room safe, and had nothing stolen. The spa was average, as were the bars, shops, and pool area. But this was a most pleasant stay with no malfunctions. I would stay here again as we enjoyed being at the end of the beach, away from the central part of hotel row. Also, it was convenient to the Waikiki Shell. Definitely should be considered as a midprice choice for accommodations.

<Author>nitabita
<Content>Nice Hotel, Great Location My husband and I stayed at the Marriott for our honeymoon. We were there from Sept. 11 - 17. The hotel is located right across the street from the beach. You can check out the hotel pool towels for use at the beach. I agree with other visitors that said that the hotel pool is small. We never used the pool. The hotel is located across from Resortquest which is one of the major pick up/drop off locations for the tour buses.There are plenty of activities to do. You should never get bored. The locals are friendly and helpful. We didn't rent a car but would consider it when we go back. You can get around easily without a car though.We stayed in the corner deluxe room... on the 18th floor. We had a GREAT view of the ocean. I think if we were on a higher floor we would be able to see Diamondhead as well. We sat on the balcony and watched the sunsrise every morning. The only negative comment about the room would be the lighting in the bathroom. It was VERY dim and gave off a red hue. Even with the poor lighting we'd stay here again because of the location and easy access to everything.

<Author>Canada_Turtle
<Content>Should be considered as one of your choices for Waikiki This review is written by a business traveler who typically frequents Marriott and Hilton-chain hotels. This review is based on a 4-night stay in September 2007 and an 8 night stay in July 2007.The hotel meets or exceeds the quality one typically finds in a Marriott property. This is clearly an older hotel that was renovated some time ago. Decent job on the renovations.Pros: - solid choice, solid service, solid value. - rooms that make you feel comfortable. - be sure to ask for an ocean view room, preferably a corner suite. - great-tasting Honolulu Cookie Company cookies are provided upon check-in in the room; leave a note on the bedside table to have the turn-down service folks leave cookies every night instead of chocolates, if so desired. - great facilities. - across the street from the beach.Opportunities for improvement:  - no concierge lounge for Marriott Rewards Gold and Platnium members. - put in curved shower bars. - elevator service to the high floors (which is now being improved).It's essentially on the Diamond Head end of the main strip in Waikiki; however, this hotel is a solid choice for comfort, service, and proximity to shopping, eateries, and amenities.
