<Author>ArkansasOrchid
<Content>Beautiful view from corner deluxe room, 20th floor Waikiki has so many hotel choices that it helps to spend a little time deciding what is important to you. I decided that for us the top priorities were getting a clean, quiet room with a great view of the beach, a good sized room and bathroom, and avoiding the congestion of the construction areas. We booked a corner deluxe room at the Marriott and were very pleased. For the same price as a garden view room at the Royal Hawaiian and less than an ocean view room at the Outrigger Reef or Outrigger Beach, we had a great view from the 20th floor with a very large room (by Waikiki standards). Best points of the hotel: The corner deluxe rooms -- especially on high floors -- have a lanai on one side (facing toward the next hotel with a side view of the ocean) and a very large window covering most of the oceanfront wall. So the views are fabulous. It would be much better if the lanai were on the front, but strangely, the K tower (which is the one closest to the beach) does not have front facing lanais except maybe on the top floor. Also the corner deluxe rooms are unusually large for Waikiki rooms. Our room was clean and the beds are exceptional with many pillows and a down-filled mattress pad. Because hotel is at the end of Waikiki where hotels are across the street from the beach, the front view is really of the ocean and not of adjacent hotels. Because it is at the Diamondhead end, it is easy to get out of the hotel and onto H1 or other major roads. Air conditioning works well and we did not hear noise from the room on the other side. Staff was friendly. Like most major hotels, there is an ABC shop in the lobby plus a variety of other shops. Although there are no views from the main restaurant, we had dinner there twice and the food was perfectly acceptable. Unlike other reviewers, we never had to wait too long for an elevator.The less positive: The ResortQuest hotel next door blocks views toward the Diamondhead side and they have live music at their pool during breakfast and in the evenings. We were on a high floor and ran the air conditioning at night, so it didn't disturb us but on a lower floor or with the lanai doors open, this could be a problem. The parking garage is horrible, but that's probably true everywhere in Waikiki. The turns are very tight and the traffic goes both ways. You have to use the mirrors mounted on columns to see if other cars are coming and usually, one car would have to back up to allow the other to pass. Valet was easier, but my husband hates to have to call for the car every time we leave. On the plus side, we always found a parking space. The bathroom was adequate but not luxurious and strangely, there is only one light for the vanity area and the bathroom so if you go to the bathroom in the night, turning on the light may disturb your spouse.Overall, we were very pleased with the Marriott and would certainly return, especially for the corner deluxe room which is a good value for the price. Many of the negatives stated in other reviews are true of virtually all Waikiki hotels. This is definitely a place where is pays to do your research, and having stayed at a number of hotels in the area, we think this hotel is a good choice. If you want to be at the other end and don鈥檛 necessarily require a great ocean view, the Waikiki Parc (sister hotel of the Halekulani) is also a good choice.  
<Date>Sep 1, 2007

<Author>Patar
<Content>Not My Favorite Marriott This hotel is across the street from Waikiki Beach, but at the south end. The beach there has a breaker wall built out in the water. That makes for a calm pool (water kind of brackish) but you don't get the feel of ocean waves like you do a block or two north.The hotel has one of the most confusing layouts I've ever seen! There are two buildings and almost no signs explaining how to get where. Even checking into the hotel is a problem. We drove up to the entrance and it was packed with tour buses. I parked out front on the street and walked in. When I mentioned this at check in, the desk clerk told me that is actually the tour bus entrance. If I had gone around to the other side of the hotel, I would find valet parking and the consierge desk. The self parking garage has extremely narrow driving lanes so is nervewracking to drive in. You have to use your room key to get out of the garage, and our key never worked. We would have to push a button and talk to someone every time we exited. One night when we got back around 10 PM, the garage was full, and a hotel employee standing there told us we would have to use valet. They did not charge us extra for the valet parking, but it was a pain, because we had to drive completely around the block again, since valet parking was about 15 feet behind the parking garage entrance .We paid extra for a premium ocean view room. When we got to our room we were not happy. The hotel building we were in was built in an L shape. Our room was a couple of rooms off the crotch of the L. That meant our balcony sat at a 90 degree angle to someone else's balcony - and they were close enough to carry on a conversation with us! I called and complained, and they moved us further down the row of rooms and that was more private.We used the spa for a massage and aloe/noni wrap one evening. The noni was recommended to help with sun exposure. It smelled like something rotten! Not a very relaxing thing to lay covered in.On the bright side, the room was nicely furnished and clean.I am a Marriott Silver Rewards member, and I often choose Marriott properties. When I go back to Honolulu I will try a different hotel though.

<Author>bvwatson
<Content>Still a favorite Waikiki hotel I've reviewed the Waikiki Marriott before, in August 2006, so this is really just an update. The hotel continues to be my favorite hotel in Waikiki, for its location, the quality of the rooms and its staff. After reading other reviews here, I paid attention to the bed -- they're right, the beds are Great!!The elevators seem to be less of a problem this time around. It's a distance of about 2.5 miles and a pretty simple stroll, in about an hour...leaving some time to shop at a store or two along the way.All in all, I still recommend the Waikiki Marriott as a friendly place to stay in Waikiki.

Overall, my stay was excellent and enjoyable...highly recommend it!

<Author>Huckleberry
<Content>Pretty great ... but still needs some work. Overall ... when we stay on Oahu this is our favorite place (I have stayed at the Sheraton, etc). If you are happy to spend $300+ on a room then it is a good bet. It does have a few issues - see below. It is in a great location, it is clean, the rooms are well laid out and the beds are positively dream inducing. The views are great and the services/amenities are also hard to beat (2 pools, parkade, laundromat, wedding services, shops, bars, several restaurants, Seattles best coffee, etc)There are however a few really annoying issues which need to be resolved.Issue 1: The elevators in the tower away from the beach (so any room that is not a deluxe ocean view) are terrible. They are so dumb that they are not staggered (they all go to every floor) and they all try to go to the same location at once. Every morning people waited as they hit almost every floor. If you are on a high floor you will have no problem getting on but you wil have to make 15 stops on your way down. If you are on a lower floor (10 or lower) you might have to wait 5-7 times before an elevator car is empty enough to fit you (and god forbid your kids) on board. To be fair to the hotel ... they are currently addressing this. Did not help us for the 8 days we stayed there ... but should be fixed in 2 weeks or so from the date of this post.Issue 2: The Kuhio Beach Grill restaurant is overpriced and has a long wait every morning. Go to Arancinos (the Italian place) which is also in the hotel. The buffet is awesome and the cappucino is great.Minor Issue #3: The room keys suck. You have to shove them in and out multiple times to get the lock to respond. The parkade seems to read them perfectly. What gives? The first time I stayed there I went down to the desk twice for new keys before I realized that I had to try 20 times to get it to work. Maybe you will have better luck ... but they are old and need to be updated.Minor Issue #4. The gym has no windows. In such a beatiful place it seems criminal to me that the gym feels like a bunker. It is a decent gym ... but I want a view.I have stayed in this hotel 3 times and have always had a relaxing and happy time so I keep coming back. It is close to the zoo and an easy hike to Diamond head. It is close to shops and has a built-in parkade if you have a rental car (tip: get a new 07 convertible Sebring not a mustang).Some tips:1.) Stay on a higher floor if you have a partial or ocean view. You will get better scenery and will get first dibs on the dumb elevators in the morning.2.) Get a deluze ocean view room if you can spend the money... you will get a better view and much better elevators. You will also get to avoid the registration desk on your way to and from the beach. Our best experience 2 years ago was when we stayed in a Deluxe room (you get what you pay for ... I am sure I heard that somewhere :-)3.) Get up early ... you will get seated for breakfast without waiting ... you can go to Hanauma Bay before it gets crowded and you will get your Americano before the line starts. Oh ... and your elevator might not stop 15 times on the way down as it picks up competitors for the breakfast line.4.) Buy booze, water, food, etc at the ABC store and keep it in your room. For anyone new to Hawaii ... this is a must. Maker sure sunblock / sunscreen is the first thing you buy. The second thing you buy should be the Oahu Revealed guide for $16. Best money you will spend the whole trip.That's it ... hope this helps you out!  
<Date>Aug 15, 2007

<Author>Zville5
<Content>It is what it is Trying to avoid grade inflation so we've rated this one with 3 stars ... nothing terrible, nothing exceptional. In fairness to this Marriott, however, it must be seen in the context of Waikiki -- one of the world's love-it-or-hate-it locations. Waikiki is lots of people crammed into a little space, with a beach on one side and a wall of retail -- everything from highest-end boutiques to tourist schlock and sleaze -- on the other side. The Marriott reflects this situation in some respects, though it tries to overcome. Hotel is enormous, with convention center feeling. Be prepared to wait in line for an elevator, as late as 10 at night. The self-parking experience is not for the feint of heart, with choke points wide enough for only one car. The two pools are a major disappointment; one is a motel-sized postage stamp and the other is maybe two postage stamps. Too much concrete everywhere. And the hotel-based restaurants are overpriced and overrun. But the Marriott beds are wonderful, the rooms quiet, and the views on the Diamond Head side spectacular (though be aware that the lanais/terraces measure about 5 feet by 3 feet, so views are best enjoyed from the inside of the sliding door). Finally, as other reviewers have noted, the hotel's location on the eastern fringe of Waikiki makes it not only a tad quieter than the rest of the area but also much easier to access without getting caught up in traffic jams.

<Author>sctraveler45
<Content>Very nice hotel I just returned from an eight day stay at this great hotel and I would highly recommend it. However, before you go to this hotel (and Oahu in general) be sure that it is what you are looking for. Oahu is much more commecial than the rest of Hawaii, but in my case that was the major advantage. I took my 9 year old daughter to Oahu and we were never at a loss for things to do. Waikiki Beach is great, there are great snorkeling beaches nearby, and at night we had a blast just wandering around downtown Waikiki. Be sure and set aside a couple of days to visit less populated (and very beautiful) parts of the island and to visit Pearl Harbor. We rented a car for half of our trip and that is proabably about the right amount of time - while you are lounging at Waikiki there is no point in paying for a car (and for $20 per day parking). At check-in, we were convinced to upgrade to an ocean-view room (a bit more hard-sell than I would have preferred, admittedly), but I am very glad that we did. If you stay at this hotel, be sure and request the front tower (the back tower is a bit further from the ocean) and an upgrade to an ocean view room. I would not recommend eating breakfast at this hotel. There are tons of places nearby and the buffet in the hotel restaurant is very pricey (for example, Duke's breakfast buffet down the street is much better, is located on the beach, and is about half the price....there is also a McDonalds a block away that my daughter wanted to eat at a couple of mornings). Save your money for a nice dinner (there are two nice restaurants for dinner here and many nice restaurants within walking distance). If you are on a honeymoom or such, this may not be the hotel for you. It is a very large hotel with lots of guests, but I have to say for the size Marriott does a great job of making the hotel seem inviting. It is quiet, clean,and we never had to wait long for an elevator. The pools so seem a bit small for a hotel this size, but even that makes sense considering we spent very little time at the pool since Waikiki Beach was across the street. One negative for me was the quality of the room service. I tried it a couple of times and I don't think it is on par with the quality of other Marriott's room service; however, considering there are many dining options nearby that is not a major issue. Overall, I would highly recommend this hotel.  
<Date>Jul 22, 2007

<Author>cbbjr
<Content>Loved Waikiki and liked the Marriott I stayed at the hotel for a week in December. It is a great location and a nice 4 star hotel. Nothing opulent, but the rooms are good sized, clean, and have comfortable beds. In addition to a couple of ABC stores there are a few shops and restaurants on the lobby level.Obviously you are in Waikiki so there is a lot to see and do. The beach directly in front of the hotel is protected by a barrier wall and is very calm. It seemed to be a lot less crowded than the portion to your right towards the Royal Hawaiian.If you exit the hotel facing the beach and take a left, that section of the beach along the park seemed to have a pretty rough bottom (although there are signs posted warning people of this) that cut my feet just standing in the water.There were a few places to eat that seemed to stand out. Duke's at the Outrigger was great for breakfast (we also did dinner there one night, which was good, but nothing special). They have a solid buffet that looks out over the water with wonderful fruit and items like coconut, pineapple, and mango bread pudding. I think it cost around $15. For Thai we went to Keo's for dinner one night and it was excellent.For cheaper food options, we went to Ono Hawaiian Foods at 726 Kapahulu Ave. It is a little outside Waikiki, but not too far. Authentic Hawaiian food for very little money (well under $10 for more food than you could eat). Also, you may want to hit one of the stalls at the International Market for something other than a hotel restaurant. Before you leave, go to Leonard's Bakery for malasadas. I had never had one before, but the fried Portuguese donut-like things were fantastic.

<Author>ms_obvious
<Content>Loved the view and the location We went to Hawaii for our anniversary. We are two late 30 somethings with double income and no kids. The 3 Marriott resorts we stayed at varied alot. I was glad we stayed at this hotel due to the location. Our check in experience was good. I asked for a king size bed because it was our anniversary and the guy at the front desk said he would rather see us in a room with a great view and two double beds. We took his advice after he showed us the rack rate. The room was on like the 10th floor but it was deceiving because there are like 4 floors of restaurants and a roof top pool on part of the 3rd floor. Our room overlooked the pool and the ocean. It was awesome. The rooms have been refreshed but are typical hotel rooms. I laughed because they had done the ugly tub remodeling to the bath (you could see how it was painted on). It didn't bother me because we love the location and view. The room was clean too. We ate at the Sansei sushi restaurant onsite. It was excellent and the prices weren't too bad for Wakiki. There was a white wine that was a riesling made for sushi and it was awesome. Sorry I can't remember the name of it but you'll see it on the menu. This hotel has all kinds of travellers young, old, families, tourists, etc. It's also a very big hotel but it was easy to go to the beach and they gave you a coupon for free chairs on the beach for 4 hours one day which was nice. My husband took a surf lesson on the beach. It wasn't much of a lesson but it was only $35 a hour and he got up on the board. The place he used is down by the Hyatt food stand on the beach (walk toward the pink hotel, it's before it). I was advised that the Marriott has a surf teacher onsite that is excellent. We didn't find that out until after the fact. I have no clue about the prices. We had a 10pm late flight on our last day and they gave us a key to use lounge to take a shower, etc . Just so you know be sure to take some soap from your room before checking out as the facilities had ran out and they don't have staff there. Also they didn't have wash rags just towels so if you like a wash rag keep one from the room to use here. They only have one shower for the women and no hair dryer. I made a friend in the ladies room who was kind enough to let me blow out my hair with her dryer. I bet you can borrow one from the front desk but I was in the middle of getting ready before discovering this. We spent most of that day at the hotel pool and they have a great mai tai that can be ordered in a fresh pinnapple. It's a $14 drink but it's attractive. We had excellent salads at the pool for lunch but they were expensive for a pool bar at $21 each (shrimp salad  tuna salad). It was very tasty. There is an ABC store onsite. We found the valet was needed and it's pricey at like $25 or something. I think self park was $18 but it felt like too much work for me and I opted for valet. The baggage guys watched our luggage but weren't helpful in bringing it to the car when we were leaving. I think they were fussed that we got in our luggage to get cleaned up and came back later to get it. My husband had tip ready money for these guys but they didn't help so they didn't get a tip. I've never had baggage folks that didn't want to help. Oh, well we did it ourselves and it reminded me of the days went we would stay at the Red Roof Inn. We needed to get to the airport so we weren't going to wait or beg for help. I recommend going to Hula Girl's for breakfast at the Outrigger. It's next to the pink hotel. They have Macadamia and Banana pancakes with coconut syrup. Also they have a great view of the ocean and Diamond Head. The pancake order is huge. Like 3 big ones. My husband and I should of spilt the order. Also the fresh fruit plate is excellent. It had pineapple, strawberry, banana, mango, papaya and a dipping sauce. Excellent coffee and juice too. We are generally diet watchers but this was a special treat.

<Author>Krd
<Content>Hawaii 5-0 at the Marriott A group (10 women celebrating some turning 50) of us stayed at the Marriott Waikiki from 5/20-5/26. After reading the reviews I was concerned about the property, but after staying there I would stay again. My sister and I were on the 22nd floor of the P Tower. Friends were in the K tower and their rooms appeared to be bigger than ours, but for the amount of time we were in the room, space was not an issue. Bathroom (toilet/shower) area was small, but worked for us. A pocket door separated this area from the sink/vanity area. Room was clean and there were plenty of towels. (I am very picky about that). Our view was a little disappointing, we were in 2265 (ocean view), and while we had a view of the ocean, there was a building right in the middle of our view. Location was great, we were close to Diamond Head and the Zoo and the beach was right across the street. We rented beach chairs (2) and an umbrella for $10 per hour/$40 per day. We only rented for an hour since we were not really into lying out on the beach. This hotel is not a bad walk to the International Market and not to bad a haul to the high end stores area (Tiffany). One of the best parts of my trip was the daily breakfast buffet at the hotel (I know I have issues), the food was great (cinnamon rolls were to die for). Service was just okay, had to hunt down our server on several occasions to get silverware/water, but the food more than made up for it. Tried the Sushi place, not an expert on Sushi but the California roll was good and reasonable ($3.25). Pool area was nice, we never had a problem finding a lounger and it appeared to be open all the time. ABC stores are plentiful around the island and there are two in this hotel. If looking for a beach mat, the ABC store near the valet was cheaper than the one near the beach (.99 compared to $1.69). Activities I would recommend. (This was our first time in Hawaii): E NOA Circle Island Tour (Tour #3) - Tour was great; it included Pearl Harbor and all the other major points of interest. Just know that the lunch stop is a company owned lunch truck and several people were not happy they didn鈥檛 get a choice. Maitai- Catamaran Sail- This was the highlight of the trip. We took the sunset sail on Friday (drinks are included). Friday the local boaters race to Diamond Head, so you are out there with all the other boats. Great!!! Also sailed near a school of dolphins, wasn鈥檛 able to get any good shots of them surfacing with my camera in camera mode, but someone recommended taking it in video mode. It was too late for me but may help someone else. Overall- I enjoyed my stay at the Marriott, but IF I go back (9 陆 hour flight), I would try to stay at the Halekulani (which was beautiful).

<Author>tripperATL
<Content>Nice location, great service Just returned from the Marriott Waikiki and overall I really liked the hotel, but thought it lacking in some polish for a hotel that advertises (and charges) as a 鈥淏each Resort and Spa鈥?yet doesn鈥檛 quite always meet those high expectations.CHECK-IN/SERVICE: easy enough, and staff was very friendly and helpful. Especially if you are wanting an upgrade. Seriously they will be happy to sell you an upgrade on the room. Side note: We stayed here redeeming hotel points, and since I was not the redeemer, I cannot complain much. But I do take exception when you have redeemed points for a category 6 hotel, but get basically a category 3 room, and are talked into upgrading to the more expensive room. It is a smaller nit to pick; I just get bugged by all the nickel and dime business, especially when you鈥檝e already paid that much more for a room. That said the service (concierge staff, bellmen and housekeeping) were all very good and helpful, worth the tips.RESORT: lovely, open lobby with waterfalls, tropical flowers. The hotel is divided into two large towers, that even if off the street, most rooms should provide some view. I say off the street, because it is not on the sand; it is at Waikiki Beach, not on it. You must cross the main street, which while not a big deal is worth noting. It is closer to the Diamondhead end of the strip, which offers a nice protected section of beach and smaller crowds. There are two small (not uncommon for the area) but nice pools with nicer deck chairs, a pool bar, a hot tub and cabanas (for a fee), a small but highly promoted spa, a garage ($18/day fee), internet access (for a fee) and a small gym (no charge!). The public areas all were very nice and impressive-the website photographer did an excellent job of making everything seem bigger and better-the halls standard Marriott with brightly colored carpet done in a tropical print. There was an open courtyard with some shops, and several average hotel restaurants. DINING: We only tried a couple places there, just for convenient meals. Most were the standard hotel fare, serviceable and overpriced, such as the Kuhio Grill and Pool Bar for dinner/lunch. My sister liked the cheaper Run sushi place, and we had good luck at the 鈥淚talian鈥?cafe. We did not try any of the nicer restaurants as we were trying more of the local places and usually ate a store-bought breakfast of cereal/muffins/fruit in our room.ROOM: We were on a corner ocean side room on the 15th floor. There is a large picture window and a nice balcony offering SPECTACULAR views of the beach and water, and Diamondhead. There is a small refrigerator in the TV cabinet, and we requested a small microwave as well. The TV was small, and with fewer channels than almost any hotel I鈥檝e visited, but with it being Hawaii and all, I guess they save on the cable knowing that most guests do not spend much time in their rooms. Even being that high, you could hear noise from the street and the pool deck below, so if you are a light sleeper, see if you can go even higher.Our corner 鈥渟uite鈥?was basically a larger room with two queen beds and a sleeper sofa. The beds were comfortable and well-made with nice white linens, but overall the room appearance was lacking. If you look at the pictures posted by others, you will see the older furniture, dated fixtures, which are cheapened by the bright green/yellow accent colors of the curtains and minimalist d茅cor. The bathroom was basically a standard hotel bathroom which is fine for a standard price, but not for the upgrade to 鈥淰iew-Suite-Third person-Resort鈥?price. It also needs an update, as there were scuff marks, and peeling enamel or tile on the tub, and the dimmest vanity light I have ever encountered. They have to think the women will use the desk as their make-up/hair area. Another nit to pick-there was a single light control for the bathroom, so if you turned on the light in the tub/toilet area, the light would also come on in the sink/vanity area bothering people in the night/morning as there was not a door to block the admittedly dim light.I feel like I am being overly harsh as the hotel is very nice and we REALLY enjoyed our stay, but Marriott could/should do a little better to stick with the claim (and price tag) of 鈥淏each Resort and Spa.鈥?br/>

I found the rooms to be more than acceptable. The small fridge in the room was also nice. The beach is right across the street. Would recommend Roberts for shuttle service to and from the airport. Also Reliable Shuttle for a trip to Pearl Harbor instead of the expensive tours. They run every hour and the drivers are great!!Would stay away from Cheese (space) burger in Paradise. Thought this was associated with the Jimmy Buffett Cheeseburger (note no space) in Paradise chain, but learned it is not. The cashier actually left to watch the last few moments of a basketball game, leaving customers standing there for several minutes. Service was poor, and the food was poor. Duke's Canoe Club was also poor. Never saw a waitress until it was time to pay the bill. Would not return. You won't go wrong with a stay at the Waikiki Beach Marriott!

<Author>calpyro
<Content>Great Hotel We stayed for 2 nights after our week in Maui. There were 3 of us total - my husband, myself and our 20 Month old. We arrived at the hotel at about 11 am and were still able to check in to a room, which turned out to be an upgraded executive suite. I have to echo how wonderful the beds were! We were on the 24th floor, so didn't use the balcony at all since they weren't toddler friendly and I was a little freaked out about it.... Spent a lot of time at the beach or hanging out at the pool. Pretty friendly hotel for an active toddler to run around and look at the water fountains... The breakfast buffett at the Kuhio Grill was VERY kid friendly - the staff was great - especially Florence! It is a bit expensive, but we thought it was worth it. Only 2 less than thrilling things, neither of them major issues...1) lots of timeshare stuff everywhere... they were really pushing the Ko'Ona stuff everywhere in the hotel... I never was approached by a sales person, but they had a huge desk outside of our elevators and I quickly learned that they were not the concierge staff! and 2) Our room wasn't serviced - we were out on the middle day from 9 am - 2 pm and came back to let my son have his nap... no one came to clean the room until 3:30, and we thought nap time was more important... I was able to call to get fresh towels brought up and they came very quickly. Nothing to major... I think it was just a bit of a change for us after having been in Maui for a week!Other recommendations - Don't get a car!! We were planning on staying in Waikiki the whole time and didn't use a car at all.. Plus parking was $25 a day... If you are planning on going around the island, there is GREAT public transit everywhere... For those of you with vehicle obssessed toddlers - save your trolley and bus riding until the end of your trip. My son would throw tantrum everytime he saw others getting on to a bus, which is ALL the time in waikiki! THat being said if you can find a resturaunt facing the road - it's great entertainment for them! There are free trolleys to Hilo Hattie and the Ala Moana Shopping Center...

<Author>Fredrock
<Content>Nice place and it's Honolulu People want to complain about the noise on Honolulu/Waikiki area. Sorry but you are in the city. If you want to get away from the touristy Hawaii go to the big island or Kaui. Or just stay at the Trutle Bay Resort on the north shore (where we just came from before checking in at the Marriott for my wife's meeting...see my review on the Turtle Bay Resort). We have stayed in Waikiki many times and this is the first time we stayed at the Marriott. The lobby is very nice. We self parked the car and if their is no space they will valet the car for you for the self park price. Bad thing about this is that they don't know when it fills up so you have to find out for yourself then circle around to the front to tell them. We switched to valet parking on our third day of our stay and we were charged self parking throughout our whole stay. The pools are ok but hey you have Waikiki right across the street. It is right across the beach, I don't know what another poster is talking about when he said it's a block away. Waikiki is a long beach, so maybe he was talking about the center of the beach where it is very crowded. Here is my secret, go in front of the Royal Hawaiian Hotel (pink hotel) near their reef, go out past the reef and just hang out....sooner or later a turtle or two will be swimming next to you. Don't handle them...it's illegal. I always go to this spot and turtles are there all the time. It does get rocky out there so get some water shoes and you can buy at the ABC stores. Waikiki is not that deep you can actually walk about two hundred yards out. That's why no sharks are out there...it's too shallow. But if you wanna see Sharks check out my shark encounter review I did in 2006. Back to the Marriott, we ate at the Kuhio grill for their dinner buffett. If you wanna catch up on your sports, you can head up to the bar up on the second floor near the pool. I still don't get why people order Budweiser when your in Hawaii....try a Mai Tai. The beds are to die for. My daughter didn't want to go in the portable crib they set up for us. She loved the bed. I used to think the Bed at the Palms in Vegas was the best until I slept on these. Yes there are other places to stay in Waikiki Honolulu area just try them all. I rate a 4 and I would stay here again but I would try other places just like trying another other hotes in Vegas. One more thing to add is, if you want to buy souvineirs there are some at Walmart behind Ala Moana mall or get them at the Aloha Bowl swap meet on Wed, Sat and Sun. The prices are must cheaper at these places. Aloha!

<Author>wanderingpuck
<Content>better than expected! We chose the Marriott in Waikiki, for our first visit to Hawaii. We went to celebrate our 25th Anniversary, and I must say, the hotel exceeded my expectations! I'm a Marriott Platinum rewards member, so I've stayed in Marriotts before. This hotel was just beautiful.....modern, clean, with all the ameneties easily accessible for such a sprawling property (contrary to some reviews I'd seen here). We upgraded our partial-ocean view room to a deluxe ocean view (front tower)when we arrived, and my only dissapointment was we were charged for that, in spite of our anniversary and my club member staus. Oh well, was worth the try! We found the view absolutely breathtaking, worth the upgrade. The Lanai looked out on the pool  ocean, and the front bay windows were full ocean. I could just stand there and take it in all day! The concierge was helpful booking activities, though she could have been a bit more informed about details like visitor volume at Pearl Harbor, closure staus at Diamond Head, etc. Just a suggestion, but if you're first timers as we were, check into the activity/ venue on line ahead of time to get a feel for it, don't just rely on the concierge. An example of this was our excursion to the Polynesian Cultural Center, I was really just looking for a great Luau, and ended up spending a long, 12 hour day at the cultural center...very educational, if thats what you want. I suspect had our kids been with us, they'd have been bored. And the Luau was pretty bad. So I'm still searching for the Hawaii beach Luau experience, more reason to return. On the other hand, Haonuma Bay and Pearl Harbor are absolute not-to-be-missed must dos! Finally, all the hotel restaurants (we ate at 4 of them) were first rate and reasonably priced, particulary the breakfast buffet at the grill (served 5-11AM, very convenient!). We had a great time  would return here again!

<Author>Eric_Beylon
<Content>Nice stay A very nice location and a very good hotel as long as one wants to stay at Waikiki (certainly not the best Hawaian experience : crowds everywhere, noise, poor beach, etc.).Valet parking, front desk, breakfast restaurant, room service, room itself : everything was as good as in other Marriott locations. Hotel welcomes a lot of Japanese honeymooners, and large American families. So be prepared to international atmosphere, kids running everywhere and some noise.One complaint about the elevators : there are not enough of them, and they do not seem to be working fast. As a result, you have to wait in line on ground floor when you want to reach your room at 'peak' hours (morning after breakfast and, worst of all, late afternoon when everybody comes back from beach or excursions) ! May be this problem is limited to the tower we were in (the further from the beach)?We tried the Italian restaurant, which was fine but with slow and unefficient service.To sum up, this hotel is perfect if you enjoy big resorts and the busy urban-like atmosphere of Waikiki. If you plan a romantic getaway, fly to less crowded islands or settle at another location.

<Author>MandyS.
<Content>TERRIFIC TROPICAL HONEYMOON We stayed at the Wakiki Beach Mariott for 10 days, on May 23rd-June1st in 2004 for a wonderful Honeymoon. We booked our stay Over the phone directly with the Mariott, there was a little confusion about which tower we would be in at first as they Would not and Could not guarantee a certain one over the phone until we arrived. We were nervous about that because it being our honeymoon, we wanted it to be oceanfront directly! When we arrived, we spoke with a nice man at the desk who was more than happy to make it happen for us though! with an increase in price from 269.00, it ended up being approx. 302.00 a night. It was by far the best vacation we've ever taken and was just wonderful. It was a very peaceful and relaxing stay! Our room was directly facing the ocean in the main beach tower and we could see a magnificent view of the ocean. We had a huge balcony and enjoyed looking at the surfers and clear water daily. The room was beautifully decorated with NEW tropical linens and soft down bedding. We had a very nice sized room, bigger than the standard ones in other towers. It was very wide and had a good sized bathroom. There was plenty of furniture for all of our things and the maids furnished us with more than enough service and towels. This hotel is breathtaking with the atrium, shops and restaurants. The concierge was more than helpful with helping us decide which excursions and trips to take. We went to the beach daily which was kinda crowded, but well worth it. The ocean is clear and has a huge wall that seperates the fish and waves. so that you may float on a float and be wet while sunbathing. ---This was my favorite thing! Only BE--CAREFUL, My float got sucked into one of the crackes in the wall, while I was sunbathing and I went under and got suked by the waves hitting numerous rocks! and lost my float. that was scary but luckily a local grabbed me from the rock pier and saved me. I had panicked because the waves here are horrendous, and I really could have drowned while hubby was on the beach asleep. We had a good laugh about it later and I couldnt have thanked that local enough!!!! Im sure I looked like an idiot. but at least I can worn others not to get too close to that thing! Needless to say I didnt fall asleep anymore on the float, I def. paid more attention.The nightlife is fun, The Locals ARE GREAT! however, some tourists --from other countries werent as nice as the locals and us in the US. <Author>DCbeachgirl
<Content>Don't get your hopes up! My husband and I stay in Marriott's all the time for both work and pleasure and honestly I am in shock that this is a Marriott property. From what I've seen and experienced it gives off the feeling of a cheap budget hotel. When we checked in we pointed out to the registration desk that we had Gold status and qualified for an upgrade. If that was an upgrade then I'm scared to see what we were originally booked in. The rooms are super small and mini balconies. In the title of the hotel they classify themselves as a resort and spa. Well I went to the spa and they informed me that they have no affiliation with the hotel. Not only that - the spa is a joke. The woman's locker room contains a bathroom, shower and some lockers. You won't find any luxuries such as a steam room or sauna but you will pay high luxury spa prices - not exactly sure why. Then there are the concierges who act annoyed that you are asking questions about what to do and where to eat - sorry thought that was their job to tell me about Pearl Harbor or give me a restaurant choice which doesn't serve greasy bar food. Boy was I wrong - do your research before going as I subsequently found out I had to do once I got there. Don't expect a nice gym either. They have the typical run of the mill overly used equipment. I can't comment on the weights since I didn't use them. Bottom line if you're not looking for anything special except a place to sleep - stay at the Waikiki Beach Marriott.

<Content>Decent, but not awesome Stayed here for two nights after being at Ko Olina Beach Club for a week. I will start out by saying that Waikiki is not my favorite part of Oahu, but the Marriott was OK. Location is not ideal, being near the far end of the strip though it does offer views of Diamond Head from some rooms. Furninshings were decent and the mini fridge was a nice convenience. <Author>Mamagigi
<Content>Very good hotel This is my fourth visit to Hawaii and my first stay at the Waikiki Beach Marriott Resort and Spa. I am a Marriott rewards member and have stayed at many Marriott hotels throughout the United States. I traveled with my husband and six year old son and stayed at the hotel for 7 nights. Check-in was fast and easy. The staff of the hotel was great 鈥?always helpful and very pleasant. We requested a partial ocean view room, in a high floor, with a King size bed and a rollaway for my son. There is a small refrigerator in the room where you can store drinks or milk for the kids. The hotel offered a number of amenities, many activities, and indoor parking for $18/day. There is an activity desk at the lobby where you can get information and buy tickets for a number of activities throughout Hawaii (Oahu and other islands). Also available at the lobby is a computer where you can easily confirm your flight and print your boarding pass the day before your trip. If you bring your laptop, high-speed Internet connection is available in the room.The Seattle coffee shop is conveniently located on the first level of the hotel. It became our breakfast routine to have one of their wonderful coffee drinks, juices, breads, muffins, or cakes, every morning. There is an ABC store adjacent to the coffee shop that has most items a traveler with kids may need, including bathing suits, floats, medicine, drinks, snacks, caps, sunscreen, etc., all for a very good price. If you like Italian food, there is a great Italian restaurant right outside the hotel called Arancino Di Mare. It is family friendly and reasonably priced.We were a bit disappointed with the 鈥減artial ocean view鈥? which offered a very limited view of the ocean. However, we did have a nice view of Diamond Head. The high floor was a very good option to avoid the noise from the streets and restaurants around the hotel. The King size bed was very comfortable, but the rollaway we requested for our son was extremely uncomfortable and old. I requested the rollaway to be changed and the hotel promptly exchanged it. Unfortunately, the replacement had the same problem 鈥?you could feel the coils in the mattress while laying on it. The TV and hair dryer were also very old. The TV did not have a video in/output to hook up my son鈥檚 portable DVD. This was a problem for us given that the hotel does not offer a single children鈥檚 channel like Disney, Nickelodeon, Boomerang, etc. When we got back to the hotel after a long day of activities, my son was very tired and wanted to watch a cartoon or children鈥檚 program, but nothing was available. The hair dryer was old and bad. It took a very long time to dry my hair and the end result was poor to say the least.I would certainly recommend this hotel given the amenities it offers, its location, and the service provided. If I were to go back to the same hotel, I would request two double beds (instead of a King and a rollaway) and a room with a newer TV and hair dryer. Aloha!

<Author>blatt1980
<Content>Great place to stay! I thought this place was great. We stayed in the K tower (closer to the beach). I don't understand what people say about the rooms not being upgraded or being old. We asked for and got a city view room with one queen size bed. The room was not huge, but it was nice and what we expected. Everything in the room seemed pretty new and was really nice. The bathroom wasn't huge either, but it had a marble countertop sink, and the floor and shower all had marble tile. The only thing I didn't like about the room was the door on the bathroom was one that slid shut, not a regular door. The lanai wasn't huge, but it was big enough for me and my husband to sit out on and be comfortable. The lobby area and the area between the two towers was very nice, lots of flowers. All of it seemed really new. I just don't understand the complaints of this hotel at all. All of the wood furniture in the room was very nice and not old at all. I only saw one pool, and yes, it was small. But for us, we didn't book the hotel for the pool, and we didn't even use it. We saw mostly younger kids using it. Walking by other pools on the beach, none of them seemed huge, so I don't think big pools are something hotels worry about in Waikiki. Also the elevators were fine. Sometimes there was a longer wait than other times, but I didn't find that it was excessive or aninconvience at all. Also I read on here about thin walls and hearing a lot of noise. Us having a city view on the 9th floor, I did hear some street noise. If a fire engine went by or a really loud truck, we could hear that. Regular street noise (regular cars, buses, people) we could not hear with the door shut. Also, we could hear other toilets flush, but we could not hear people talking, or making any other noise, we could also hear the people around us close and open their lanai door. I will say that some of the people at the front desk are not very friendly. One lady just seemed like she wanted to get rid of us. But we did talk to one guy that was very helpful, so they are just hit and miss. The concierge was very helpful and they are very friendly, so don't hesitate to ask them even the littlest question, they were always very nice to us. So in all I would say that this is a wonderful place to say. Very resort like, very comfortable. This is a long review, but I wanted to give my honest opinion and talk about the issues I had read on here. We didn't rent a car (really wasn't necessary) so we didn't have to worry about parking. But I noticed on Friday night the parking lot was all full and people were having problems finding a spot (our room overlooked part of the parking garage). It looked like the parking garage was pretty tight too, but we drove in another hotels' parking garage, and that was tight, so it seems like it might be a Waikiki thing. And the bed was the best, but I figured from all the other reviews that that goes without saying!

<Author>Bessert1
<Content>Decent Waikiki Hotel Our stay at the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort was my first stay in Waikiki, but my wife's second. We had read up on all the lodging choices both in our Oahu Revealed guidebook by Andrew Doughty (reccommended!) and here on TripAdvisor and were prepared for high prices and tired-looking rooms. We decided to try this property both based on the reviews here and because we've had good experiences at other Marriott locations.This hotel was, in comparison to our expectations and my wife's previous Waikiki stay, a bit better than we expected. There were several postive aspects and a few negatives, but overall we would choose this location again when staying in Waikiki.Most of the positives have already been mentioned, so I'll just sum up: very comfortable beds, nicely-appointed rooms, nice ocean views, plentiful bathroom amenities, very good location, great housekeeping, an ABC store right in the hotel, decently-sized lanai with two chairs and a small table, etc. We had a one king room in the K Tower on the 9th floor and a partial-ocean view (although it was a very nice view). The hotel staff we encountered were always nice and friendly.The two main negatives (although you ARE in Hawaii, so things like these should bug you less) were the parking situation and the elevators. While some come to Waikiki to lay out on the beach the whole time, my wife and I like to experience the area. So we did rent a car during our stay and paid the $18/night for parking. I can understand the price, but almost every day the structure was full because the hotel allows restaurant patrons and others to also use the structure. When full, the hotel directs you to either use the valet parking service or some other offsite parking location. If you don't plan on renting a car, this would be a moot point. The other negative was the elevators in the K Tower, which sometimes took forever to arrive. We were on the 9th floor (a little to far to hoof it on the stairs... with an 8-month old child in a stroller) and we could hear elevators by the dozens flying by while we sometimes waited 5-8 minutes for one to stop for us.In all, though, we felt that for the price, we did get a reasonable value and what negatives we did find were offset by the fact that we were in Hawaii in February. We're already thinking of returning in the next couple years and the Waikiki Beach Marriott will be on our short list next time as well.

<Content>Waikiki Beach Marriott Hotel and Spa - It's all about the view! Booked 6 nights using Marriott Reward Points for March 1-8, 2007. Arrived at the hotel for check in and found our points certificate had not arrived. Front Desk agent seemed a bit rushed and not the most welcoming. Our assigned room was not what we had requested, with a queen bed instead of the king. Also, the view was of the parking garage top floor. After a 10 hour trip we were told check back the next day for alternate rooms. The following morning my wonderful husband arranged to pay extra for a full ocean view room. What a difference $120 extra per night makes! Absolutely stunning view from room 1923. The room itself was clean and spacious. The bathroom was very small. There was considerable noise in the corridors and also between rooms. We could hear the guests in the room next door talking till quite late. The pool area is fairly small for a hotel this big. The area around the hotel was lovely and the City of Honolulu does a wonderful job of keeping Waikiki Beach clean and picture perfect. Nice restaurants, not overly expensive and if you are in need of anything from wine to bandaids there is an ABC convenience store on every corner and in all the large hotels. We rented a car for two days and drove the island. It was well worth the cost. The North Shore is spectacular. Driving is easy and the roads pretty well marked. We thought the people of Hawaii were genuinely friendly and helpful. Can't wait to go back. Next time a different island, probably Kaui'i.

<Author>ESS_lover
<Content>Very close to the beach We booked a last-minute trip to Honolulu and ended up staying at this hotel for 5 nights. The hotel is very nice and Waikiki Beach is literally across the street. We had paid for a garden-view room, but when we got there they had automatically upgraded us to an ocean-view room which was very nice. The staff were very polite and accomodating.We did a package deal with the hotel that included free buffet breakfast every morning. I thought the buffet breakfast was okay (the scrambled eggs were gross) and my husband liked the custom omelette station. There is a pool with a bar near it on the third floor (the Moana Terrace) with a view of the beach below - the view is nice, but the drinks there are pretty crummy and expensive. I only mention it because it's a nice place to sip a drink and watch the sun go down. Parking at the hotel is expensive (as it is with other hotels in this area). We paid $25 a day for valet parking. It's cheaper if you self-park, but harder to do in their small parking garage. Unless you plan on driving all over the island, pass on getting a rental car. We found that most of the things we wanted to do we could get there by walking or by taking a shuttle bus. A lot of the tour companies picked us up at our hotel, so we really only used our rental car for driving around the island one day and getting to and from the airport.

<Author>YTC
<Content>Great beds! We stayed at the Marriott Waikiki Feb 14-17, 2007. Because I had read reviews about noise at this hotel, I e mailed them to request a quiet room on a higher floor. They responded quickly and promised to honor my request. We were completely satisfied. The beds were really comfortable. The room was decorated nicely. We had a full view of Diamond Head out our sliding doors and a partial view of the ocean. The air conditioner on the roof of the building across the street that another Trip Advisor contributor complained about was below our balcony. We could hear it, but we felt it served to muffle the sounds of traffic that one can not escape in most Waikiki hotel rooms. We have stayed at many hotels in Waikiki (all the Sheratons, Hilton, Outriggers, Embassy Suites, etc). Waikiki is a busy place; it is somewhat unreasonable to expect a room in the middle of a busy city to be quiet. We found the Marriott to be as good or better than other hotels. We would definitely stay there again.

<Author>sawdust444
<Content>great place Stayed 5 nights through Pleasant holidays which included partial ocean view upgrade and 2 breakfast buffets each morning. We were in the rear tower which made it tough to see the ocean without hanging over the railing but we weren't in the room enough for this to matter. The breakfast has many items and was delicious but I dont usually gorge myself in the morning so wouldn't pay 20 bucks or so for it. Drink service around the pools was nonexistent for us . I went up to the bar and the bartender would only give me one drink at a time so had to deliver wifes then go back and sign again for mine. Do not stay on back side of front tower that is where air conditioner and parking lot is. The temp in our room was perfect day and night I dont even know if the air was on or not, never heard anything. Our departure was at midnight and we cou;ld access our luggage to change but were not informed of a hospitality room. We arrived late also, 11:30pm by the time we got situated, Tiki bar next door saved the day for food and drinks. After a hike to top of Diamond Head we stopped in to LuLu's on the corner. We ordered lunch and 2 beers. Lunch arrived before the waitress could walk 20 feet for the beers. ( the place was almost empty) She then informed us one of the beers we ordered was all out. We finished lunch before she could return with a replacement. Way to hang loose baby! Our room was very quiet, never knew we had neighbors. Elevator service was fine although sometimes funky. Once while descending just as we got to the first floor the elevator suddenly shot upwards and got to the 25th floor before we could stop it. I believe disneyland has a similiar ride. The staff and housekeeping were very friendly, I borrowed the maids vacuum cleaner to suck the air out of my space bags! No need for a car although one should rent one for a day and go to the north shore. I wouldn't hesitate to stay here again, good place and location

<Content>Pretty Good experience, BUT!!! MY wife and I stayed at the Marriot for three nights after an 11 night Hawaiian cruise.Overall, the stay was excellent. The room was large and had a kingsize bed that was the best bed we had ever slept in. Trucks, buses, cars, loud music and incessant beeping noise from trucks and buses backing up were the constant irritation nightly. As stated previously, we werepleased overall and understand that being in central Waikiki was a big plus and overall were quite pleased with our Marriot stay.

<Author>trustyrusty
<Content>Not bad...for Waikiki This isn't a bad hotel. It has many rooms with amazing views of Diamond Head and Waikiki beach. The main problem with the hotel is that it is Waikiki. This is a gross little part of Hawaii that most locals would like to see fall off into the ocean. <Author>Jaquesspratt
<Content>First Class Experience All The Way We stayed 4 nights at the Marriott Christmas week, after a planned move from the Sheraton Waikiki. Although we arrived quite early in the AM, we were offered for immediate occupancy, an inexpensive, major upgrade to our booked room. It seems one has to take their web description of 'ocean front' with a grain of salt. An older property, the Marriott oozes class. Liberal use of wood and rich colors, along with maximum use of space open to the outside, sets the tone. The staff was friendly at all levels. Our room featured the new ultra Marriott beds, which some will find too soft. The pools are on a third floor open space and apart from a surfeit of ankle biters, were great. The floor also hosts two superb restaurants - Sansei contemporary Japanese, and B.K. Steakhouse and Seafood, by the same owners. These are highly rated by Zagat and others, and can't be faulted. A third restaurant, Arancino,on the first floor, offers excellent Italian food, despite very ordinary ambiance. The same can't be said for the hotel's own major first floor restaurant, the Kuhio Grill, featuring smorgasboard dining, where we had the worst Christmas dinner I can recall. The Marriott is located at the extreme East end of Waikiki, close to the Zoo. The area is replete with local color, which ads to the experience.A top pick for a longer stay and for those who appreciate a more relaxed environment.

<Author>blenderbringer
<Content>Marriott is convenient The Waikiki Marriott is a great location. You walk out to the beach where you can see entertainment, learn to surf, swim, eat, drink, you name it. The hotel rooms are clean, but not modern. We stay in the newer tower, but the rooms still have popcorn ceilings and old style window treatments. If you are looking for a plasma TV and streamlined design, this is not your place. We have stayed in four different suites over the years, one of which was featured in their hard-cover book in the room. We have had views of Diamond Head and Waikiki beach. The beds are amazingly comfortable, with a featherbed, down comforter and plenty of pillows. The rest of the room is pretty average. They have two pools which are basic. They are both rectangles, no fancy fountains, swim up bars or kids stuff. They are large enough that you could get a little exercise. One is next to the restaurant and bar. You can be served in your lounge chair. They have massage available. They added a hot tub this year. The staff commitment varies. Some people are very helpful and personable... but not all. We always enjoy our stay, but we are not that picky.

Did not hear our neighbours at all and apparently the hotel was quite full while we were there. The only complaint was the plumbing wasn't the quietest. We could here a toilet flushing and ours seemed a little loud.The location of the hotel was perfect for us. Isn't wasn't in the busisest section of Waikiki Beach which was only a few minutes walk from the hotel. We also enjoyed watching the movies on the beach on our balcony. On Saturday and Sunday nights they have Sunset on the Beach where a 30 foot plus screen is set up on the beach and movies are played. We found all the hotel staff to be very friendly and helpful. We would not hesitate to go back to this hotel.While there we rented an SUV and took TheBus. We drove around the North and East coasts and found some beautiful remote beaches. Snorkling at Hanauma Bay was great. The bus trip to Pearl Harbor was a breeze. We got on at the bus at the hotel and it went all the way to Pearl Harbour (#42).

<Author>LuvTheGardenIsle
<Content>Fun and relaxing place to stay My husband and I stayed here on August 24, 2006 for one night between our arrival in Honolulu and our departure the next morning to Kauai. We LOVED this hotel! It was the perfect blend of city excitement with Hawaiian relaxation. The hotel lobby immediately made us feel relaxed when we arrived, because of the beautiful plants and water feature in the lobby. Check in was efficient and helpful, and they gave us a free upgrade to an ocean view with balcony! It was soooo nice to be treated so well, especially after the grueling 10-and-a-half-hour plane ride. We could feel ourselves decompressing already! The room was very nice, although the drapes needed cleaning. Other than the drapes, everything was clean. And the bed was amazing!! So comfortable. Lots of other people have commented on the beds already, so I won't say any more except that we slept very well. The hotel was very conveniently located in Waikiki and was right across the street from the ocean. We were only there one night, but we did go for dinner at the hotel's Japanese restaurant. I can't remember the name of the restaurant. But it was excellent sushi, particularly the octopus, which was very tender. The waitstaff even made chilled green tea with honey for us when we asked, even though it wasn't on the menu! Needless to say, we were very impressed. We highly recommend the Japanese restaurant -- it is Zagat rated, I believe, and has been featured in several publications. After dinner, we walked around outside by the ocean. It was a bustling Thursday night, and people were out and about, walking by the ocean, taking photos, shopping, etc. We walked to the nearby Coldstone Creamery, got ice cream, and took it back to the hotel and ate it while sitting out on our balcony and enjoying the city lights and views. Checkout the next morning was smooth and efficient. We were sad to only be there one night! It was a very nice hotel, we had a great experience there, and we will definitely stay there again on future trips to Hawaii.

<Author>meleana
<Content>Paradise Abounds We stayed at the Waikiki Beach Marriott for five days before going to stay at our timeshare in Kauai. Check in was quick, easy, and without any problems. Because we had so much luggage, we had help in bringing our bags to our room. The gentleman was VERY knowledgeable about the area and was quick to find out from our kids what their interests were. He then recommended activities that we could do easily and told us how to go about scheduling those. In addition, we mentioned that we needed more towels, and before we could count to ten, he was back with an armful of them!We had connecting rooms. Each room had two queen sized beds and a separate bathroom area. There was enough room left to move around the room easily. The view of Waikiki Beach and Diamond Head was breathtaking! What a way to wake up each morning!The pool was relaxing. At night the kids enjoyed eating at the grill located by the grill so they could go back and forth to the pool. My husband and I enjoyed watching them, and looking out over the beach as it is located on the third floor. They also had a man serending the diners which made it seem more like a dream!On the lobby level, there are many shops to walk through. In addition, there is a relaxing sitting area by the check in desk. You can sit here and listen to the Hawaiian music while you enjoy a cup of coffee. This hotel is located at the far end of Waikiki Beach so it is a little bit less congested than further up the street. You cross the street to get to the beach. The water is calm as there is a breaker wall. However if you pass the dock, and go to that section of the beach, you can enjoy the waves. In addition, the zoo is within walking distance.The restaurants on site offer a wide variety of dining options. Our entire family enjoyed the buffet that was offered in the main dining area at night, and again for breakfast.The only problem we encountered was parking. The spots were tight and we had to drive around a lot to find a spot to fit our minivan. Hold on to your childrens' hands because cars go around the bends quickly.All in all this is a wonderful hotel for couples, or for families. I would - without a doubt - stay here again, if we get the wonderful opportunity of going back to Honolulu!

<Author>Kansasman
<Content>Relaxing Stay at the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort We stayed for ten nights beginning July 18. This was our third trip to the islands and first time back to Oahu in several years. We wanted the nightlife, restaurants and bigger city amenities of Honolulu this time and the Marriott Waikiki was a great location for that purpose. We also chose this hotel because of the Marriott Rewards points. Check in was quick, efficient and friendly. Lucked out and there was no line at our late afternoon arrival. We had booked a corner deluxe ocean view in advance. Oversized room with sitting area on the front corners of the K Tower. Room 2133. Spectacular views of Waikiki from both sides. Splurge and book it if you care about the view. Room amenities and maid service was excellent during our stay. Refrigerator in room which is a nice touch. Marriott has upgraded this hotel, or at least this room, to their new Revive linen collection. Very nice. All beds have the Marriott pillow top mattress and lots of pillows. If you don't like the soft pillow top, I am sure they will adjust bedding for you on request at any full service Marriott. Beach is right across Kalakaua Ave. from the hotel. This hotel is at the Diamond Head end of Waikiki. Two ABC stores, Hertz, travel agents, and several other boutiques on premises. All staff we interacted with were friendly, and welcoming. Used the concierge twice and were very pleased with their service. The pools are small, but recommend renting one of the cabanas pool side if you want a day away from the sand and sun of Waikiki. Attentive pool side service is available for food and drink. The hotel restaurants were expensive, but what isn't in Hawaii? Within easy walking distance or short drive to countless other fabulous restaurants in all price ranges. We did not have a bad meal at any of the Marriott on site eateries.We did the luau at The Royal Hawaiian Hotel this time just for fun. Recommend it highly. Book it early. Fabulous food, limited seating, so it fills up quick. Check out was also easy and efficient. The valet staff pre-arranged our cab pick up back to the airport ahead of time. Very easy. We will certainly consider the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort during our next visit to Honolulu.  
<Date>Aug 1, 2006

<Content>Marriott Waikiki Excellent Location This was my second visit to the Marriott Waikiki. A group of us visted from July 15-18th. The Marriott is in the heart of Waikiki. Close to shopping, directly across the street from the world famous Waikiki beach, close to Diamond Head, the International Market and many other attractions. I agree with the other reviewer having the ABC Store in the Hotel was very convenient (they sell everything). The buffet breakfast outstanding! They offer a prime rib and crab leg buffet on weekends (great value) and delicious. We thoroughly enjoyed the Honolulu Cookie Company shop in the hotel (great gift ideas). We had two rooms one of which was a family style room which accomodated 4 adults with separate beds. The room was very large and comfortable. The bedding seem to have been upgraded since my last visit in 2003 (VERY COMFORTABLE). The concierge can arrange any type tour or activity that you'd like. I highly recommend the Pearl Harbor/Grand Island Circle Tour (the tour includes the North Shore a must see). I highly recommend visiting Oahu and at least 2 of the other islands. Our trip consisted of: 3days- Oahu, 2-Big Island and 3-Maui. If you can plan a total of 10 days split time on the Islands that will give you a diverse taste of Hawaii.Hawaii is one of the most beauitiful places I've visited. Enjoy!

<Author>mamieb
<Content>Good deal at the Marriott in Honolulu After a very disappointing cruise on the new NCL Flagship the Pride of Hawaii, we took a three day lay over on Oahu and stayed at the Marriott Waikiki Beach Hotel. The Hotel is across the street from the beach, and many of the rooms look out on city buildings, but the rooms were very clean, linens were excellent and the mattress and pillows extremely comfortable. They have a buffet that offers a discount for early bird dining which was very good. The hotel is on the main strip on Waikiki Beach and is an easy walk to many nice shops and good restaurants.The only down side is that Marriott does not give Freguent Reward points for any of the concessions inside the hotel such as Seattles Best Coffee or the DK Steak House. Only Marriott owned services apply for the reward points. You may want to get a list of these when you arrive as we were confused which services applied and which ones didn't.Overall, it was a nice hotel, very comfortable and worth the price.

Never knew the show hawaii 5-0 meant that hawaii became our 50th state, thus the name! Expedia offerd us a pick up and delivery from the airport to our hotel with a welcome lei for both of us at a reasonalble price(lei's used to be free but that is not the case anymore) , don't do it! we had a long wait outside the van, and we were pretty tired having flown ove 12 hours!.The drivers were waiting for other passengers and releif drivers to show, although there were 3 greeters.We eventually started towards our hotel still very excited about actually being in hawaii, when the driver took us through the the part of town we can only asssume to be the industrial part of Honolulu, that was kind of depressed and all we could think waswhat a dump About 20 minuits later the scenery changed into a thing of beauty and we did feel like we had arrived in paradise!. Our accomodations were fantastic, the hotel reflected the old world charm and beauty that is experienced only in this part of the world, yet ultra modern.The decor in the lobby was breathtaking, from the music to the lava rock water fall that spouted every half hour or so, to the rows of orchids lining about 40 feet of the lobby on one side, as well as the wooden patio furniture and tiki palm umbrellas. But the best was our bedding! The finest down pillows and mattress covers of down, we floated into or dreams and hated to get out of bed! We did all the tourist things being clueless, went to the free breakfast orientation, listened to a local tell us all about the tours we could book, and we did book a weeks worth of activities, from the Arizona, which is a must see, the watery graveyard of our heroic man, threw flowers said a prayer and cried. I was moved and didn't even want to go! To the Polynesian culteral center, had an authentic luau and learned about the many different islands.What we didn't know was the pass to the PCC was good for return for 2 more days, as we opted to not rent a car we didn't get to go back.We took the 150 mile bus tour around the north shore, saw the Dole plantation(you must go inside the main house and buy a pineapple whip! It;s a combination of soft custerd ice cream and soft ices mmmm so refreshing and not too sweet.The trolley cars are free and take you to specific destinations, such as Hilo Hatties best place on the island to get anything as well as the A.B.C. stores. A must is lulus for breakfast or whatever. you are never rushed and the view of the beach is worth a million! They serve the best pancakes in the world, and evey meal has an orchid placed on the plate along with a twist of orange slice. Have the guava juice! You will never experince anything so fresh, anywhere! (ask the concierge, or any 1 working in the area where lulus is, its a local favorite, as is Dukes great steaks, good prices. Go to the beach,waikiki beach is 5 different shades of tourquoise, and safe and warm.You can rent beach chairs and umbrellas for about $20.00 a day. Our 1 regret was not having brought our cam corder, although we did take over 500 pictures on our digital camera. I would have loved to have recorded the music at the PPC.We can't wait to go back, the whole experince was great, from the funny and knowledgeable tour bus drivers, to the people we met on our tours! Aloha, and Mahalo for allowing us to share our trip to hawaii! And 1 more thing, all are welcomed home because the Hawaiian people consider all of us family! Thus the expression, Aloha Cousin! If the world had that attitude towards each other, there would be no wars.  
<Date>Jun 30, 2006

We would definitely go back to this hotel.

<Author>ms.go-go
<Content>daughter's 20th birthday present My daughter and I stayed here for her 20th birthday. We had stayed a week on the big island and then came here for 4 days. We loved the hotel. Again it is at the end of the strip and right by the ocean and beach. Our room was clean and beautiful with the most gorgeous view of the water and of the mountains. We requested the front building as I got this tip from this site. We watched the surfers every day from the balcony. We had no problem with the elevators. We did eat one night at the pool restaurant which had the best fish tacos. There was live music and to sit outside on a Spring night was wonderful. We watched the people on the street and the palms swaying in the breeze by the ocean. We walked everyday in the park nearby and we were even fortunate enough to have a craft fair that week-end. We walked to the Aquarium only 5 minutes away and the view of Diamond head is great on the walk . One thing I did get miffed about was when I checked in I told the front desk clerk that I had an 11 pm flight out and I was asking about a late check out or 1/2 day rental as I did not know what to do till 11pm. She did not help at all  the the cost of 1/2 day was too much and not much time. So I solved the problem by taking a full day tour of the island with my daughter that started at 8 am and ended at 6pm. ( It was a great tour) When the bell man came to store our bags I casually mentioned the I had a late flight and he said no problem that the Marriott had a courtesy room with showers and a tv and to just keep my room key and I could come back after the tour and get fresh clothes from our luggage and take a shower and then off to the airport. This really helped us out . But I can't believe that the front desk did not offer this solution! needless to say he got a big tip! And here is another tip. The airport is super crowded with late flights and you have to go through an agriculture security and regular security so do plan to leave extra early!We loved eating at the Tiki restaurant and saw the most beautiful sunsets there. We ate there 3 x. The food was just great and it was so close , just on the corner above Wolfgangs. It was so good . Try the bread pudding served in a coconut shell and you will just love it! The wait staff is so nice. This was a great hotel in a great location with beautiful rooms and great views.

<Author>bitbytravelbug
<Content>Enjoyed my stay; beach info My husband was here on business, and I joined him for 5 days from March 10 -15. What people have said about the beds is true- they have pillowtop mattresses and are incredibly comfortable. We were in the front tower with a nice view of the ocean from our balcony. Additionally, the Resort Quest across the street has live entertainment starting at 7:30 in the morning, and again starting around 6:00 in the evening; you can sit out on your balcony and enjoy the music for free. Being here on business, my husband appreciated the nice desk and internet access. My only complaint was that housekeeping would come somewhere between 11:00- 12:30, and on 2 occasions, I came back from the beach and had to wait about 20 min to get into my room.NOW ABOUT THE BEACH... the beach right across from the hotel has a breaker, and is very shallow with no waves. If you go to the right, you end up on a very narrow, very croweded stretch of Waikiki Beach. But, if you go to the left of the pier, you will be on a wonderful, much wider, much less crowded beach with nice waves and very reasonable snorkel and boogie board rentals. They also show free movies here under the stars on Saturday nights.The WAIKIKI ZOO is a half block away in Kapiolani Park, and the AQUARIUM is a few blocks farther.

<Author>CVUK
<Content>Ask for the K Tower!! We stayed at this hotel at the end of April 2006 and on the whole were really impressed with the service.Good points:* We stayed in the K tower (do ask, they were very happy to accede to our request and its nearer the beach) and the room was really large, with 2 double beds which were amazingly comfortable. We had also been upgraded at no extra cost to a room with an ocean view which was stunning.* Very friendly service - from front desk, to bar and restaurant staff.* The pool is quite big by waikiki standards and there are plenty of sunloungers. The sun deck does get sun all day, contrary to other postings, although the pool is shaded until around lunchtime.* The concierge we found very helpful, in terms of organising cabs and excursions. (We thoroughly enjoyed the E-Noa tour we took of the whole island - an absolute must to get out of Waikiki and see more of the real Hawaii)* The hotel has plenty of useful amenities - such as an ABC store, selling essential food and drinks and tourist stuff, several swimwear shops, shops selling local produce, a spa (book early!) and a gym.* The room we stayed in had a great mini-fridge which we used to store drinks in to save money, as we found Hawaii quite an expensive place.* The poolside bar is open in the evenings and is a nice place to sit - it is lit with flaming torches and there is live music.* The location is great - at the quieter end of Waikiki, but the walk up the strip is very pleasant. The Ala Moana Shopping Trolley stops right outside the hotel as well.* Room service is pretty tasty!Bad points:* Breakfast is not amazing and is relatively expensive. The buffet is fairly repetitive for breakfast. We tried to Italian restaurant for dinner which was also a bit sub-standard.* The decor is the rooms is a bit dated, although the rooms themselves are very clean.*Lifts are occasionally slow at busy times - waiting 2 or 3 mins at most.The only other point to note is be careful who you use for cabs when you order them through the concierge. You can get cheaper cabs through the Island Express but we had a very bad experience with them on one of the days and would not recommend their services. However, when we raised it with the manager, he offered us his apologies and gave us complimentary drinks which was a nice, and completely unexpected, touch.
