<Author>five0
<Content>Marriott Waikiki a Great Choice!!! Having traveled quite a bit recently, I was anxious to see if the Waikiki Marriott would live up to my expectations or, as so many other hotels have in the past, left me wondering where all the good stuff in the brochure went off to!I can confidently say that I definitely got what I paid for at the Marriott. Check-in was smooth, only a short line and no problems with the staff. I had sent an email about a week before we arrived asking for a room in the K tower with a king bed, and our requests were honored. We were on the 24th (of 25) floor with a partial ocean view: Diamond Head straight ahead, beach and ocean to the right. My only complaint was that I had also requested champagne and fruit in the room upon our arrival, but it came about two hours AFTER we had checked in. No big deal though, given that we checked in a bit early anyhow.The room itself was everything I had heard about and more. The linens and mattress are superb, and always more than enough towels/pillows/etc. The view was as promised, and the morning sunrise was an unexpected bonus that we just loved. Plenty of space to stash our stuff and the quickly accumulating souvenirs throughout the week. Shower was a bit dark (the liner is completely opaque and it can get a little scary in there if you're shaving with no light at all!) but absolutely spotless. No signs of mold or creepy-crawlers.Another unexpected touch was that we could tell the housekeeper had VACCUUMED the carpet each day. Totally not necessary, but kind of nice to know it's being done. The few mornings I ordered coffee I was aghast at the prices (One full pot of coffee and two muffins ends up being $21.50 US after taxes and gratuity!) but service was incredibly prompt and the food certainly was tasty. (Try the pineapple muffins)We didn't use the pool although we sat by it on our last day. Every day before we headed out we grabbed two or more towels at the stand there, and sometimes they took our room number and sometimes they didn't. They certainly have no way of tracking whether you return your towels or not, because it's simply a bin you dump them in as you head inside for the evening. I guess the formality of asking for a room number is exactly that: a formality and nothing more. Some nights we just left our beach towels in the room for the housekeeper. Wasn't a problem.PARKING really sucked. To be blunt. I valeted a car three of our seven days, yet I was charged for 5. (at $19/day, it was a real pain) The reason being is I was foolish enough to alert them upon check-in that we would be GETTING a car, but I didn't specify that it wasnt for another two days!! So if you're planning on using their parking facilities, please check your bill and make disputes accordingly. There's no excuse for that. Although I will say it was nice that the valet parking is right across the street-- once my girlfriend forgot her shoes in the car and getting them was a snap, not a laborious process as has happened in the past.The restaurants all look fantastic, but we only ate at the Kuhio Beach Grill for breakfast. I am a sucker for buffets, and this one was of good quality. The Easter Champagne Brunch even featured crab legs and prime rib, which I wasn't quite expecting at 11AM. Good though!Overall, we were very pleased with our stay at the Marriott and I won't hesitate to stay at another one of their facilities. I would, however, like to check out the Sheraton Moana Surfrider the next time I am in Waikiki. It looked like the only hotel in town that might be able to beat the Marriott's quality dollar-for-dollar.  
<Date>Apr 30, 2006

<Author>Andreita
<Content>Great stay!!! My boyfriend and i decided to go to Hawaii at the very last minute when our hotel was ruined during the hurricane that hit Cancun. We had a lot of trouble trying to find available hotels as it was such a last minute thing but we luckily found this one. We were a little unsure as we had seen many reviews that were not that good . I was finally convinced and booked a Deluxe Ocean View room . On arrival , we could not have asked for anything more . The staff were so friendly to us and helpful that all my worries about the hotel were going away . There was only one more step to go...the hotel room . Our room was located on the 24 floor from what i remember , it was the highest balcony room there. The view was spectacular and the room itself was very very spacious and clean. The only thing , there were a few dirty stains on the curtains but that was nothing when i had a view like this one. The sunset from our balcony was something else ... it was so romantic, beautiful and breath taking all in one. The pool is very small but you spend so much time at the beach that you dont really have time for the pool. We did however eat at the bar which was very nice , the band that was playing was so good . At the time , there was a large Japanese tourist group and a few sports groups staying at the hotel so going up at down the lift was a long wait . There was about 5 lifts but it still managed to take a long time. The hotel is located across the road from the beach so that was perfect also . Very central to alot of stores so alot of shopping was done. It was about a 5 minute walk to all the fancy stores like Prada , Chanel , Gucci....There is also a tram a little further down from the hotel that takes you down to the Shopping Mall.I strongly recommend this hotel as it had such a casual feel that made us very comfortable. If you are however looking for something fancy and elegant i would suggest staying at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider. We stayed at both hotels but we will stick with the Marriott for next time we liked the friendly casual feel about it .

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lovely! My fiance and I stayed at the Marriott Waikiki in January. It was absolutely wonderful! The rooms were newly renovated and oh so CLEAN! The beds were SO comfortable. It has been 3 months and I still picture all of the beautiful orchids in the lobby area. The location is excellent. We did not rent a car, but instead walked or took the bus everywhere we went to. Near by (walking) attractions included the International Market Place, the Honolulu Zoo, and the Waikiki Aquirium, and a cheap/short bus ride and a long hike got you to Diamond Head. I would highly recommend the Marriott to any traveler. It was worth every penny!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location This hotel is a great choice if you are looking for a really good hotel room in the best beach front location. If you want to be in the middle of the city shopping areas and noise then choose to stay farther down the strip. But, if you are pretty mobile then everything is in walking distance anyway. I found that the rooms were kept very clean by the hotel staff. The bed was wonderful, and the balcony had a wonderful view. The front tower was worth asking for since if you are in and out of the hotel a lot, then you dont have to carry all your stuff so far. But, the back tower wasn't so much farther that it would ruin the hotel experience. I wished that there was free in room wireless internet access. It was available but did cost about $15 a day. It looked like the Seattle's Best Coffee shop in the hotel provided access if you were a customer of theirs. Sensei's Sushi had amazing rolls, some of the best that I have had. And if you can wait until after 10pm on Friday nights they were half off. Dont use VIP Car Rentals!!! I wasted a morning trying to save some money by using a local agency, but they qouted one price over the phone and when I got there they increased the price. Then they tried to nickle and dime me to increase the price of the rental that I wanted. Shaddy business!!! I went with Hertz right in the hotel lobby and got a really nice car for just a little bit more money, with great service. I should have used them in the first place.

<Author>knitsafghans
<Content>Good hotel; our second time - and would stay again. Stayed here for 4 nights in March with my husband and two boys, 13 and 16. This is our second time at the Marriott. Last time we were in the front tower, back corner, probably about 12th floor in a large family room on a $115 Priceline rate. This time we paid $195 Marriott Rewards for the first night then 3 nights free redeeming a Marriott Rewards Award. We stayed in the rear tower, but on the 32nd floor. View was very nice, a bit dizzying. One negative: the air conditioning unit at the next door hotel (Aston?) was VERY noisy and made sitting on the balcony a not-so-great experience. I hope they fix this noisy unit (it looks old, rusty and is spewing water).The room was fine; standard Marriott in good shape. The bed is a fluffy pillowtop type and can be interesting in that it has aspects of a waterbed when someone sits/lies next to you.Elevators weren't a major problem in terms of waiting, but we did have an issue where the car would stick unless you physically pulled the doors shut together. We reported it to the hotel who seemed to address it.Pools are so-so. Small, rooftop.You are very close to the beach, though. Our soon took surfing lessons at the nearby Hans Hedemann surfing school.This is also currently the nicer end of Waikiki. You are near both beach and a large park. We used to stay down near the Hilton Hawaiian Village, but I much prefer this side now.The only hotel restaurant we tried this time was the Pizza/Italian place. It was fine with crisp crust pizzas. Lots and lots of restaurants in the area tho. I would NOT stick to the hotel.Front desk staff was much grumpier than I remembered. No smiles on check-in or out, atypical for Hawaii. This was not the case last time we stayed, so perhaps something was going on.All in all, a good experience and we would certainly return, assuming the rates were good.

<Author>Relax4Life
<Content>Great Option for Business or Pleasure Stayed here during the week when I was in Oahu on business. Here are some thoughts:Positives: - Alot of rooms have ocean views. The K tower is closer to the water and has better views, but more expensive. If you do stay in the P tower, try and stay towards the top because you will be able to see right over the K tower into the gorgeous ocean. I stayed in the P tower on the 30th floor with a corner room and it was AMAZING!!! Especially because it had 2 balconies and I could hear the ocean at night.- Wireless internet! Awesome because it works in the room and in the lobby and near the pool. You can probably get on another service in Waikiki for cheaper than the $13 Marriott fee, but not sure about security.- Location can't be beat. It is right across from the water and awesome if you like to take early morning walks along the water (what I did). Shopping and restaurants are a block or two away and very convenient (although more expensive than buying things on the mainland).- Breakfast at the K Grill is awesome and convenient.- Easy location to get in/out of when you are navigating there are giving anyone directions to pick you up (what i was doing w/ my business appts) - Business center is available with internet, fax, and photocopies- EXCELLENT staffNegatives:- Very tourist oriented- and there is certainly tons of tourists who stay here.- Probably not really good for honeymooners who would prefer more of a quieter setting.- Tons of kids running/jumping/crying and any given time in the public areas- but this could be a plus if you are looking for a kid-friendly place-Fitness center mediocre but easy access to run on the beach Overall: Awesome choice if you are looking for the best value- If you are traveling for business and want to choose an optimally located hotel on the strip, then this hotel is for you!- especially because this Marriott gives pretty good corporate rates compared to the other big names nearby.

<Author>aloha1123
<Content>Loved The Waikiki Beach Marriott We just returned from 10 days at the Waikiki Beach Marriott, and had a great time! The location is awesome, right across from the beach, on the best stretch of beach in Waikiki. This location is far superior to the location where the Sheraton Waikiki is located. We were originally going to stay at the Sheraton Waikiki and are so happy we changed. Trust me, there is so much construction down at that end that you really don't want to stay there. It is noisy and ugly to look at. To us, the proximity to the beach, and therefore the views are extremely important. The hotel is beautiful. I recommend getting a Deluxe Ocean View if you can, the view of Waikiki Beach is postcard perfect. Drinks by the pool were great, although the bartenders were not that friendly and it took some of the serving staff a few days to warm up. The towel attendants, both of them, are first rate and super friendly. Always had a smile. The hotel is clean, beautiful and we would definitely come stay here again next time we are in Waikiki. Felt very safe staying at the Marriott, and overall we had a fantastic stay. Thanks to all for recommending the K Tower, we did request it, and it was far better than the P Tower, which is set back quite a bit.

<Author>singh1975
<Content>Not worth the high price... Stayed here from feb 15 to 20th with my wife and two girls. Location is good,right across from the beach in waikiki. (As far as I'm concerned, you don't really need to be on the beach in Honololulu, it makes no difference at all).This was my first trip to Hawaii since I was a kid, and was really looking forward to it. I'm a Marriott rewards elite member--that combined with the fact that the Marriott had the lowest price of all 4 or 5 star hotels on the beach ($275/night), made it a good choice for me. We arrived at the hotel about 11pm on the 15th--took forever to find the valet entrance--the actual entrance to the hotel is actually on a side street. Once there, it took another 10 minutes to find the valet who looked rather grumpy, and became even more so when I didn't leave him a tip, (I usually only do so when I pick up the car). So far, not too good, but I wrote it off to the late hour.Had a bell hop pick up all our luggage and got to the check in desk. No line ups, quite a few clerks. My check in agent wasn't exactly very cheerful, but she was very efficient in her broken english (she was Japanese). (As a side note, this hotel really does cater very heavily to the Japanese Group Tours market). Lobby was nice, nothing spectacular. Had a nice little waterfall in the center of it with some tables and chairs. Entire lobby is open air, however, it is covered.Room was nice enough, beds and pillows were fantastic, some of the best I've ever slept in. No mini-bar, but there was a small fridge. Very small bathroom, with standard amenities. House keeping was always courteous, and always cleaned up perfectly no matter how much mess my kids made. Asked for a crib, and it arrived in two minutes handled by two people. Room had a balcony with an ocean view. As others have said, these rooms are not ocean facing--you have to lean over the side of the balcony to get a partial ocean view.Room service menu was very limited and way overpriced. The breakfast buffet was reasonably priced and pretty good. Service was average, nothing extraordinary. Concierge desk however, was always courteous, very helpful.Takes about 5 to 7 minutes to get from room to beach, as we were in the south tower. Not too much of an inconvenience. The beach in front of the hotel was a breaker wall as previously mentioned. However, this proved to be great for us with our little kids, as they could walk as far as they wanted and only be in 1 to 1.5 feet of water. Two swimming pools, both tiny--ridiculous for a hawaiian resort.Overall, I'd say this is an average 3 star hotel with room service. Nothing spectacluar about it--if you're looking for something more, go elsewhere. Certainly the price I paid for the room wasn't justified. Wouldn't stay here again if in Honolulu.

<Content>Loved it! We visited the Marriott January 10-15, and it was great!The beds are the best beds we have ever had in a hotel. (I am 29 and it was too crazy for me) This was down the road more and wonderful. Still the great Waikiki experience, but really relaxing at the same time. They say to stay in the front tower facing the ocean, and made the other tower to be not as good. We were in the back tower (paokaolani??) and it was great. It has more floors and seems to be a quicker elevator anyway. You do have to walk to the other tower to get to the main road, but the walk is maybe 2 more minutes if that. I would happily request the 2nd tower again in a heartbeat. This is a great hotel.

<Author>Gordo
<Content>A great pre-cruise hotel We stayed at this wonderful hotel prior to taking a cruise on the Pride of America. We had a great flight on United and pre-reserved a taxi pick-up with Bob from Star Taxi (800-671-2999). He has a flat rate of $25 from the airport to the hotels on Waikiki Beach. After getting our bags we called his 800 number. He was waiting for us outside the airport and we had a quick ride to the hotel. There was no line at check-in. When the clerk showed us that our room was in the back tower, we decided to pay for the upgrade to a deluxe ocean view room in the front tower. We were very glad that we did and felt it was well worth the additional charge. We had a wonderful view of ocean and the hotels to the north. We were able to watch the surfers and see beautiful sunsets from our balcony. The room was nicely appointed with an AWESOME bed - it was unbelievably comfortable and well appreciated after the long flight. There was also a safe (free), mini-fridge (big plus), coffee maker and blow dryer in the room. We had read that there were long waits for the elevators, but we did not find it to be an issue. We had breakfast at the hotel buffet and the food was wonderful. The fruit was fresher than we had anywhere else during our visit. We also ate at Duke's and had a great meal at the Shorebird. The ahi tuna was incredible - and we were able to see the fireworks at the Hilton from right outside the bar. A big plus to staying at the Marriott pre-cruise is the NCL office located in the lobby area. We were able to check-in for the ship the night before our cruise. They took our pictures and we breezed through the cruise terminal and were on the ship in less than ten minutes from arrival. We spent a little time at the pool at the K Tower. We were only there in the late afternoon since this was the only time you were able to get any sun by the pool. The staff was very friendly and provided quick service for a snack and drinks. There was an ABC convenience store right in the lobby and on the street level in front of the hotel. There was also some nice shopping available on the lower level of the K tower.We walked down to some of the other hotels which seemed a lot more crowded than our hotel. Even though the Marriott was sold out during our stay, we didn't feel that was an issue. We really liked the feel at the Royal Hawaiian - we stopped by their beachfront bar for a Mai Tai - very tasty. The hotel opens right onto the beach and has lounge chairs on it for their guests' use. We were able to get a late check out which was greatly appreciated. We were extremely happy with our stay at this Marriott property. We were lucky to get a chance to spend some time on the North Shore. What an absolutely fantastic experience. We ate several meals at Hale'iwa Joe's and would highly recommend it. We hope that everyone visiting Honolulu gets a chance to see the beauty of the North Shore. It is a vast difference to the big city feel of Honolulu. We had an 11 pm flight out of Honolulu. It was easy getting through the airport. Stores were closing at 10pm, so if you have a late flight don't count on the stores being open for any last minute gifts. I hope you find this information useful. Please feel free to send an email with any questions.

<Author>daisy
<Content>Great hotel Just returned from a week long trip to Oahu. We originally were booked at the Pacific Beach, but after staying there one night, switched to the Marriott. The Marriott is in a great location with fantastic views of Waikiki beach. The decor is modern and the room was very clean. There were constant upgrades even during the time period we were there (a new carpet was placed in the main entrance area, walls were being painted, etc.) The main floor is open to the outside and has beautiful fountains and vegetation. Everything is located in or near the hotel including 2 Seattle's Best locations, an ABC store and Arancino, an italian restaurant with a great breakfast mini buffet. Also, for those of you interested in surfing, there is a beautiful long board break right in front of the hotel. For people with children, there are protected ocean waters in front of the hotel as well as two pools on the 3rd floor. Overall, I definitely recommend this hotel. By the way, request a room in the front building (Kealohilani Tower) because its a bit closer to everything.

<Content>Nice enough, Good Location Stayed here over Thanksgiving 2005. The rooms were above average for a Marriott. The price was a bit high but I suspect that is just Honolulu. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolutely the best beach on Waikiki !!! Absolutely the best beach on Waikiki !!!!! Most of the water front Waikiki hotels have either a narrow or very little beach. The Marriott is situated on the widest beach on Waikiki. We rented one of the timeshare units, which had one bedroom and completely equipped kitchen. The price was fantastic in comparison to one of the Marriott's luxury double rooms. The unit was super clean, and cleaning service was daily. They even cleaned the kitchen! On our side of the timeshare tower, we had a fantastic view of the Pacific, the surfers, and Diamond Head. The View was obstructed by another tower, but still fabulous. The timeshare rentals are available through normal Marriott reservations. The pool is also the best and largest on Waikiki that I am aware. If we returned to Waikiki, I would only stay at the Marriott.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Nice place to stay in Waikiki My boyfriend and I spent 4 days at the Marriott from Oct 12-16/2005...having just arrived from Maui, I was disappointed at first by how commercialized Waikiki was, but soon found it a fun place to be....we had a room on the 14th floor in the back tower, with a partial ocean view....which meant, if you stood on your balcony, overtop of all the traffic going by below, and looked left, you could see the beach between the hotels....having had a breathtaking view of the beach in Maui, this was a little disappointing...and with the sound of the traffic, we weren't able to sleep with our doors open at night....for a large Marriott hotel, this was very nice, but there wasn't any personal service, everyone was simply a room number to the staff due to the size of the hotel....the location of this hotel is great if you want to be in the heart of all the action on Waikiki...we opted not to rent a car, and took the city bus to many places, or simply walked...if you have the opportunity, take one of the guided bus tours of Oahu as you'll get to see what the entire island is like, not just Waikiki....we took the city bus to Hanauma Bay to snorkel, Diamond Head, Pearl Harbour, Alo Moana shopping centre, and Dog, The Bounty Hunter's office....the city bus drivers were great about making sure tourists got off at the right spot....we only went to the pool at the Marriott once as we enjoy the beach, but were able to take hotel towels with us to the beach...the beach directly in front of the hotel was crowded, so we opted to walk further down the street to San Souci beach just the other side of the Aquarium (at the W hotel)....it was about 10 minutes, but was cleaner and quieter, and less crowded...I enjoyed that the shops stayed open late each evening so tourists can wander the strip and shop until 11pm....we never ate at the hotel, but would recommend Tiki's (in the hotel next door) for mahi mahi, and Chuck's (in the Outrigger) for a great steak and view of the beach....if I were to return to Hawaii again, I doubt I would come back to Waikiki as it's very much like Miami or NYC on the beach, but if I did, I would consider staying at this hotel again...it was nice, not outstanding, but nice  
<Date>Nov 6, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Bait and Switch! If you don't read my entire post, please read this first part at least. There are two towers at this hotel. One of them is across the street from the beach. The other is a half block back from the first tower which blocks any reasonable view of the ocean. I don't know how someone would guarantee the front tower, but being stuck in the back tower was really disappointing.Upon check-in we told the woman at the front desk that we were honeymooners and had requested a room upgrade on the web (from an ocean view to deluxe ocean view). She told us they were booked solid and no upgrades were available. Typical! Not such a big deal though. But then we were told that all they had were rooms with 2 double beds or rooms on a smoking floor. Neither option made us happy. We were exhausted though. So we took the smoking room which, to be fair, did not smell like smoke at all. When we got to our Ocean View room though, we discovered that we were in the Rear Tower and had to stand on the balcony and look between the front tower and another hotel to see the ocean.All of this wasn't really a big deal. But when you have the fantasy of a Hawaiian beach and ocean view from your room and you get stuck in a lousy room, it puts a damper on things.On a good note, the sushi place in the Marriott called Sansei (sp?) is fantastic!!!

<Content>i'm here right now hi all, I'm currently in Waikiki staying at the Marriott beach resort. I also seached the word rental car coupon on the web and used one of the discount codes that i found. It gave me 20% off. I would definetly rent a car on this island and drive around the island. too much to see here. Hotel,Waikiki Beach Marriott is is pretty decent hotel. its located at the end of Waikiki but right accross the street from the beach which is beatiful. Chkin was good. I did arrive at 12pm so our room was not ready. The guarentee is at 3pm. They did provide us with a hospitality room to change and clean up. I also recived an upgrade from a garden view to partial ocean view. I did ask for the upgrade very nicely and also lied and said that this was my honeymoon trip.... :) I am also a Marriott memeber so i'm sure all of the above factor counted. - very nice and friendly staff - Room 2418: nice size, full view of the Diamond head and partial view of the ocean. room is good size with a king bed. decor can use some updating. the bathroom is really small with very week water pressure in the shower. might be because this is one of the top floor (25 in total).- ELEVATOR: yes...the world famous elevator problem. it isn't as bad as i though it would be. there is the sign that states they are going through the remodel. most i had to wait was about 5min...also keep in mind that i'm on the top floor.- air conditioner works great! - internet connection is $14 a day. if you have a wireless card, you can connect to other networks in the area for cheaper. I found one that was $25 for the whole week.- This hotel is on the end of the Waikiki towards Diamond head. shops, resturants, and other hotel are all along the street so its very nice. The beach is also right accross the street.- The pool is very dinky and small but i found that most hotels on the strip are the same. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good place to stay in Waikiki We booked the cheapest room on Marriott's web site (senior rate, city view), and when we checked in we were automatically given an upgrade to an ocean view room. I am a member of their rewards program and use their affinty credit card, so that may have been a factor. Nice large room, and a decent, but not full, view of the beach and the ocean and also of sunrises over the mountains to the east of the city.Positives: Great location: across the street from a not too crowded at the time section of the beach and right in the heart of WaikikiVery nice, good sized room, up to Marriott's ususual standards, and helpful staff.Negatives: Parking costs $14 a day (with in and out privileges) and the room key sometimes took 3 or 4 tries to make the gates work. May be better to use excellent public transit around the city and rent a car by the day (Hertz is in the hotel and others are nearby) to see other parts of the island.High-speed internet is available in the rooms, but costs about $13 a day.Other:Elevators were OK most of the time but had to wait a couple of minutes a few times. Signs say they are upgrading the system.Could hear music coming from outdoor restaurant across the street, but was not very loud and did not keep us awake.Stayed five nights and would stay there again if I wanted to be right by the beach and in the heart of Waikiki.

<Author>Basics_from_Barb
<Content>Always count on Marriott After much reading and decision-making, we chose the Marriott Waikiki Beach resort for 3 nights to experience Waikiki Beach. I read more trip-advisor reviews than anyone, and I am here to tell you that what one person found a negative, another may find a positive. It was a great place to stay (did request the K tower as someone suggested and very pleased with that choice) and found September to be a great month where there were not a lot of children and a very fun adult time to go. The Marriott had a great location, friendly people, clean, easy to catch tours at . . and I enjoyed listening to the music the Aston (across the street) had going at night. If you plan on going to bed at 8:00 and want peace and quiet, don't go to Waikiki Beach. Go to the Turtle Bay Resort on the other end of the island, where we stayed for one night and it was wonderful. So experience the noise and excitement of Waikiki Beach - and go expecting it!! - and then go to the other end of the island to get away from traffic and city noise. It's all in what you expect. Super picky people need to go and pay the tremendous prices at other hotels. But for the money we paid per night at the Marriott - we found it to be just what we expected and had a wonderful trip. Enjoy!!

<Author>vikkij1980
<Content>Fantastic Hotel - Some people must expect too much! I stayed at the Marriott Waikiki Beach for 5 nights on September 4, 2005. I am 25 and 3 of my girlfriends are within the same age group. I thought there were mixed reviews on this hotel but thought I would go ahead and book it anyway, as it seemed to be the best price for the location and average on good reviews. I honestly loved this hotel and would stay there again and recommend it to anyone. The staff were extremely helpful and friendly. When we checked in, I realised I had requested a high floor room forgetting that one of my friends was scared of heights but we were moved to a lower floor room with no problems! As we were 4 females we didn't want to share beds so two roll away beds were taken to our room immediately. The room wasn't huge but still big enough for 2 double beds and 2 full size roll away beds and with us still managing to move around freely, so we had no complaints. I was expecting the elevators to be very slow because of the reviews but something must have changed because we didn't have to wait longer than a minute each time and were constanly in and out of them. The hotel is in a very good location, right across from the beach and within walking distance of the restaurants and shops, which was a huge selling point for us!I have stayed in many holidays, as this year I have been on 5 vacations to date so I can compare this hotel to many hotels of it's star rating and price range. I cannot see why people could rate this hotel not that great because it exceeded all my expectations. All we really wanted was a clean room, great location and helpful staff. We got all that and much more.I realise that some people are always going to complain about something and not everyone has the same views but if you are looking for a clean, beautiful hotel, with great amenities (especially the gym) and a great location, you should certainly stay here!The breakfast buffet was also good and was included in our Paradise plus room package, which I am glad I chose as it was $12.99 (Continental) or $19.99 (regular) normally. I would also really recommend going to Kauai, even if just for a day trip! Oahu really wasn't what I imagined Hawaii to be like as although it is lovely, it is very Americanized with tall buildings etc. However, Kauai is very Hawaiian and the real Hawaiian experience.

<Author>ennl
<Content>Nothing good here We stayed at the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort Hotel in August 2005 for 7 nights. We have stayed in many Marriott hotels, mainly in England, and expected the same high standard that we were used to. We were very disappointed. We had problems at check-in. Although we had informed them that we would arrive at 12 noon the room wasn't ready and they asked us to come back at 3pm, it still wasn't ready. At 3.30pm we were given the keys. Having to queue up for about 15 to 20 minutes each time was not what we wanted on the first day of our holiday here. The room itself was clean, but the bathroom needed attention as there was mould in the shower and the bath was peeling. We paid for an upgrade for a partial ocean view which was worth it and it was nice to sit on the balcony at night. The concierge desks were a joke, two desks but with too many customers. Typical waiting time to speak to the concierge was 20 - 30 minutes and after a few attempts we gave up. If you decide to stay here (and we strongly recommend that you don't), choose K tower for better views. However, be prepared to wait ages for a lift and then when they arrive be prepared for the a squash. There were 5 elevators, but one was broken the whole time. Once in your room don't expect to get any peace until after midnight because the hotel opposite has a live band playing every night very loudly. We were on the 18th floor and even with the windows shut we could hear them. To summarize, we were very disappointed. We thought we had chosen one of the best hotels and it certainly wasn't. We would definitely not stay here again.

<Author>Lasemuse
<Content>Great Location Our family of four stayed here for two nights on our way to the Big Island. We had a spacious deluxe corner room with two queen beds and a fold-out couch - perfect as we were staying with our two teen-aged sons. Our room over-looked the beach and promenade with its terrific tiki torches after dark. The bathroom was a little small with only one sink and a tub/shower with shower curtain but the view made up for it. We were high up, but in the evenings if we opened the balcony door we could faintly hear the live Hawaiian music from Tiki's Restaurant next door. This may be a problem on lower floors. We found all of the staff we dealt with to be very gracious. There were plenty of shops and restaurants within walking distance and of course the beautiful beach across the street. We were even able to walk down to the last of the Wednesday evening concerts at the zoo which was great fun. The only real negative was the elevators that everyone mentions. With one always out of service we had to wait quite a while several times and all the guests were complaining.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Brilliant Hotel Booked hotel on marriott web site and went for the Romance Package as we were celebrating our Silver Wedding Anniversary.On arrival greeted by friendly and helpful bell staff and exceptionally pleasant and helpful male receptionist (Jatin) - he was really helpful and advised that if we changed our room to a double queen status we could have a room in the K tower nearest the beach. (I had originally booked a room with a King bed but apparently there are very few of these and their locations seem to be towards the rear of the K tower and P tower).We were allocated a front corner room on the 23rd floor of the K tower - what views we had; it was tremendous. Picture window towards the ocean/beach and lanai looking up Kalakaua Avenue and Wakiki Beach.Room was bright and clean; small bathroom but adequate. Housekeeping staff very friendly and diligent.Lifts didn't cause us any problems - always arrived in reasonable time. When you are on the 23rd floor any wait is preferable to climbing the stairs!!Breakfast included in package - buffet style in Kuhio Grill and exceptionally good; plenty of choice and eggs/omelettes cooked on request.Also ate in the Steakhouse and again couldn't find any faults - food very good and staff very efficient.Large amount of shops on ground floor of hotel with the customary ABC store (very reasonable prices)Hotel located at the quieter end of the strip but within easy walking distance of shopping malls and international market.Had to cross the road to the beach but this didn't cause any problems.We went to the Polynesian Cultural Centre and would recommend this trip. Also went to Pearl Harbor and yes we had to endure a lengthy line and wait before going to the arizona. Everyone says to go in the morning but by lunchtime the lines had disappeared and waiting times reduced - I would recommend you time your arrival around 1.00pm so as not to waste your morning.The beach was clean and plenty of space. The hawaians are very friendly and we thoroughly enjoyed our 5 night stay at the Marriott. We would definitely stay there again if we return to Oahu.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location but hotel has some issues We just got back from a five night stay over fourth of July weekend at the Marriott Waikiki. We stayed in the recommended tower closest to the beach on the 24th floor with a great ocean view. The good--The balcony view was fantastic; the bed was big  comfortable; the location was perfect; the laundry room was convenient by the pool with comfortable seating/television; the lobby was nice with open air, waterfalls, pond and a Seattle's coffee to get moving in the morning. The bad--the elevators were horrible (as stated many times). People would wait so long they packed in to any that opened. The toilet flushing was somewhat loud. The air conditioner took a long time to cool the room. But the worst was the valet giving our rental car away to another party on the day of departure. They did accomodate us by taking us to the airport themselves, handling the return of the rental car the next day and paying all late fees/gas fillups and sending a $50 gift card with apology, but it definately bothered me the first whole day in Kauai until we heard from them (didn't call until the next morning even though the car came back around 7pm the evening before) that the car was returned undamaged. I never had that happen before and I knew the car wouldn't leave the island, but was extremely concerned that I would be responsible on the remote case that the new driver would damage the vehicle or hurt someone driving it. Nothing happened, but I still wish they would have been more diligent in giving cars out no matter how similar they look. At $19/day plus tip, you think they could master matching the hanging ticket in rearview mirror to the number you held relatively easily. I would have given the hotel 4 stars even with the elevators because of the great visit, but the valet issue made me reluctant on revisiting the hotel in the future.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good hotel since it was free My husband and I spent 7 nights at this hotel in May 2005. The hotel was nice, but after reading all the reviews about people getting upgraded rooms, we were disappointed that we were stuck in a standard room with a city view on the 4th floor in the back tower. When we asked for an upgrade, the clerk treated us like we were ridiculous. (Overall, people in Hawaii were very friendly, though). So, despite what you read about free upgrades, don't expect one. Also, our balcony railing was a concrete wall, so when I actually sat down in a chair on the balcony, I had NO view, unless I looked up at the sky. The 4th floor appeared to be the only floor with no-view concrete wall railings on the balcony. Fortunately, we had enough Marriott Rewards to use to stay for free for our whole visit, so at least we weren't out any money. I doubt I would pay full price to stay at this hotel. Besides the disappointing balcony, the room was nice  clean. We did get a couples massage at Spa Okalina in the hotel, but you cannot use Marriott Bucks for this service. Even though the back of the coupon says you can use it for spa services at Marriott resorts, when we tried to pay with the Marriott Bucks at check-out, they refused to accept it because they said the Marriott didn't own this spa, so that was $100 we weren't intending to pay.Even though this may be the quieter side of Waikiki, that doesn't mean that it's quiet. Our main problem was the noise from the city buses that have the really loud brakes and stop at every block, it seems. The street noise from traffic was bothersome sometimes in our room, even at 11 p.m. We were facing the Aston, but didn't hear any of the loud music other reviewers have referred to, but maybe that's because we were in the back tower. If you are expecting to hear the waves crash on the shore from your room or balcony, this is not the place for you. (Even if you had an ocean front room in the front tower, I doubt you'd be able to hear the ocean becasue there is a street with a lot of people, stores, and restaurants between your room and the ocean).We didn't eat at any of the hotel restaurants. We did enjoy Cheeseburger in Paradise for dinner - fun atmosphere. And, we really enjoyed breakfast at LuLu's next door -- you can eat at a breakfast bar that faces an open window with an ocean view. We also rented a convertible from the Hertz in the hotel and spent a day driving around the island. That was very worthwhile and so neat to drive so close to the ocean. If we ever return to Oahu, we would probably try to stay in the Kailua Beach area instead of Waikiki Beach. Snorkeling at Hanuma Bay, hiking up Diamond Head, and hiking the Manoa Falls trail in the rainforest were all GREAT activities. We went to Germaine's Luau. The luau itself was ok and the food was pretty good (the pork was delicious). If you're a AAA member, you'll get a good discount at this luau. However, I would NOT recommed taking the shuttle that's included in the price. It's about a 45 min. ride to the luau and they have VERY annoying hosts that talk on the microphone on the bus the WHOLE way there and the WHOLE way back. The guy just kept repeating stupid jokes, had some inappropriate humor for kids (much of his gabber related to alcohol), and just wouldn't shut up and let you ride in peace. The only way I would go back to this luau is if I drove myself there. Since it was our first time to Hawaii, we thought we just had to do a luau; however, I probably either just wouldn't do a luau again if I returned, or I might try to Polynesian Culture Center even though it's more expensive and farther away. All in all, we enjoyed our time here, but if I didn't get to stay with Marriott Rewards and was going to pay as much as these rooms cost, I would prefer a hotel that's actually on the beach (although we didn't think the walk to the beach was that bad), a location where you don't hear traffic noise in your room, and place with much fancier resort-type pools.  
<Date>Jul 20, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic location, beautiful view My son and I spent 3 short days in Honolulu at the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort and Spa. We splurged on our hotel because we wanted to be right on Waikiki, and we were there for such a short time, we felt we could afford it. It was so worth it! We were happily surprised to arrive and find our room was ready for early check in - 11:00. They also upgraded us to an ocean view (from a partial ocean view) room, without our even asking and at no extra charge. The hotel itself is not as spectacular as some others - but the service was excellent, the elevators quick and convenient, and the hotel is not so huge that you get lost. The room was very clean and nicely decorated in Hawaiian style. But the very best part in my opinion, was the balcony overlooking the beach. We were on the 15th floor and you could just sit there for hours taking in the view. The hotel is at the quieter end of the strip, and very close to the zoo and the aquarium. The other end of the strip seemed noisy with lots of shops and people. Nice to visit, but I wouldn't want to stay there.One of the reasons I chose this hotel is because they didn't have a kids club. This seems to be a more adult oriented hotel - I didn't really see any kids - which was what I wanted. We ate breakfast at the Grill restaurant (buffet) twice - and it was excellent. We ate dinner at the steakhouse, and it, too, was very good. In the evenings there is a restaurant by the pool, and there is live entertainment. We didn't go downstairs for that, but listened to it from our balcony.I would definitely stay here again. We really really hated to leave. It was a wonderful vacation, and a beautiful location.  
<Date>Jul 17, 2005

<Author>Viking78
<Content>4th of July weekend at Waikiki My family and I stayed at the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort and Spa over the 4th of July holiday. After reading past reviews before and after our stay, I would like to make a few comments that may or may not be helpful to you...Before booking our vacation, our travel agent mentioned that everyone's experience with a particular travel plan and hotel varies with their own expectations and preferences. We did quite a bit of homework before booking our trip and traveling to the islands. For us, it paid off in the end.We booked our stay through Pleasant Holidays (Hotel and transportation only, we booked our airfare and tours separately), and were given a partial ocean view room on the 19th Floor in the K tower. From our lanai, we had a view of the Aston Hotel, Diamond Head and Waikiki Beach. We loved our view and spent every chance we had enjoying it. No complaints there whatsosever.We ate breakfast every morning at the Kuhio Beach Grill and made good use of the buffet. Our experiences with the servers were very positive. Considering we were in Hawaii, the prices were reasonable since food on the neighboring islands is more expensive. In addition, we ate dinner at Arancino's one night and Moana Terrace Grill two nights. Arancino's is reasonably priced and thought the prices at Moana Terrace Grill for food was fair. You could say that the drinks are expensive, but as a previous reviewer mentioned, part of it is based on the glass and to me, you are paying for the ambiance as well (i.e., Music/View of the Ocean).The pools are small, however, most guests spend their time across the street at Waikiki/Kuhio Beach. The pool is great for evening use.The elevators are very slow. No need to elaborate here. What past reviewers have said explains it all.Overall, we were very satisfied with our stay. We thought the staff was friendly and accommodating to our needs. Based on our experience, we would definitely stay there again and use Pleasant Holidays if we return to Oahu.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Stay in Paradise We stayed two days prior to our NCL cruise. They gave us an upgrade to an oceanview-corner room without us asking. The room was very large with two very comfortable queen beds. Noise was not an issue even though several reviews have mentioned that as a complaint. The elevator in the tower was very slow, which was the only complaint. The concierge was very helpful and worked hard to make things right when a tour bus didn't pick us up. I would love to go back to Hawaii and would stay at the Marriott again. I think it is a good value. Sure you could find a better hotel but look at the prices. Is any hotel worth $500 a night?Pearl Harbor was a mixed bag for us. It is a must see, but you are treated like cattle. You get herded into lines, forced to wait for very long periods, subjected to huge lines for the ladies bathroom and museum, and not really allowed to let the surroundings settle in.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Definitely not a 4-star hotel We stayed here for the last two nights of our honeymoon. We had stayed a week at the Four Seasons Resort in Maui and we loved it. If we had stayed at the Mariott first and the Four Seasons second, then maybe I would have given it more of a chance. With that said, when we first arrived the Marriott staff let us check in a few hours early and upgraded us to an Ocean View room in the tower further from the ocean (there are two towers). The room was on the 19th floor and had two full beds. The decor is very green and quite tacky, seems as if they have not updated it since the 70s. We asked them to change to a room with a king bed and after about 30 minutes of searching, they had switched us to a Partial Ocean View in the tower closer to the ocean on the 11th floor. The view was actually a lot better than the previous room which was an Ocean view and higher up. The bathrooms are small and very basic. The balcony is very small and the room has a mini-fridge but not a mini-bar. There is a coffee maker in the bathroom. We got free breakfast as part of our package and the breakfast was actually prety good. There was a very good selection of buffet foods. The staff is ok, they aren't overly friendly. Overall, I this this is a very basic, no frills hotel. We booked with Pleasant Holidays, I would avoid booking with them, they changed our flights around and we had lots of layovers on the way back. Also, while we were there we got tickets to Germaine's Luau through the concierge, I would avoid eating the food there, it made me sick that night. Also, give yourself extra time if planning on going anywhere, the elevators take forever and are almost always packed to full capacity. Location is pretty good, not the best, but above average. It's not right on the beach, you have to cross a road to get to a public beach. I wouldn't stay here again, but then again I wasn't a fan of Honolulu/Waikiki as a whole and do not plan on returning.

<Author>coopchang
<Content>Mostly ++++ at the Marriott Just got back from a 6 night stay at the Marriott Waikiki! Mostly good things to stay. From previous reviews asked for the K tower even though originally we were booked in the P tower. The K tower is the tower closer to the beach and was the most recently remodeled. Our room was an ocean view and we later discovered there is a deluxe ocean view which is much better, but 65.00 more per night and no King beds left. We did have an ocean view but only from the balcony. We were up on the 24th floor, facing Diamond Head and the Aston Hotel. If we sat on the balcony we could see a stretch of ocean. The pool is larger on the K tower side although we found both pools pretty small. Food at the pool was decent and OK priced. Drinks are very expensive ($8.00) at the pool because they serve them in a fancy take home plastic parfait glass. Ask for the plain plastic cup instead. Pools also have cabanas which you rent for $15.00 a day. We splurged on our last day for a cabana. We had already absorbed way too much sun in 6 days and the chaise lounges in the cabanas are padded and cushy! What a luxury to take a nap outside by the pool with a cool trade wind! Slow elevators continue to plague this complex. Sometimes you could wait 10+ minutes to catch an elevator. Marriott recognizes this as a big problem and 1 elevator was taken out of service completely for an upgrade. Our room was nice size and the King bed was luscious!!!! Water pressure in the shower is low....hard to rinse soap from long hair....but toilets had a super-sonic flush! Places to eat that were close by that became our favorites: Tiki Grill at the Aston, Dukes, and the always popular...Shorebird Grill! For every day essentials...the staff at the K tower ABC store was the best and we purchased water, beer, wine, chips, and other snacks! P.S. Loved the room's refrigerator and closet safe!  
<Date>Jun 29, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Nice hotel of you like the touristy thing, but not for everybody The Marriott Waikiki Beach is a nice hotel across the street from Waikiki Beach. I paid $265/nite in June which was a little overpriced in my opinion. The elevators in the Paoakalani Tower our extremely slow and you often have to wait 5+ minutes between 4-6pm to get on one. The Marriott hotel is in the middle of everything and with that there are lines at all of the restaurants in the neighborhood so reservations are suggested. There is plenty of action always goin on in the area and you shouldn't have a problem finding something if you have kids or want a drink. The gym was nice and no charge, unlike most things in Honolulu. If you don't mind the touristy feeling of Hawaii it is a good hotel, but if you are looking to relax than I would go elsewhere.

<Author>fredandkell
<Content>Great hotel, but noisy.... The GOOD: Got a double upgrade to corner oceanview without asking...stayed in K tower, which is the nicer tower....huge room, comfortable beds, large balcony, convenient to everything, less hustle-bustle side of Waikiki, friendly staff, robes in room, good bathroom toiletries. Waikiki Beach is great! Spa was nice - had a good massage - but locker room facilities were small (one shower in women's locker room?)The BAD: Let's face it, Waikiki is a party beach. The Aston next door is LOUD. They play nonstop music until about 10:30 pm every day so a mid-afternoon nap is difficult. We were on the front corner of the K tower on the side AWAY from the Aston, and it was still very loud. Also the Marriott itself plays music on the 3rd floor by the pool (but not so late) and on Saturday and Sunday nights they set up a big movie screen on the beach and you can hear that too. Would I stay here again? Yes. I would just insist on being in the back tower, FAR away from the Aston. THINGS TO DO: Disagree with the below reviewer, we loved Cheeseburger in Paradise. At first I was skeptical that it was a tourist trap, but they really do have some of the best cheeseburgers and fries you will ever eat. Also liked Run Sushi in the Marriott Lobby. We honestly thought Pearl Harbor was a bit overrated. You get there and you get a ticket for your time to see a 23-minute movie (I found very interesting, but my husband thought was boring, because he's a big history buff and found it to be too simplistic for people who already know a lot about WWII). The memorial itself is simply that, a place to reflect and read the names of the fallen. So if you do go, be prepared to wait about 3 hours to see a movie and look at a memorial and go home. Not being disrespectful to the fallen men and women of Pearl Harbor; just letting you know that there isn't much to do here.

The sand isnt very nice and unless you stay at one of the major Sheratons (Pink Palace or Moana) then you probably won't be able to get a beach chair/umberella. Also keep in mind this is wall to wall people everywhere. Think Disney World crowds. The food at a so called nice restraunt from what I experienced is NOT good! Better yet plan on spending alot of money for lousy food and dining experience. I hate being this negative but considering the time and exspense of traveling one should be forewarned. I did get out to other parts of Ohau and didn't find it much better...still a ton of traffic and people compressed. Beaches/meals ok not anything great. I have visited Kaui and Maui and find that Maui is the best in my opinion. My husband agrees with me having the same opinion. Go to Waikiki if you must for a couple of days but you could skip it entirely and you would not miss much. Those who are so in love with it, I have to question whether they have traveled and been to really nice beaches/resorts. I guess it depends on what you are looking for...it is somewhat similar to South Beach in Miami, except South Beach is better. Good luck!  
<Date>Jun 6, 2005

<Author>Cindylovestotravel
<Content>Most comfortable beds ever! Stayed three enjoyable days, loved the location across from the Waikiki peir, walking distance to the the zoo and park. On Saturday night they had a drive in movie on the beach. Walking distance to great shopping including a local swap meet and upscale shops. We saved a fortune by using the coupons in the tourest guide books you find in lobby's and in displays on the street. The hotel was nice and clean and the room was large. The rooms have a refrigerator and coffee pot and they sell yogurt, snacks, fruit, coffee etc. in the ABC store in the lobby. We were upgraded to a partial ocean/diamond head view but we were in the back building so honestly the view wasn't that great, it was a good upgrade but not sure it would have been worth the money. When I go back I will definetely pay for the full ocean view in the front building on the oposite side of the Aston hotel which has an outside lounge which you would be able to hear. I took advantage of some hotel freebies which were great... I made a free Lai from orchids in the hotel lobby (didn't see it advertised so ask at the desk). I took the free snorkel lesson in the pool. At first I was disappointed because they give you the stuff in the scuba shop and tell you what to do and you go to the pool alone to practice, but the practice was needed and it was good to do it at my own comfort level. When I really went snorkeling it all paid off! If there was any real complaint it would be the pools they are small and cold but being right across the street from the beach we didn't spend any real time there anyhow. The beds are made especially for Marriott and I found out they sell them to the public (around $1500. after shipping, etc.) I am ordering one! I registered for their email specials and they sent me one for my dates so we stayed here on a great price of $159. per night. We stayed here before we went on the Pride Of Aloha cruise which worked out great! Definetley spend the money to get at least one day of the prepackage if you are cruising. Pre-check in is in the lobby and they came and got our luggage on departure day, we didn't have to deal with it until we were in our room on the ship. We had a special line at the ship and didn't have to deal with long lines for check in! Next to the hotel there are several shuttle/trolley pick up stations making getting places easier. We went to Germaine's Luau which picks you up at that shuttle location you can book it through the hotel but I found a coupon and got 20% off booking through Germaine's. For $10.00 PP we got a shuttle through the conceirge to go RT to the memorial. The pick up location was right outside the doors not at the shuttle location and the shuttle was a half hour late but the ride was good and they picked us up to bring us back right on time.

<Author>onedude
<Content>Yet another amazing stay with Marriott We stayed at this property from 5/23 through 5/28 and this was our first time back to the hotel since 2002, when on that occasion they had recently taken over from the former Regent Hotel chain.Everything quintessential about Marriott was there. Relaxed check in, friendly welcoming staff, the open air lobby...even though we were early we were given a room number and a time it would be available, along with a double upgrade to ocean view. We were invited to relax by the pool and to recheck for our keys later. We did that (and reminder - please use sunscreen as we forgot and ended up like a honey glazed ham :)Room was 2268 in P tower - Non Smoking King. Great room size, the amazingly comfortable Marriott Bed and heaps of room for our 3 suitcases and to stretch out. This room was interconnecting but we heard no noise from our neighbours on either side despite the hotel being full.The view was great from our room - straight ahead to the azure waters of Waikiki Beach. A little street noise even at 22 stories, but easily blocked out with the sliding door closed.The pool in K tower is better (more resort style) and can be easily reached by getting out of the elevator on Level 3 in P tower and walking across the ramp. Great bar and great views and loads of deck chairs.There are a heap more shops in the Marriott lobby now including 2x Seattle's Best Coffees, a Hertz depot and lots of food options including the Kuhio grill and Sushi Restauarant. The Sushi place does happy hour Bud for USD1.95 from 1130am - 9pm - looked a great deal.We tried Cheeseburger in Paradise like one of the previous reviews here as it was close - but we were disappointed. Our check for two burgers, fries and a few beers was pushing USD50 - you could have done a lot better for quality and quantity at Denny's down on Kuhio.Walking distance to everything including bars and the Food Pantry on Kuhio (opposite the Ohana Waikiki) and great value with great staff. I would pay top dollar to stay here again - the Marriott experience is world class at this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved this Hotel We just got back from a vacation on Oahu. We arrived at the Marriott Waikiki on 5/20 and checked out on 5/29. I agree completely with most of the reviews on this hotel. The hotel is a great place to stay. We stayed in the K tower in a corner room on the 21st floor. We had an ocean view picture window and an ocean view balcony. We upgraded to this room and it was worth paying for. The views were amazing. Most mornings we had coffee on the balcany while we watched the surfers. The hotel and our room were nicely furnished with modern, comfortable furniture. Our room was immaculate upon check-in and thouroughly cleaned by our maid each day. The hotel staff were also able to answer our questions about any subject. We were never given wrong information or mislead by any staff member.The pool area of this tower was also great. The pool is not very big, but with the Pacific Ocean across the street, it doesn't need to be. The only bad review I have applies to the elevators. There are too few of them and they are too slow. I have read other bad reviews of the hotel and find much of them are not based in reality. Perhaps some people are experiencing sour grapes.

<Author>KMurphyAtlanta
<Content>Very pleased I am platinum with Marriott (75 stays or more per year) and like to use my my status for Marriott vacation upgrades. I stay in a lot of dumpy courtyards for business in order to have nice vacations at better Marriotts. Usually while on vacation, Marriott treats me very well, and the Waikiki Beach Resort experience was no different. I paid for a non-ocean view room because Marriotts always upgrade Platinum members- even though there is no guarantee. This time, they couldn't upgrade me, which was a disappointment. This would normally be met with suspicion as the hotel is quite large even though the number of rooms directly on the ocean are few. However, the manager lowered the rate that I paid to the lowest quality room rate and I had a partial ocean view which had a fantastic view of both the ocean and the skyline. I was very pleased. We could look up the road that runs along the beach and see the nightly torch lighting of the lights along the ocean. Once again, Marriott rewards their platinum members in a consistently good way. The room was quiet, large and clean, the balcony very large. The service quite good. The bathroom was modern and clean- all you need to know about the quality of a hotel is a picture of room's bathroom. Sorry I don't have one to attach.Oddly, the three things that make Oahu famous to me- the beach, pearl harbor and the luau, were all strangely disappointing. One thing I would tell anyone who has a love of the mid-east and islamic arts is to visit the Doris Duke house. It's a logistical nightmare to do it, but the highlight of the trip. Read up on her- she had an interesting life and a fantastic home. Also, rent a car for at least a day and drive around the island- easily feasible. The surf on the North Side must be seen to be understood. TV doesn't do justice to just how big those waves are.

<Author>Kymani67
<Content>Business/Vacation..it was wonderful!! I stayed at the Marriott for 5 nights. I asked to be upgraded for free but I had a government rate so, I paid the extra $30 a night. I ended up in the K tower room 730. The view was a partial ocean view and across the street was the party hard Ashton Hotel. It is kind of loud but when you have to work in the morning..it can be a drag!! The breakfast downstairs by the shops was great...a buffet and cook to order eggs, omelet, waffles..It was 21.00 for one person but I was not paying for it..I ate at the pool a few times..a little expensive..your best bet is to walk to the restaurants around the corner like paradise cheeseburger. The best place for breakfast was the seaside grill. Breakfast was like 5.00..great place if looking for low budget. After working for three days, I got to take some personal time to myself..I ended swimming with the dolphins and sea lions..it was expensive but an enjoyable time to remember. Also, try the catamaran boats on the beach..There are about 3 different boats. The one I pick was the blue/white boat. It was $15 and you get to bring your own drinks (they did sell drinks on there!). The boat took you out in the ocean for about 1 1/2 - 2hours...the 3 men on the boat was very nice and made sure your cup was always full...the music on the boat was great and also, the owner has a dog..a small dog..the dog stayed cover-up right under the captain..I thought that was cute..On the boat, the sunset was beautiful. One place that you have to eat is the TOP of Waikiki. The service and food was surperb...I had the lamb cooked in the 3 different ways...If you arrive between 5 -6...a sunset menu is available for lower prices...AND DO NOT FORGET TO MAKE RESERVATION!!! Also, ate at Bubba Gumps at the ala Mona mall..Across from Bubba Gumbs is the Mai Tai bar..a nice place to have a few drinks and good convo. THE MOST IMPORTANT THING TO REMEMBER..while walking on the strip, pick up a magazine that says 101 things to do in Oahu..there are coupons, and everything you can imagine to do for the whole family..BTW, the TOP of Waikiki coupon is in there..15% of the dinner entree..One complaint about the hotel in K tower is the elevators..they are slow..one day it took me 10 min to get an elevator...either the elevator had too many people or it was just slow...OH!! saw a famous person..Phillip Bailey from Earth and Wind Fire!! Still looking good!! I may be 31..but Mr. Bailey has it going on..If you looking to club...party..hip-hop music..Rumors on Friday at the ala Mona hotel...On thurs..Ocean Club..500 ala Mona blvd....

<Author>SingleTraveler98
<Content>Best Vacation in Years I spent a wonderful week at the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort and Spa in April 2005. I stayed on the 20th floor of the Paoakalani tower, the newer of the resort's two towers, in an ocean view room. The view was great, although next time I will stay in a deluxe ocean view room in the Kealohilani tower, which is just across the street from Waikiki beach. It's apparent that the hotel's owners have spent a considerable sum remodeling this resort, and the rooms are quite impressive. The room I stayed in was large and included a king size bed with a half dozen comfortable pillows. The bathroom had a marble floor and a complete tub with shower. I was pleased to find a refrigerator, rather than a mini-bar, as well as a safe in the room. The people who work here are wonderful. Every employee I met was friendly, knowledgeable, and helpful. I appreciated complimentary copies of the Wall Street Journal and the Honolulu Star Bulletin each morning. The resort includes a steak house, two hotel-operated restaurants, a sushi place, as well as an Italian restaurant. The food was delicious, the service commendable, and the prices lower than I would have expected at any hotel, let alone a hotel as nice as this one. The hotel includes a Paul Brown spa, Spa Olakino, where I experienced their signature massage, which was very relaxing. In addition, the hotel is home to a number of shops, two ABC stores, and two Seattle's Best Coffee locations. There are two swimming pools and an additional large area devoted to tanning. The hotel is located at the less crowded east end of Waikiki beach and is one block from Kapiolani park and the zoo, which is worth visiting. I've stayed at other hotels in Honolulu, all of which were satisfactory, but the Marriott was outstanding. I will be making a return trip.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic location... I stayed here for 6 nights. I was upgraded from a city view to a partial ocean view without asking. The room sizes are standard for the Marriott label and I have stayed at numerous Marriott locations throughout the U.S and Europe. The location is unbeatable. It is within a few minutes walking distance to all the major attractions, restaurants, markets, etc of Waikiki Beach. Although the hotel is not on the beach rather across the street, that doesn't really matter because you'll walk to find a nice empty space to set your goods down anyway. Service was friendly and efficient. The pools are not resort style pools even though this is a resort  spa They are standard boring pool areas. The Japanese restaurant Sansei, located on the 3rd floor is excellent. Don't bother with Kuhio Grill-they charge exorburant prices--you're better off walking down the street and eating somewhere else and getting more bang for your buck. I would recommend renting a car for at least a couple of days so you can explore the island. My hubby  I got tired of the hustle and bustle of the Waikiki area and found exploring the north  eastern shores to be rather calming. Plus the beaches are far less crowded and absolutely breathtaking. Waimanalo Beach Park and Sandy Beach were not busy at all and far cleaner than Waikiki. Of course you should not miss snorkeling at Haunauma Bay and make a trip to the USS ARizona...its free so don't let those pesky tour operators try to make $$ off of you. Get there early (b4 8am) so you would have to wait long. If you can splurge on dinner, you MUST make reservations at Alan Wong's restaurant. You'll need a car to get there, but 3 people we encountered who live on the island recommended it and said it is the best on the entire island. I must agree.

<Author>savytraveler
<Content>Very clean, convenient location Everything was awesome. If you stay here, make sure you get a room facing Diamond Head or the ocean, and high enough to overlook neighboring hotels/buildings. (Be aware that a partial ocean view means a sliver of ocean out of the corner of your eye) We had a room overlooking Diamond Head and it was high enough so we weren't staring at a building (30th floor I think). Really no complaints other than the pool was very nice, but small and no hot tub. We enjoyed the 'hustle and bustle' of Waikiki' since this was our first trip to Hawaii. It was great to be so close to the shops and resteraunts, but next time, JW Marriott at Ko Olina will be more our pace. The JW Marriott at Ko Olina has a gorgeous private beach and I hear their are Sea Turtles! If you're young and never been to Oahu/Hawaii, or don't care to drive all over the island, you'll love the Marriott Waikiki. There's a lot to do and they just poured a lot of money into this end of Waikiki, beautifying the parks with beautiful trees, flowers and statues everywhere, great for taking pictures. This end of Waikiki was less congested than other parts and seemed more green than concrete. Really a nice part of Waikiki.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Comfotable stay. Good service and location. We just returned from a week long trip in February. The hotel is on the far end of strip but is right across the street from the beach. If you want a hotel right on the beach then try the Sheraton Moana Surfrider or the Outrigger Reef Hotel. The Marriott was clean and the bed was the best i have ever had at a hotel. We got a cabana by the pool for $15 a day which was worth it if you do not want a scorching sunburn. They also bring you complimentary bottled water and some snacks. The K tower is closer to the beach and has the better pool and the better view. We called ahead from the airport to get a room upgrade and they were nice enough to give us the free upgrade. I think we got our room for 130 a night on priceline. Nearby restaraunts were a better value than the hotel, especially for breakfast. Lulu's and Cheseburger in Paradise are a block away and breakfast for 2 was around $25 versus $45 at the hotel buffet. The sushi restraunt on the 3rd floor was pretty good. Sushi dinner for 2 was bout $70. Overall be prepared for pricey meals especially if you like to dine. We bought the Hawaii Enertainment book a month in advance and it saved us about 100 buck over the week. Whatever you do, do not go to the Don Ho show. He is old and came out very intoxicated. We had to walk out. It was sad really, and not worth 35 a person. You don't need a car per se on the strip as there is no place to park and the hotel charges 14 a day for parking. We rented a car for the week but did not even use it for two whole days. There is a Hertz rental in the hotel. You are probably better off just getting a car for the days you want to get away. There are free public tennis courts a few blocks away but they fill up quick. There is a 45 min limit if people are waiting. Diamond Head is close to the Hotel but you better drive there. Start hikking very early, like 7AM, as there is no shade after 8 o'clock. It is about 45 minutes up the hill if you are in good shape. I saw a couple people look like they were going to have coronaries and probably should sit at home. All in all, I reccommend the hotel highly. The staff was friendly and accomadating and the beds were to die for. I have certainly seen nicer pools and more modern facilities and spas, but have no real complaints about our trip. If I went again I would stay there or more likely at the Moana Surfrider for a little extra money.  
<Date>Feb 28, 2005

<Content>The Marriott is Convenient and Comfortable. Have stayed at the Waikiki Marriott 2 separate times in the last 2 weeksfor business, Feb. 2005. <Author>DCpost
<Content>Clean and Comfortable We spent the first 3 nights of our January 2005 vacation here. This hotel is located across the street from the beach, on the quieter section of Waikiki near the park. It's not at flagship level but still meets one's expectations from Marriott. We were in the newer and taller P tower which is more inland of the two towers and sits on top of the attractive tropical main lobby and reservation desk. The six P Tower elevators were fairly quick. Other reviewers have complained about the poor views from the P tower, but our ocean view room (26th floor out of 33) truly had a panoramic view of the ocean down to the Ewa (west) end of the island. We also had a nice nighttime view of the Waikiki skyline. We were above all of the other buildings in the immediate area, but I could imagine that if you were below perhaps the 18th or 20th floor that your view would be obstructed. The oval balcony had room to move even with two chairs and a small table. The room was standard issue Marriott and was neat and clean, which is more than what I've heard about other hotels. The bathroom was nicely finished with an outside marble vanity area and a clean tiled inner room with a 5 ft bathtub - and I've heard that a lot of other hotels in Waikiki don't have tubs. The king-sized bed was soft and very comfortable with plenty of pillows. Strangely, there was not a lot of drawer space for keeping clothing, but there was a large closet. We didn't have any unusual service needs except for cashing travelers checks, but the staff was friendly. The free breakfast started at 5 am, which was great for jet-laggers like us. The food was fine but not compelling enough to eat at the hotel restaurant outside of breakfast. As with many Waikiki hotels, the ground floor is an open-air shopping mall for buying gifts and beachwear. There is a Seattle's Best coffee shop on the ground floor and a Starbucks one block over, just before the park. We appreciated the fact that the area was active but not a maddening crush of people like the area around the Moana and the Outrigger. Please note that on Friday/Saturday night everyone seems to converge on Waikiki at once. You should make restaurant reservations well in advance and still be prepared to wait. While the Waikiki Marriott is not high luxury, we were both happy with the experience and would book there again.  
<Date>Jan 24, 2005
