<Content>Best Kept Secret at Waikiki is the Marriott Love it ! Obtained our reservation on Marriott's web site, had the best rate and I did not have to worry about some stories read about those who book on Orbitz and alike. Beautiful Rooms, received a free upgrade from city view to partial ocean view without asking at check in. View was great.. ok I had to look over the AC on the roof of the restaurant but no big deal saw the ocean in all its glory and saw down the beach to the Royal Hawaiian. We were in the K bldg which is the best location. The distance to beach and shops and restaurants were close. Rented beach chairs for $10.00 next to the K Boys near Honolulu PD across from Hyatt. It became our spot. Not crowded, Loved watching the surfing lessons. ABC in hotel is oh so convenient.. bought bottle water by the 6 pak every day.. besure to save your receipts for the free mug. The beds at Marriott are heaven... feather beds with feather pillows and comforters.. slept with the balcony door open, perfect! We were on the 5th floor. The lanai's are huge compared to other hotels in the area. The staff at Marriott very friendly and helpful. The concierge's are knowledgeable. Hotel and rooms are clean. Fridge in the room. The pool is lovely in K bldg. and quiet with drink and food service.. We saved money by having papaya from ABC already cut up and ready to go for breakfast.. Seattle Best Coffee is in the bldg and their is kona coffee (free) in the room, want a second pot ? just leave a note for the maid and she will leave what ever you need. Sometimes I would get an scrambled egg at McDonalds, on the way to the beach and have my coffee, papaya and egg on my lounge chair at the ocean.. the life... take bottled water with you. Lunch time, hungry ? across the street behind the Hyatt is Burger King in Kings Village... great salad with several fresh veggies and grilled chicken to go for $4.99 and back to the beach with that ! in the mood for a sandwhich, why not split a huge egg salad sandwhich and a bag of Maui Chips ? under $5.00. Splirge on Dinner: Go to Keo's, Longhi's, Aaron's on top of the Alamoana, Duke's on the beach and the Tiki Bar. Have a maitai at sunset at Halekulani ( short walk beach side or take a cab for $8.00 ) and if you are at the Alamoana Mall Shopping in the evening, go to the food court and to Lahaina Chicken and Co. and have the Rib eye Roast or Chicken Dinner and pick your sides....best meal and only like 7 or 8 dollars! Buy your souveniers at the SWAP MEET at 1/3 the price same stuff they sell on the strip.Must: do the luau at Paradise Cove.Can't wait to go back next year....Aloha

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>worth every dollar... first of all if you can afford it - ask for the K tower - which is the shorter of the two towers, but closer to the beach. and please do get a deluxe ocean view room - it is well worth the bloody money. we had a room on the 21st floor and the view of the ocean was breathtaking. dont ask for the side facing diamond head. instead opt for the sunset view - facing west. reasonable pools and service. we spent most of the time outside the hotel. but the view from the room does look impressive while relaxing in the evening with a cold beer in hand. everything you can possibly need is available at many abc stores throughout the beach strip - and there are two abc stores in the hotel itself.my wife and i were in hawaii in late october 2004 for our anniversary. here is what i'd advise you to do. trek to diamond head on the first day. on the second day - rent a ford mustang with retractable roof at hertz (in the hotel) and drive around the island - eat lunch at Jameson's by the sea. ask the concierge for a detailed map of the island and where to drive and what to do. check out all the beaches around the island - they are great for snorkeling and just having a good time away from the crowd at waikiki. third day - visit pearl harbor - just take the local bus early in the morning and return for free (with the same tickets) by 2pm. fourth day - check out shopping at the ala moana center and the beach nightlife. fifth day - do some serious snorkeling, surfing, or parasailing - ask the concierge for the best deals as soon as you check in - you might have to book these in advance. also ask the concierge for your style of dining - the choices are amazing - and the food and drink are superb all around the island. enjoy! mahalo.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Enjoyed the Marriott In November, my husband and I and five other couples spent 4 nights at the Waikiki Beach Marriott in November, and we really had a great time at the hotel. Upon arrival we and three others received a room upgrade at no charge and no asking, some of us even received double upgrades. The room was great and the view for us was ok. Yes we could see Diamond Head from one lanai, and the ocean from the other lanai, but it was not a direct ocean view, which I would have preferred better. The beds were super!!!!! Practically everyone that traveled with us, went back home to redo their bedrooms, trying to duplicate the Marriott Beds. The bathroom in our room (Deluxe Corner Ocean View) was really large we had a 2nd closet, and the tub and toilet were in a closed room seperate from the vanity/dressing area. The buffett in the hotel provided a very nice variety, and it probably was about the best place we ate the whole trip. We found bad experiences with the food in Waikiki. Especially at the Top of Waikiki Restaurant. The food was cold, and the service horrible, half our table received their food while the rest of us waited about 30 minutes for our chilled food to arrive, and the view although nice, was no different from the view we had in our room. Overall the hotel was nice and the pictures on the websiet were exactly like the property. I actually read all of the posted reviews and the ones that gave positive reviews were pretty accurate.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lovely hotel...teensy bit out of the way My husband and I stayed at this hotel for 6 nights this December. It was a lovely hotel, the lobby and facilities were all pleasant and inviting. The room was exactly as it was pictured on the web site. There were no surprises. We received excellent service, all the staff were helpful and friendly. Upon check-in, we were upgraded from a city-view room to an ocean-view room for free, without our asking. The first room we got was in the P tower and faced another hotel building, with a partial ocean view. It was close enough that we could see two guys playing cards in their speedos on their lanai. We requested a room change and they gave us another ocean-view room on the other side of the P tower that had a gorgeous view of the ocean with less buildings in the foreground. The gym was small, and the weight machines limited. The pools were lovely but not ones you could do any laps in by any means. If you stay there, request to be in the K tower because it's closer to the ocean and your view isn't as obstructed by nearby buildings. The beds were as comfy as described. The breakfast buffet was included in our package and was well worth it. There was tons of variety, waffles, eggs, fruit, salmon, an omelette bar and even Japanese options. My only complaint about this hotel is that I did find it a slight bit far from the main center of things, that is where the Moana and the Royal Hawaiian were. It's nice to have a quieter beach but it's about a 10 minute walk at least if you want more food options. The elevators are as slow as mentioned, but it's a small thing to put up with for the price and value of this hotel. I also noticed many guests pulling their luggage up to their rooms themselves. It seems like bell service is lacking here.

<Author>Danuary
<Content>Average I was actually considering not writing a review because I don't really know what to say. The Marriott was just average -- nothing more, nothing less. The room was a little cramped. For a full oceanview, the ocean could really only be seen from the balcony. The staff we came into contact with was all very friendly and helpful. The Kuhio Grill isn't that great but they serve an OK if expensive breakfast. Sansei which everyone seems to love we thought was horrible. They (along with other restaurants in Hawaii) seem to have a fascination with putting mayonaise in California rolls and aioli on everything they can think of. It gets a little gross after a while. Not sure if this is a regional thing but I have certainly never encountered mayo in sushi before! The fast-food sushi place downstairs is fine for a quick bite, and it's cheap. This end of Waikiki is a little more laid back; the beach directly in front of the Marriott is lovely and quiet. So in short... Eh. Just average. Nothing special. I was staying on Marriott Rewards points, and I'm glad I didn't pay to stay here. Given the cost, I plan to go elsewhere when I return to Waikiki.

<Author>Aussies1
<Content>Nice hotel with very comfortable beds Our family of five had a one week vacation at this hotel in September. The hotel was relatively quiet, only one-third occupied. We didn't ask for an upgrade, being Australian, but after reading other reviews, perhaps we should have. I did request to be in the building closer to the beach which we found very convenient given we had a fair bit to lug to the beach each day. One of the reasons we chose the Marriott was for the pools but found we really didn't use them as the beach was so much better. Who wants to use a pool on a building anyway? The beds really were as comfortable as everyone is saying. My only complaint was the size of the bathrooms. We have stayed in a lot of hotels over the years but these bathrooms (we had two adjoining rooms) were miniscule. The POV was quite good but probably better on the Waikiki side and the breakfast package saved us heaps. The kids loved the waffles. The Marriott was certainly at the quieter end of Waikiki and we found the beach outside the Sheraton Moana to be our favourite spot which was probably a 10 minute walk from the Marriott. We spent the days swimming and touring around the Island and loved browsing the shops in the evenings. Great holiday, one week was plenty as we then had a fabulous week in Maui and I would recommend the Marriott although I would probably stay elsewhere if there is ever a next time as we love to try new places.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Great location, superb value My wife and I have just returned from a one week stay at the Waikiki Beach Marriott Hotel and Spa, and we have nothing but praise for this property. The location cannot be beat--directly across the street from the beach, on the quiet end of Waikiki, with unobstructed ocean front views of the Pacific (Kealohilani Tower). We opted for the Paradise Package, a great value, which includes room and daily breakfast buffet--ONO! Upon checkin, we were upgraded from a standard ocean view room to a corner deluxe ocean view, with not one, but two lanai! Our friends stayed in the Paoakalani Tower, with an equally appealing view, facing the Kapiolani Park and Diamond Head, with a beautiful slice of the ocean. This is a large resort, but it isn't overwhelming in stature, no does it seem overly crowded. Staff members here express a genuine concern and sincerity about making you feel comfortable and welcome. Everything you need to make your stay enjoyable and memorable is located on site, but should you wish to venture out, you're a short stroll from the Waikiki's vibrant stream of activity along Kalakaua Avenue. I wouldn't hesitate to recommend this hotel to anyone considering a visit to Honolulu. It offers a great Waikiki location, at an unbeatable price.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great hotel We stayed at the Marriott in August 2004. It was part of a package deal that included air, car rental and hotel. This was a great hotel to stay at. The service is what I expect from a typical Marriott hotel. We were upgraded to a partial ocean view room at no charge by the friendly staff at the front desk. They also honored our request for a non-smoking room. The room was extremely clean and the beds were extremely comfortable for hotel beds (one of the most comfortable I have stayed in). The hotel is just across the street from the beach, which is convenient. I also liked how it is located near the end of Waikiki, where there are less crowds. But if you want to go to the more crowded section of Waikiki you can easily walk there. Some of the things I didn't quite like: the bathroom was fairly small and they charge $14 per day for parking which is a little steep. But overall, this hotel was a great value for what we paid. I would stay there again in the future.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent Value My family (wife-44, son-22, and daughters - 19/17) and I just returned from a 5 night stay and we really loved the hotel. Rather than repeat other reviews that you can read, I'll just give you a few tips. First, ask for the front tower and don't be bashful about asking the great staff for a free upgrade if available. We were upgraded to the 21st floor with beatiful ocean and Diamond Head views, plus they put a cot in my kid's room for free. Second, make sure you plan to spend Thursday late afternoon/early evening at the pool. While they have excellent free entertainment every night poolside, don't miss Aunty Genoa, who is a living legend. She is in her 80's but can still hit all the notes and hold them with great power...amazing...my 17 year old was literally brought to tears by the beauty of the music. Third, while I can understand why you would not want to pay the $14 per day parking, my advice for families is to get a mini-van (National gave me one for $200 for the week) so you have the freedom to come and go as you please. The concierge desks are usually open and you can get directions and maps from them...seeing the natural beauty of the island is best done by taking a cruise and pulling over at the lookouts. Finally, here are some recommendations for food and shopping - Irifune is a local Japanese retaurant not far away which is excellent and affordable; Tiki across the street at the Aston is great for late night plates ($10 each) that are fresh and tasty and they have late night live music too; Cheeseburger in Paradise around the corner is great for lunch...for shopping, go to the swap meet at Aloha Stadium on W/SA/SU morning for your souvenir tee shirts and knick-knaks, and ask for directions to Diaei (10 minute drive), which is a superb market that carries everything from the best prices on 100% Kona coffee to fresh local fish to beautiful flowers (bird of paradise just $0.25 each). You'll have a great time at the Marriott...we did.  
<Date>Sep 10, 2004

<Content>Marriott nice, Wakkiki average, Volcano and Pearl Harbour Great! After reading everyones reviews before we went we can totally agree with the beds in this hotel they are amazing!!! We stay in Marriotts all the time and know them well - this marriott was clean, staff friendly cant fault that at all.We would say however if you were looking to go for a romantic break, honeymoon or family holiday - Wakkiiki is not the place to go. <Author>Steviek49
<Content>Waikiki Marriott- A Nice high rise across from the beach Just returned from a 16 night, 4 island vacation which began with a 4 night stay at The Waikiki Beach Marriott. This hotel was actually our 3rd choice on Oahu (Sheraton Moana and Sheraton Waikiki were 1st and 2nd) but because of possible reservation rate problems with those two hotels and being 6000 miles away from home I decided to stay with Marriott.We are a family of 4 with 2 daughters ages 14 and 12. We arrived at the Marriott after more than 12 hours of flights and check in went quite smoothly. Although they were totally sold out and unable to upgrade my partial Ocean View room - we were quite happy with the room we had. We were in the K tower (the closest to the beach). They put us in a 16th floor Partial OV which had a nicer view than the other 3 hotels we booked on Kauai, Big Island and Maui even though those hotels said their rooms were Ocean View. Out Lanai faced the Aston Waikik Beach hotel across the street but just tilt your chair to the right and you have a very big view of the Pacific Ocean via Kuhio Beach. The room was roomy, modern and comfortable. The hotel itself was a typical city high rise hotel but clean, updated and nice. The location was great because it was toward the end of Waikiki ( alittle quieter-yet just a few blocks from the heart) and although it was directly across the street from the beach, there were no hotels in front of you. The K tower pool on the 3rd floor was larger and nicer than the P tower pool. The price was a bonanza at $112 per night.The only negaitives I can give are the elevators (all 5 of them) are very crowded and slow. Yes the hotel was sold out- but still we had to let many go by because they were packed. The hotel restaurant's breakfast buffet was overpriced and I must admit that the Sheraton Moana down the street was beautiful, on the beach, and had alot of Hawaiin atmosphere which was somewhat lacking at the Marriott.Would I stay here again? Perhaps, but would like to try one on the beach like the Sheratons or the Outriggers.

<Author>Delphini
<Content>Good, not Great Hotel This is a good, not great hotel, but I feel it's marketing is a bit missleading. First, you should know this location is NOT on the beach, but across the street from it, and odds are your room is not going to have a view of Diamond Head. It's a property that Marriot purchased and refurbished a few years ago. I think the Hotel's original design in the 70's leaves a bit to be desired, so Marriott can only fix up so much. It's located at the northern most end of waikiki so it's a 5 to 10 minute walk to the heart of the beach. If you really want/need to be right on the water check out the Sheraton Moana Surfrider, the Outrigger next door (Dukes), The Royal Hawaiian (older crowd) next to that. Dukes seems to be the epicenter of Waikiki.The Marriott Waikiki's rooms are standard size (remember built ing the 70's), very comfortable, but nothing to write home about. But here's a great tip that Marriot can pay me for later. We missed our flight out and stayed an extra day at the JW Marriott Ihalini on the west side of the island. From the airport the drive time to it is about the same as to the Marriott Waikiki. The rooms are amazing!!!! A standard room here was only 30$ more than the standard room at the Marriott Waikiki. I'm 6'4 and the walk from the front door to the end of our lania or our Jr. Suite was 28 paces, they're HUGE. Walk in his and hers closets, 2 tv's, large living area, private lania with chase lounge table and chairs, seperate sinks, shower and tub, 4 large semi private lagoons, pool, marble everything. If your familiar with Las Vegas, these rooms are larger and nicer than the Mandalay, and paired with the view (2/3 face the ocean), truely spectacular. Oh and did I mention that down stairs the fish ponds have manta rays and hammer-head sharks? Hey, I don鈥檛 even golf, but if I did they'd probably never get me to leave. It's not down in the action of Waikiki, it's fairly quiet here, but we just loved it. And you can always head down to waikiki for a day and surf Canoes ant get cocktails at Dukes or the Moana if you want.

<Author>leolady
<Content>Great times... wonderful hotel stay! I stayed at the Waikiki Beach Marriott from May 26-29th - Labor Day Weekend - with my best friend who was scheduled to move to NYC, Monday June 14th. This was our last hoorah before she begins surgery residency for 6 years! This hotel is absolutely great for the price. They've recently remodeled - so the hotel itself is in great condition! The beds are probably the best I've ever slept on (including my bed at home!). The front desk was originally going to give us a room on the 11th floor, but my friend requested for an upgrade - and the lady at the front desk upgraded us for FREE to the 33rd (TOP) floor!!! It never hurts to ask - ever! The room was located at the P tower - not K - although I've heard that the K tower is wonderful. But oh my - the views of Diamond Head and Waikiki beach were absolutely breathtaking. We were so stoked to get this! Everything about the hotel was great - the maid service, room service (although it's quite expensive), front desk, Spa Olakino (in K Tower)... although we opted to venture out and eat outside the hotel (suggestion: Cheeseburger's In Paradise is close by - you can grab some yummy burgers and fries to go, and watch the sunset on the beach - which is right across the street!). We also rented a standard car (at Budget rent-a-car at the hotel) one of the days to drive down to the south shore - and on the weekend - we rented a Jeep Wrangler Sport ($130) for one-day rental plus insurance  gas refill - to check out North Shore - and basically drive around the entire island!!! Let me tell you... it was TOTALLY WORTH IT to get a jeep - it was a very fun ride. We explored as much as we could - and took tons of pictures. But going back to the hotel again - I recommend this hotel for active travelers that like to be comfortable and close to everything. You can't beat the cost for what you get!!!

<Author>MOjourneyer
<Content>Great hotel! Great features and a great location at a decent price for Waikiki! We stayed in the Paoakalani Tower which is the newer of the two towers and had a nice view of Diamond Head and the ocean.The Marriott complex occupies an entire block at the east end of the Waikiki strip with the beach right across the street. It is also within walking distance of most all of the shopping, dining and night life Waikiki has to offer. We really enjoyed the various street performers that come out at twilight to earn your tips.Parking is expensive, but unless you鈥檙e part of a tour group you鈥檒l want to rent a car (Hertz has an office  cars at the Marriott) to get out and explore the island beyond Honolulu. The traffic was congested as reputed, but nowhere near as bad as driving on the LA or NY freeways. There鈥檚 easy access via Kapahulu Street to Interstate H1 to drive over to Pearl Harbor and the North Shore, plus there are also some scenic drives we made on Highways 61  63 through the mountains northeast of Honolulu. The hotel lobby has a beautiful open-air atrium complete with waterfalls and there is a convenience store and a coffee shop adjoining it. There are also other stores in a mini-mall plus three good restaurants in the complex.The staff was friendly, helpful, and tri-lingual since several major Japanese travel agencies book tours groups at this hotel. Service was excellent and we loved the tropical d茅cor in our room.We will definitely stay there again!

<Author>JaneDoe29
<Content>Best beds! We stayed at the Waikiki Marriott in May, 2004. The room was very attractive, comfortable and nicely furnished. The bed was probably the most comfortable hotel bed I've ever had. It even had five down pillows on the bed (king) and a down comforter. Our view, however, was lacking. We were in a partial ocean view which was on a fairly low floor (11) on the noisier side (Diamond Head side) of the hotel. Lots of city (buses, cars and A/C) noise and the view was as urban as it gets (of the neighboring buildings). You could view the ocean from the lanai. It may be worth it to pay for the ocean view or at least try to get a room on the Ewa side of the building (a much quieter street). The gym was very well equipped and uncrowded. The treadmill machines even had individual personal TV's. Although we didn't eat at the hotel, we did have a beer at the pool bar/restaurant and at $3 for a nice premuim draft beer, in an oceanview setting, it was a good deal for Waikiki. I was also happy to see that the inroom coffee was free...somewhat of a special thing in Waikiki, even among some of the higher end properties (Hilton). Overall, the Marriott is a very pleasant place to stay.  
<Date>May 11, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A nice place to stay. We stayed in this hotel for 5 nights in Apr 2004. We had stayed at the Radisson Prince kuhio hotel behind the Marriott for 2 nights. This is clearly a much better hotel than the Radisson. Of course, the Marriott is more expensive and you get what you pay for. The (newly renovated?) lobby is outstanding with beautiful plants and a waterfall etc which by itself is a nice place to sit, read a newspaper and relax. There are two towers comprising this hotel and we were given a partial ocean view room on the front tower (K tower, I think) closer to the beach. It was a very nice large room with a big balcony with a pretty good view of the ocean from the side. The place where the hotel is located is slightly quieter than other places on the Waikiki strip. The only problems we had I can say were minor. During weekend nights we had trouble finding parking in the hotel lot as not only hotel guests are allowed to use it. Also, the maid service was a bit slow and sometimes the beds weren't done and place not cleaned even after 2:30 pm or so when we got back from our visits.We certainly did not have the horroble experiences that some people have described. It was pleasant throughout and management was friendly and addressed our minor problems promptly.One thing to note however. Hotels in the waikiki area are expensive and sometimes still don't offer much. IMHO it is best to lower one's expectations before the trip :). Food/gas is also more expensive than on the mainland.

<Author>Carole-Renee'
<Content>It's so big! We stayed at the Waikiki Beach Marriott in Feb. of this year. We came down from spending a week up at the North Shore. It was kind of like culture shock, as there were so many people in the area. I guess the pro bowl was part of the reason. The Marriott was very nice. Our room was clean, attractive, and had an unsurpassed view of Diamond Head and the park. We were on the 32nd floor. Never stayed that high before. I was not comfortable sitting on the lanai (much less looking over it) but this wouldn't affect everyone this way. Didn't bother my husband. This was a very large resort. I was not comfortable being in such a large place with so many people. I think it has over 1,000 rooms. This is, of course, my opinion, but for anyone who likes a more intimate setting you might want to look elsewhere. The eating areas were usually very crowded and I found them not to be very relaxing. Next door is the Aston, which seemed like a more laid back place. Their eating places seemed less expensive. We liked to duck into Gaylord Puck's for some tasty food to take up to our room (you can also eat there) and we ate for a very reasonable price at Peary's Smorgy. The Marriott is across the street from a pretty swimming area with a sandy bottom. It's not a long walk to the acquarium or the park or the zoo. It was just so big that it seemed to take us forever to just get out of there to go those places!

<Content>I Don't get the NEG Reviews My wife and I stayed here from 14-21 March 04 and I don't get the NEG reviews. I travel all over the world and have visited Oahu several times. I've stayed in 9 different hotels (JW Ihilani, Hilton Hawaiian Village, etc.) I would have to rate this as the 3rd best in Oahu. I was getting skiddish reading the NEG reviews - Here's what I experianced: It was pouring rain when we arrived. We pulled under the canopy and were greated by valets who showed us to the lobby past several (watch your step, slippery when wet) signs. Self parking was $12 a night, $10 plus tip for valet parking. As we ventured past the pleasing sceanary and soulful sound of Brudaah IZ we appoached the counter and began our pleasant vacation. There were 3 employees at the counter for check in - we were in our room in less than 10 min. The room was very spacious, clean and brightly decorated. The bed was the most comfortable we have ever slept in. We stayed at the second (P.... ) Tower. We had a great view of Diamond Head and the Ocean from the balcony we often lounged on. The room was a 3-5 min walk to the beach depending on the elevator. Let me summarize from here. SPA(B+), GYM(A-), 2 POOLS(A+), BAR(A), LAUNDRY(A), HOSPITALITY/SERVICE(A+), COMFORT(A). If you don't mind staying at the far end of town, I'd recomend staying here.

<Content>Great Experience ! Aloha, we visited Oahu and stayed at the Waikiki Beach Marriott from March 13th - 20th, 2004. It has a wonderful location right across from the beach. We found the place a beautiful experience. We had the ocean front tower, with a deluxe corner room where we had a view of the ocean from anywhere in the room. The room was very spacious and beautiful decor. The room service was good, the stores were nice, with an ABC store in either tower, and a Seattle's Best coffee shop in either tower also. We ate at the Kuhio cafe for breakfast and it was always wonderful. Ate at their new Italian restaraunt (not owned by the hotel chain), and it was terrible, but do go next door to the Tiki bar and grill, nice Hawaiian fare there. The pools were very clean and well kept, the employees were always helpful and kind. The beach in front of the hotel was quiet and peacful, great for just laying on the beach for a while. Not crowded and loud like behind the Duke statue or further down in front of the Hilton Hawaiian Village. I'd have to say it was the most pleasurable vacation I have ever had. Mahalo Hawaii ! Hope to see you again soon!

<Author>Tennis_JD
<Content>It wasn't so bad.... Stayed here primarily for business, and then through the weekend for pleasure. Marriott (and Hilton properties for that matter) have an edge over other hotels because business travelers, like me, are trying to collect points for free future stays. So this was an obvious choice to stay since the Hilton property on Waikiki was pricier.My room was not all that bad. It wasn't the best, but it was comfortable. What I didn't like about the room was the entrance to the bathroom did not have a door. The toilet and the shower had a door, but the sink did not. Therefore, when my girlfriend or I went to the bathroom, turning on the light shined a bright light onto the bed in the room.I upgraded to what I thought was an oceanview room. Come to find out that it was a PARTIAL oceanview room - and the FULL oceanview room is $30 more per night. So, I DID have a view of the ocean, but it was partial. Make sure you check technicality when checking into this hotel.Also, there are 2 towers on this property. Both towers are rectangular in shape. Both towers are perpendicular to the ocean - meaning the short side of the tower directly faces the ocean, and the long side of each tower provides the partial view. The second tower is located behind the first tower, thus creating one long hotel (the towers do not sit side by side but instead in-line). The reason why I pointed this out is because my room was in the 2nd tower, and the last room furthest from the ocean. Although it was on the 27th floor (#2772 to be exact), it was well away from the ocean. Even though you select an oceanview room, you may not get an ideal room that you are expecting.Despite explaining the above, the room was adequate. And the view of Diamondhead crater was definately enjoyable. No noise from the other rooms were heard at all, however at 27 floors up you can still hear the traffic below (no big deal). There is a small fridge in the room, and enough space for 2 people and full luggage. Room service was good and prompt. Maid service was polite and thorough. The elevators didn't make me wait a long time (pet-peeve of mine about nice hotels), and the lobby was spacious and adequate with enough shops, etc for what you need. The front desk was adequate which didn't seem to coordinate with other reviews on this site - maybe they cleaned up their act. I didn't eat in the hotel restaurants because there are too many good restaurants within walking distance (1 block). Try Cheeseburger in Paradise for breakfast AND lunch, try HY's steakhouse for a classy dinner, and try TIKI's for a nice atmosphere dinner/drinks.The Marriott is located in front of one of the busy parts of Waikiki Beach. There's always alot of people tanning on the sand, so you may have to walk further down to get a spot. Driving to/from this hotel is kinda difficult, but that's Waikiki - the traffic in Honolulu is ridiculous for the amount of people they have - not to mention the construction of Kahio Ave which runs perpenticular to the rear of the 2nd tower.Overall, I feel this hotel is decent. I can stay there again, but I feel there may be others that have a better room (including location) for the amount I paid.If you get a chance, go see the KO OLINA Marriott Hotel. It is NOT in Waikiki and is about 30 minutes west, but if you want to stay at a resort with the whole 9 yards (golf, private beach, luau, hammerhead sharks) this is the spot!Feel free to email me with questions.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful Hawaiian Marriott Experience Aloha,We visited Oahu and stayed at the Waikiki Beach Marriott from Feb 25th through Feb 28th (2004). I just can't understand the negative reviews written here. It has a wonderful location right across from the beach iand is newly renovated. It should not be compared unrealistically to other higher priced luxury resorts.The extended family was in Waikiki in May of 2001. At that time, the end of the beach where the Marriott is now located was absolutely dead. You had to walk a block or so up the strip before anyone was around. Stores were closed, restaurants were run down, and people were just running past to get to the zoo or towards Diamondhead.Now, it is different. The area is revitalized, in much part do to the new renovations and upgrades to the Marriott (and the area). The shops in the Marriott were dead and nobody was around. Now there are people shopping, nice restaurants, two coffee shops in the hotel, lounges, and beautiful Hawaiian ambiance.Without asking for it, we were upgraded to the front tower facing the ewa (towards Honolulu) . We had a spectacular view of the beach, and overlooked the new pool and terrance. The decor was all brand new and had a wonderfall Hawaiian motif including bright new carpets and newly painted hallways. It rained much of the time we were there but the hotel provided a nice array of activities. There were native craft displays to purchase and also craft activities. My mother was able to make an authentic professional quality orchid lei for free. There was also a talented hula dancer in the courtyard performing daily. Even in the rain the pool bar was fun to sit at and have a drink, as was the Seattles Best coffee shop inside the back tower of the hotel. The only negative was that the nightly native music performances that used to take place at the old lobby level bar are now gone. They have been moved to only once a week on the terrace. Even so, the new waterfall fountain and rock formation is beautiful and a wonderful place to grab a tropical drink (if it wasn't raining).We found the place a beautiful experience. All things being equal we would return to the Marriott in a heartbeat.  
<Date>Mar 14, 2004

<Content>Average Hotel, Not a great location My hushand  I have travelled to Hawaii (Maui, Big Island, Kauai) several times but it was our first time to Oahu. From reading a previous review, I was concerned about the rooms being mostly smoking rooms. My room was smoke free which was nice. I am not sure if I would stay here again since there are so many other hotels in Waikiki.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fails at even basic service principles I was not impressed with this hotel at all. Being in the hotel business myself, I understand that when you're running an operation as large as the Waikiki Marriott, there are going to be problems. Unlike most leisure travelers, I am not high-maintenance. The Waikiki Marriott failed even to meet with my low standards.First of all, I was staying with my sister who had arrived a few days earlier. I had asked her to put my name on the reservation, so I could just get a key and be done with it when I arrived. But when I got there, the non-English speaking and rude front desk clerk would not give me a key. She said that my name wasn't on the room. As my sister and I went downstairs to get it sorted out, we spoke with a desk clerk who had 1/2 of a brain, and she confirmed that my name had been on there all along and that (after showing ID) I should have been given a key.My sister's room service breakfast was garnished with open/used jelly containers. There's not a better way to eliminate an appetite than realizing that someone else had already eaten your meal.The furniture was mismatched, the carpet and the sheets smelled funky, and the bathroom was nothing to rave about either. We did have an ocean view (sort-of) which was nice, but we were also kept up all night by our neighbors--seemingly all Japanese juvenile delinquents--because the security was really lax. The fitness center was a joke. Enough said.The rental car office in the hotel is a joke, too. Parking was ample but expensive for Hawaii. C'mon. This isn't New York, here...The pool was ok. The restaurant was edible, but nothing special. Checking out, we discovered they'd double charged us for parking. Explaining this to the desk should have been easy, but it wasn't. The views of Diamond Head and the beach were the only redeeming quality of this place. Other than that, it is an overgrown Motel 6. I can't even imagine what this would be like for someone who needs pampering from their hotel.

<Author>sullyboy
<Content>A Great Choice in Waikiki As a very frequent visitor to Honolulu, I've tried out just about every hotel in the Waikiki area (Kalakau BLVD). Here's my review of the hotels I've stayed with and know, beginning with the Marriott Waikiki:1) Marriott Waikiki: A very good value, at a great location just a 3 minute walk to Waikiki beach. There are two towers that make up the hotel; you should ask for the one nearest the ocean for the best view. I had room 1810 (corner room) in the tower farthest from the ocean, yet I still had a great view from the balcony and picture window. The rack rate was something over $400, but they were running a special for $225/ night. I got the room for $120 on Priceline, and asked to be upgraded upon check-in. I was very nice to the girl, and she upgraded me for free although she didn't have to. Priceline customers generally get run-of-house rooms with no view. The hotel is basically brand new... the rooms are fantastic, even complete with black marble countertops. Bed are very comfy and large (mine was a king bed). Air conditioner was very effective, which is a must in Hawai'i. You must have your balcony door shut for air to come one though. I guess Marriott doesn't want to pay for you to cool off the whole city... :) All in all, a great hotel, great staff, and a 1st class, 4-star facility. I would return as long as I get a rate under $150. I was pleasantly surprised by the quality of this Marriott in contrast to some of the negative reviews on this website.2) Sheraton Waikiki: A GREAT location directly on the beach, but lousy dated rooms. Our room faced Diamond Head, and while laying on the bed, you could look outside and imagine yourself on a cruiseship....all you saw was blue....no buildings in the way or anything. However great the view was, the room was not worth $200/night. I'd take that $200/night to the Hyatt and get the same great view, with a better room. The pool area is nice, albeit crowded, with nice Hula shows at night. Lobby is grand central station, as it is a main thoroughfare to the beach for guests and non-guests alike. This is a very large hotel. almost Las Vegas casino sized. If you want nothing but a great view and large crowds, this may be your hotel. If you don't want large crowds, first off you probably don't want to come to Honolulu. Secondly, your best bet is the Kahala Mandarin Oriental on the back side of Diamon Head, in the exclusive Kahala neighborhood.3) Hyatt Regency Waikiki:A great ocean view from either tower, provided you opt for ocean view and not city/mountain view. Again, you can lay in bed and see nothing but the blue ocean out your window. Large open air lobby, pretty crowded. Rooms are average to large. Great sushi restaurant in the hotel. Easy to get lost in the lobby, until you get it in your head. All in all a great choice. This hotel embodies the Hyatt name. Truly a cut above the Sheraton Waikiki in terms of quality, yet on par with the new Marriott Waikiki in terms of room-quality. The Hyatt is directly accross the street from the beach though, and has no buildings between it and the sand. The Marriott is accross the street and down the road about 200 feet, so you have 1 or 2 buildings between the hotel and the sand.4) Halekulani: A top-notch 5 star hotel on Waikiki. In fact, the only 5-star on Waikiki beach, contrary to anything else you may hear. Absolutely gorgeous hotel, very exclusive and A++ location on the beach. Everything about the hotel is great, except the prices. Don't expect to find this hotel discounted on Priceline or any other website. Unless you are privy to special industry rates, you're going to pay through the nose for this hotel ($400 for a non-ocean view room). I think this hotel is way overpriced, even though it is very lovely. If you want luxury, stay at the Mandarin-Oriental, which trumps the Halekulani in my opinion. The M-O will can also be had for closer to $200, just depending on when you book and when you plan to travel. Check mandarin-oriental.com for best rates.5) Sheraton Moana Surfrider: Hands down the most romantic hotel in Honolulu. The first lady of Waikiki as she is called was built in the early 1900s and is just picture perfect. Check out their website for pictures and info. The only downside is that the rooms do not have balconies in the original hotel. Newer towers have been built next to the original hotel, and they have every modern convenience, including balconies. All rooms have air conditioning. This is my favorite place to relax in Waikiki. I especially love the Banyan courtyard. Stay at this hotel if you love nostaligic things...from wrap around porches with rocking chairs to large white columns. This is grand old Hawaii at its finest. Even if you don't stay here, you've got to experience breakfast on the Veranda.6) Outrigger Waikiki: Although this hotel is right on the beach, the rooms are old and musty, and for $200+ per night, I'd rather go to the Hyatt or Marriott or Moana Surfrider! I'd avoid all things Outrigger and Aston (2 hotel giants in HI). You pay too much and get too little at those chains. Outrigger and Aston have many dumpy hotels to fit most budgets. I'd go so far as to recommend staying at home and saving up $ until you can st least stay at the Marriott. Staying in a nicer hotel can make all the difference in a vacation, trust me!!7) Royal Hawaiian (a Sheraton hotel):The other landmark Waikiki hotel, dating back to the early 1900s. This great pink hotel is centrally located on the sand. Again, if you are into nostalgic things, you'll love this hotel and overlook its flaws which come with age. Such flaws may include small rooms, no balconies, etc. The biggest problem you may have is getting your husbands to stay in a pink palace. Ah, but remember this is Hawaii...the place men can wear leis and not be thought to swing the other way. At the very least, you must walk through the lobby and grounds of this hotel to take it all in... it is afterall a piece of history. FYI: All the government officials from D.C. stayed at this hotel immediately following Pearl Harbor in 1941 while conducting the investigation.8) Sheraton Princess Kaiulani:A 3 star hotel accross the street from the beach. Nice enough, but really not your best bet for Waikiki. If considering this hotel, I think you'd be far happier at the Marriott for a similar price. Nice thing about the Sheraton hotels (Sheraton Waikiki, Moana Surfrider, Princess Kaiulani, Royal Hawaiian) is that you have access to all of them (pools, etc) and can sign charges to your room from the restaurants at all 4 hotels.9) W Hotel Honolulu:This hotel is off the beaten path in Honolulu, south of Waikiki Beach, and at the base of Diamond Head. If you want ecclectic and less crowds, you'd enjoy this hotel. A 15-20 minute walk will put you close to Waikiki beach and most downtown shopping, dining, etc. Everything here is a bit abstract, but that is essentially what the W brand represents.10) Kahala Mandarin Oriental:By far my favorite hotel. I stayed in room 711, which had a great (HUGE) balcony and perfect view of the ocean. Kahala is around the bend from Honolulu, but still only a 10-12 minute drive by car or hotel courtesy shuttle bus. Although all Hawaiian beaches are technically public, the hotel enjoys a very secluded 'private' beach. This is truly the 1st choice hotel in Hawaii for VIPs, celebrities, etc. If you have the cash, go for it and enjoy every second. Check their website for seasonal rates.Rooms are oversized, parque wood floors, large marbel baths, comfy beds, Wonderful breakfast buffet @ Plumeria Cafe. Some rooms are on the lagoon, which is home to 2 bottlenose dolphins. I think you can swim with them and a trainer (for a price). The grounds of the hotel are lush and perfectly relaxing. Being at this hotel is what Hawaii is all about to me: tranquil beauty, and proximity to the busy city for when I want/need that aspect.Bottom line: My top choice on O'ahu is the M-Oriental hotel, but if you must be in Waikiki, I'd say go with the Hyatt for modern comfort and a great view, or the Moana Surfrider for nostalgia/on-the-beach-location.Also be sure to try Dukes restaurant on Waikiki for their amazing breakfast buffet. Cheeseburger in Paraside is a must for lunch (try their Island Burger) and the Shorebird on Waikiki is a must for dinner (arrive early for the early bird special) and grill your own fish or steak while watching another perfect sunset in paradise. Your dinner comes with a great all-you-can-eat salad bar. Don't forget to try breakfast on the Veranda at the Moana Surfrider Hotel on Waikiki. Prices = $15-$25, but believe me, you don't want to miss this!!Enjoy your trip, and prepare to get hooked on Hawai'i! Aloha!

Everyone we encountered was friendly and accommodating. The pool area was crowded, to get a cabana you must go early in the morning. There were so many lounge chairs available that it was never a problem to find seating though. The hotel is in the perfect area. At night all of the beach area here is lit by tiki torches, as is the pier and streets. If you stay at the Marriott, be sure to go next door to the Pacific Beach hotel for lunch at the Oceanarium restaurant it was our favorite place to eat! Quite reasonable and what a treat! A 3 story high aquarium with every tropical fish you can imagine swimming by as you eat, even sharks and stingrays! As for Waikiki beach, if you have young children the beach here is the best! The way the breakers are set up our baby (16 months) could just wade in the water, sitting and splashing under our watchful eye. We will stay in this hotel again, can't wait to come back! Aloha!  
<Date>Aug 25, 2003

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort... Good and Bad... I've just got back from a 10 day stay at the Marriott Waikiki Beach Resort. I read the reviews on this web site and they all sounded good so I booked a deluxe ocean view room (corner) by telephone. (Prices booking by phone were exactly the same as the prices on ALL web sites!) I paid 300 dollars a night but more later....The hotel is located on the East side of Waikiki in a great location. The beach there has a pier and a wall to stop big waves coming in. This makes the location perfect for little kids (ours are 8 and 6). Right next to this beach is an area without a wall allowing people to boogie board too if they want. What's better is that this side of Waikiki is much quieter than the area around the Sheraton, so it just more pleasant. Also, tour buses etc pass right by the hotel meaning that if you plan to do activities you're in the right place to start with. One problem I suppose, is that it's a bit far from most of the main shops (Hawaiian Shopping Mall etc) but they are only a 10 min walk away. Also, there is an ABC store in front of the hotel (like every other hotel in Waikiki!) and close by is a Denny's, Starbuck's etc..As for the hotel, the lobby is beautiful with a mini volcano and water fall. The site of the hotel is huge so you get a feeling of space. The hotel has 2 pools, both on the 3rd floor and they are perfect for a dip before bed and great for kids. The shalllow end is 3ft and the deep end is 8 ft, but they allow inflatables so the kids loved swimming there. The hotel has two restaurants, but we only used one of the first floor, the Kuhio Grill Bar. This was good for breakfast, with a typical buffet menu, with lots to choose from. At night, they served a variety of foods, all good and reasonably priced.So, where is the bad? Why only an average rating?? The answer is the room itself. Paying 300 dollars, I expected a perfect room. Unfortunatley, it was far from that. The room was a corner on the 23rd floor (Room 2332). This room is fairly large, clean and has an amazing SHAKE!! If you don't know what earthquakes feel like, this room is a good demonstration. The shake is due to a vent in the corner wall just by one of the two queen beds. The shake is bad enough to cause the corner light and bed head to vibrate enough to be heard, and is very unpleasant at night. I had quite a few nights with a poor sleep due to it. I heard from the hotel staff that all corner rooms in that block above the 18th floor had the same problem. So, my STRONG advice would be to avoid those rooms. Also, the view from the left side corner rooms (e.g. 2332) is not as good as the right side (e.g. 2333) so it you want to get a room get the right side. Aparently, the hotel has other corner rooms in a different building which don't have the shakes, but I didn't see these so can't comment.Other small problems, were poor service at the front desk on arrival and not great service in the restaurant on occasions. In particular, we booked the 'Romance Package', but the front desk attitude did not reflect this at all. The lady at the desk was blunt and overly formal. No smiles at all. Other people working there also showed a similar attitude.Fortunately, on the day of checkout I mentioned my problems with the room and got a reasonably discount. That made up for the problem a little but 9 days with the shakes is not that nice. Next time, I'd probably book a cheaper hotel with a nicer ocean front room. There are a few to choose from in the same area.Saying all this, if we didn't choose the expensive room we did, (e.g. chose a standard ocean room on the right of the building instead) I think the rating for the hotel would be much higher. The kids and the wife loved the holiday, and enjoyed the poor and breakfast buffet a lot.  
<Date>Aug 15, 2003

<Author>Mountain77
<Content>Loved the Marriott My new husband and I stayed here the three days we were on Oahu for our honeymoon. We had spent several days on Kauai where there are not any huge hotels and were afraid the room would feel too small. From the moment we entered the lobby, we were very impressed. Everything looked so clean and new and our room proved to be of the same quality. Our standard room was not huge, but definitely comfortable for the two of us. The decor was beautiful - sunny yellows and greens. The bathroom was spotless too. There is a mini fridge so we could have cereal, milk and fruit wach morning purchased from one of the many ABC stores. The 2 pools were clean and overlook the ocean. The prices at the hotel restaurants were reasonable and food was tasty. We will definitely stay here again!
